Unlock Thy Hidden Gate

by WitchHeartsRunFree

Summary

It's 1922, Prohibition is law of the land, and an underground speakeasy scene runs rampant across New York City to fill the need of the people. Rio Vidal arrives in the city to be with her long-term boyfriend, but what will she do when he turns to the bottle instead of her?

Finding solace in a new job, she quickly finds herself under the watchful eye of Agatha Harkness - renowned for her quick wit, killer fashion, and a tantalizing back-alley secret.

When Agatha calls in a favor from the Sokovian gang boss, Wanda, to protect Rio from her abusive partner, the consequences may be more than she bargained for.

Or: Prohibition-era slow burn romance featuring Protective Agatha, Baby Lesbian Rio, Unhinged Mob Boss Wanda, Sidekick Fanboy Billy, and a whole cast of characters navigating the trials of the Roaring '20s.

Marching ever forward

Rio knelt over the bucket and twisted the towel as she rang out the sickening mix of vomit and soapy water. The hardwood floor was stained with patches of damp from many similar morning cleanings. Every floorboard felt a sense of deja vu each night as it re-lived the same trauma from the same broken man.

Tony had never been cruel, he wasn’t always temperamental, nor sappy or miserable. But, four months out of work, and his pride was in the gutter.

When Rio arrived in New York City a year ago, he had the same spark in his eye that had first pulled her in back in their hometown of San Juan. He was working at a cigar factory downtown with his cousin, Miguel, pulling in $250 a month in hard-earned wages. They shared a 2 bedroom, 5th floor walkup with another couple from Puerto Rico, and they got by. It wasn’t glamorous or ritzy, but in comparison to their life back home, Rio felt like she was living in a postcard.

She still remembered the feeling of seeing the skyline from the boat on her arrival day. It was akin to the first breath of air after diving underwater. It was like seeing the concept of possibility as a physical reality. Every dream she had conjured was no match for the breathtaking beauty of New York.

She had held the letter from Tony in her pocket for the five day journey, alongside a dark pink flor de maga that her sister had picked for her as she boarded the ship. “So you’ll always remember la isla.” She had whispered in her ear at their final embrace on the dock.

It was a battle to fight off seasickness as the boat tossed and lurched with each wave. The words in his letter were a mantra she repeated to ground her mentally (and physically).

Mi preciosa,

These past few months without you have tested my every will. The city is everything we imagined and more but sometimes I feel so alone and lost. You cannot believe the sheer size of everything! I feel like a pitiful little bug at times, dwarfed by the magnitude of buildings and steel above me. I now know how the ant experiences the world and why they seem to scurry in terror.

I am so grateful for each letter you send - your words keep me steady and resolute. I cannot wait until we are together again as one heart. Please tell me that you are coming soon. I have enclosed the boat fare and hope this conveys my genuine commitment to you. My job is steady and will provide us a life that is not possible on the island. I know we are yet to become man and wife, but it is my sincerest promise to make that so in due time. You are the light of my life, mi futura, mi corazón, I love you with every piece of me.

See you soon,

Antonio

Now his letter lay forgotten in her bedside drawer - a reminder of empty promises. And the flower lay shriveled, limp, an apt reflection if there ever was one.

Rio stared down at the man sprawled out on the double bed they share. The stench of gin wafted from his every pore despite the early morning hour.

How did we get here? She thought to herself with a long sigh before hauling the cleaning bucket to the kitchen sink and disposing of the evidence. She gathered the glass bottles in the living room and washed them out quickly and efficiently.

Although the sale of alcohol had been illegal in the US for the past two years, it was not actually illegal to consume it. Still, she knew it was better safe than sorry and any evidence was unwise, especially as immigrants.

Tony had been trading cigars for liquor with the variety of neighbors who had home stills and cranked out bathtub gin or good old-fashioned moonshine. But at this point, the cigars were long gone, along with their money. Rio didn’t know how he was getting his fix anymore, and she didn’t know if she wanted to.

“Tony,” she called for him as she re-entered their tiny bedroom, “Papi, time to wake up.”

He failed to stir, failed to do much of anything. “Tony, ay, please! We need to talk.” She raised her voice and pulled on his arm that flopped over the bed.

Her man rolled over and looked at her with bleary eyes that seemed to see nothing at all. “Por favor, I’m tired…” He grumbled, exhausted.

Rio’s patience was gone. She went to the bathroom, grabbed a cup of water, stomped back in and unceremoniously dumped it on his head. “Tired from what Tony?! You haven’t worked in months, you barely leave this apartment! We have no more money. We have nothing!

“Rio, mi amor, I just” he started but was cut off immediately.

“Don’t start with me now. I’ve heard this before.” Rio felt her anger rising like a tidal wave, but it fell flat when she saw the tears start to flow from Tony’s eyes.

“I’ll be better. I will.” Tony rose to a kneel on the bed, the springs squeaking beneath his imposing figure. “Please, mi vida, I’ve been lost, but I can do this for us. I’ll go out today and take the first job I see. I don’t care what it is. I’ll wash dishes, I’ll clean toilets, whatever it takes.”

“And the drinking?” Rio lifted an eyebrow. She could convey so much with a look and could see the way he shrank beneath her stare. The embarrassment written across his face, so plain and bare.

“I’ll get off the juice.” He conceded, head down as if avoiding her stare could save him some dignity.

“One more thing,” she started, “I’m going to look for a job as well.”

“ No ” The sudden boldness caused her to step back. He stood quickly, towering over her in a flash.

“It wasn’t a question. We’re on the nut, Tony. We are flat broke. If it wasn’t for Miguel and Claudia, we would have starved weeks ago.” She clapped her hands together in emphasis as she stated the facts for him. Unafraid yet blind to the way his knuckles were clenching, his face contorting to a grimace, his eyes narrowing.

“Women don’t belong on a payroll. I’m not letting my gal go out there and do, who knows what?” Tony looked down on her with all the machismo he could muster on a hangover.

Rio looked up at him and saw how he was trying to rebuild his ego. “Fine. You have until tomorrow to scrounge up some dough. But, we need the money. If I can get it, then why does it matter where it came from?”

She was suddenly staring at a pigeon flying across the clouded blue sky. Her head a full 45 degrees turned to the right when just a moment ago she had been looking right at her partner. The pain didn’t even register until she realised her left eye had started to water and she saw Tony’s open hand fall back to his side.

The words that were sitting next in line on Rio’s tongue dissolved like cotton candy on her lips. She grasped her cheek and turned heel towards the kitchen and let her feet carry her out the door. The five flights of stairs passed in a blur as she floated down the street completely unaware of her surroundings. She had fled without a hat, coat, or proper rags but proprietary was the last thing on her mind.

Her feet took her down the street, past her regular shops and familiar faces. The buzz of the city settled her nerves and calmed her down. Where it once felt like a concrete jungle of noise and fear, she now felt energised and at home. Rio walked and walked, watching the other folks go about their business, feeling both like a stranger and a part of something bigger. The gnawing anxiety of returning home to Tony quieted.

It was just a mistake. She allowed herself to think. He has never raised a hand to you before. He’s not like those violent sorts. Not my Tony.

She found herself down in West Harlem, wandering among a street of bustling restaurants feeding the lunchtime crowd. A sign in the window of a corner drug store stood out among the otherwise grey landscape. It was beautifully painted, a brilliant deep purple and read “Help Wanted - Shop assistant, regular wages, inquire within.”

He said no. I really shouldn’t…I don’t even know the first thing about working. Rio stood kitty-corner to the shop and read the sign outside, “Westview Prescriptions - Drugs, Soda, Luncheonette”. The windows reflected stunning calligraphy, and the interior looked inviting with fully-stocked shelves lining every wall. Before she could talk herself out of it, Rio crossed the street and opened the door. The light silver bell jingled in announcement as she stepped into the warm space, unaware of just how cold she was without a coat.

A counter ran along the entire east wall, with a few wooden stools available. A soda fountain near the back, while the impressive cash register stood sentry near the front door directly in front of the rows of cigarettes. The pressed tin ceiling drew the eye up, while the perfectly organised boxes of goods filled each shelf and cabinet.

An old dame looked up at the bell and greeted Rio with a smile from behind the counter. “What can I get you, doll?”

“The sign in the window - The “help wanted” one? Do I talk to you? I’m Rio. I’m new to the city.” Rio suddenly felt shy in front of the older woman with brilliant curly grey hair and all-knowing eyes that seemed to sense hesitation.

“I’m Lilia. I’ve worked here since my father opened the place back in 1901. We recently expanded and need a bit of extra help during the week and on some weekends. There’s a new Big Cheese running the joint. Just looking for someone to help stock the shelves, work the register, help with service during meal times, you know? What experience do you have?”

Rio bit her lip and looked away. Of course, she’d made a fool of herself again. How could she be such a dumb dora? What am I meant to say? My boyfriend’s a drunkard, and I need the money or else we’ll be homeless in a week. I have never worked before, but I’m desperate. No, god, why did I think this would be a good idea?

Lilia took in the woman in front of her with appraising eyes. She noted the lack of normal accouterments to her outfit, the accent to her English, the angry red tone to her left cheek, the quiet battle being waged in her head. She’s taking a risk being here .

Before Rio could speak, Lilia asked, “Look, we’ve had that sign up for a while now and need someone who can start immediately. The boss prefers female staff anyway. If you’re able to make it here every weekday from 10am to 5pm, then the job’s yours. It’s not much, but we can offer you $20 a week to start.”

Blinking in confusion, Rio could only nod quickly, “I can start tomorrow. I won’t let you down, Lilia.”

“I expect that you won’t. Now, we don’t have a formal uniform, but I will provide you with a standard apron and ask that you show up clean and presentable each day. I don’t tolerate tardiness or foolhardy behaviour. Any personal problems are to be left at home, understood?” Lilia noted the look of gratitude on Rio’s face, in addition to anxiety and fear.

She hoped she wasn’t making a mistake, but Lilia had always been able to read people. Ever since childhood, she could get a sense of a person within minutes of meeting. Her father called her his little divinaturi, Sicilian for “diviner”. And what she saw in Rio reminded her of her mother. Tender, eager to please, new to the country, strong yet reserved, and under the spell of a man who wielded his power over her.

“See you tomorrow, doll.” She watched Rio exit in a whisper and prayed that she would see her the next day.

Tame your fears

When Rio arrived back home after her sudden departure that morning, she looked around for any sign of Tony. He wasn’t in bed (for once) and didn’t seem to be anywhere else in their tiny abode. She sighed down into the couch and laid her head back.

She had a job, a real one. She would be making money for the first time and could finally put food back on their table without relying on handouts and pity. Her shoulders relaxed for the first time in months and the weight that had sat upon her chest eased slightly. But then, she remembered the slap, the reaction Tony had at even the suggestion of her working, and the pressure returned to her body.

What was she going to tell him? How could she explain her daily absence and sudden appearance of money? She kneaded her hands and closed her eyes.

The front door opened and Claudia, Miguel’s wife, strolled in, “Chica, why the long face?” She asked, setting her bag and coat down gently.

Rio groaned into her hands. As she raised her head, Claudia caught the swollen red mark along her hairline and cheek, the red slowly turning yellow and light purple.

“What kind of pill did this to you, sweets?” She ran a tender hand along her face, tracing the angry marks with her finger. Claudia and her were not close friends by any means, but the two had found solace and familiarity in each other’s company while living together.

“He didn’t mean to. He’s never even raised his voice before.” Rio’s voice was quiet. “It’s the drink, it’s…changing him. I see why they outlawed it in the first place. What good can such a devilish drink bring? Tony isn’t like this, I swear.”

Claudia had seen the way Tony had spiraled downward quickly once the factory laid off half its workers. Miguel had survived the cuts due to sheer luck and thank god he had, but Tony wasn’t so lucky. She saw the glass bottles he stuffed in his pockets and carried up the stairs, clinking with each step. She watched him disappear drink by drink and end up on the bedroom floor most nights. She hadn’t thought him a violent fellow, but how long can a person suffer before they break?

“It never starts with pain.” Claudia looked into Rio’s heartbroken eyes. “It starts sweet and beautiful. A rush of ecstasy and bursting with love and adoration. If it started with pain, nobody would be married, Rio.”

“I just told him that I was willing to get a job to help with money. It wasn’t an attack or a jab. You know how much we need it right now. We’ve got nothing left, I don’t even know if we’ll have enough to cover rent this month.” Rio felt the energy leaving her as the reality of their situation settled in her bones.

“Men don’t like to feel worthless. They don’t want to feel like they can’t take care of their family.”

“But he isn’t taking care of us!” Rio retorted.

“You’re right, but that doesn’t make it hurt any less.” Claudia replied. “Tony is blinded by self-pity and shame. Violence is often the quickest reply that animals turn to when backed into a corner.”

Rio seethed with her own feelings of rage. It wasn’t fair. She wasn’t going to sit silently like her abuela, who suffered an entire lifetime at the hands of a volatile husband that wouldn’t let her enjoy a second of independence.

A moment passed in silence, then “I may have already gotten a job.” Rio couldn’t help but smirk guiltily.

“Ay dios mio, you’ve done it now! How are you going to explain that one?” Claudia asked.

Rio tried to put on her best puppy dog eyes. “Please, can you just tell Tony that you got me a cleaner position like you? Maybe he will accept it if it's something familiar.”

“And what are you actually doing?”

“Shop assistant at a pharmacy. Nothing fancy.” Rio replied.

“What do you know about all that? You’ve never worked in a shop before!” Claudia chuckled at the thought.

“Hey, they really needed help and they are going to pay weekly in cash! I can learn whatever they want. It can’t be that hard.”

“Alright Rio, but you owe me for this.” She headed to the kitchen to start prepping supper.

Rio waited for Tony to get back, but as the hours passed and the sun set, she started to wonder where he could be. She readied herself for bed when she finally heard the front door open.

As she was standing in front of her dressing mirror, taking her hair down. A boisterous voice called out “Rio! Mi amor! Wonderful news - I got a job downtown. Meet the newest longshoreman of the Manhattan Docks.”

He tumbled into the bedroom and lifted Rio off her feet in a twirl. They laughed in relief and joy before falling into bed. His eyes staring deep into hers, trying to convey what he couldn’t say out loud - I’ll be better for you.

Tony placed a big wet kiss on her, and she tried not to pull away. Tried to feel grateful and enamored - rather than guarded and repelled. She had so much love for her boyfriend, despite his faults. But something had shifted, and she hoped it wasn’t permanent.

Maybe it will be okay. Rio let herself hope and decided not to tell Tony about her own adventure today. She knew that dock worker hours were long, and the subway journey from their place in Washington Heights to Manhattan would be time consuming. He doesn’t have to know - was the last thought as she drifted to sleep.

She woke up the next morning regretting her spur of the moment job hunt. Should she even bother anymore? Something inside her felt excited at the prospect of getting out of the house though, and she resolved to give it at least a day. If she felt uncomfortable or completely out of place, she could always quit. No harm, no foul.

Luckily, Claudia came through and said that she needed an extra pair of hands this week for a big cleaning job at a nearby office building. Suddenly, Tony didn’t seem as fussed about Rio leaving the house; he was too elated in his own prospects to see much else.

She left the house promptly at 9:15am, donning her dark green cloche hat, longline wool coat, and walked the 20 minutes to Westview Pharmacy for her first day.

Lilia smiled as Rio entered the drugstore, the bell dinging as usual when the door clicked open. “Welcome Rio, glad you made it.”

“Of course, I wouldn’t miss it. Where should I put my things?” Rio asked earnestly.

“I’ll show you to the backroom, follow me.” Lillia quickly rounded the counter and walked them towards the back of the small shop. Through a wooden door, they were in a little lounge room with a few sitting chairs, a dining table, and storage shelves.

“You can place your bag on the shelf, and hang your things up here” She pointed to the coat rack along the wall.

Rio noticed the most beautiful coat hanging up already. A deep navy blue, verging on teal, with a stunning purple silk interior from what she could see along the cuffs. It was clearly custom, tailored to perfection, and utterly original. Whoever wore that coat meant business. From the little she knew of Lilia, it did not fit her in the slightest. So who could the owner be? There wasn’t anyone else in the shop that she could see.

“Whose coat is that?” Rio asked innocently.

Lilia didn’t even need to glance back at the coat rack to know what she was referring to. “The Big Cheese herself” She laughed. “Don’t worry about that for now, I have to make sure you’re on the level first before you go meeting anyone else.”

Rio’s brow knitted in confusion for a moment, wondering who else there could be. However, this passed quickly as she jumped into her first day of work. She learned the in’s and out’s of everything the shop sold, where the products came from, how to work the ancient cash register, how to stock a shelf, who the regular customers were, and every other piece of knowledge Lilia could bestow upon her.

Around 11am, a young man entered the store. “Lilia, I’m here!” He announced loudly. Dressed in grey slacks with a slightly wrinkled white shirt and tan suspenders, he sauntered down to greet them.

“Billy, will you keep it down? I’m training our new little bird - meet Rio.”

“Hi Rio, pleasure to meet you. I run the soda fountain during the week. I can’t wait to work together! It’s been a pain handling the lunch rush alone.”

Rio extended her hand, which Billy shook quickly. “Nice to meet you too.” She stated plainly. Her mind overfilled with all that she had learned that she could barely register the teen. Lilia continued her training until being thrown into the deep end of lunch service with Billy.

“Okay, here they come! It’s really not so bad. Just write down each order on a ticket, post it up here, and move on to the next one. I’ll handle the rest.” He ended it in a wink as the customers started taking up stools along the counter.

Rio was a quick study and found it surprisingly easy to converse with the customers. Her idle chit chat kept them occupied as Billy whipped through orders with efficiency and grace. Egg creams flew along the counter as well as all types of cordials, juices, and fancy sodas. Hot food rolled out from the commissary next door, and the patrons left full and satisfied.

“Rio, I’m out of sugar syrup. Can you run to the back and grab a few more bottles? Just go through the back door to the storage basement in the back alley. Quick!” Billy rang out with urgency.

She finished writing down the latest order and hurried out the back with haste. As she flung open the door out the back, it collided with something or someone. “Oh god damn it! Ouch!”

Standing in the alleyway, grasping her shoulder, was a woman. Her hair was old-fashioned and should have looked unfashionable on someone her age. Not the trendy bob cut but an older, Victorian era high bun that somehow seemed to fit. Her dress was casual, clearly just meant for working around the house yet it had a hem line dangerously close to her knees. Rio felt heat rise to her cheeks as she tried to quickly raise her gaze. As her eyes moved up, she caught exposed shoulders and beautiful toned arms, finally settling on the stunning blue eyes squinting in pain.

“I’m sorry!” She squealed out quickly. Stunned at both her own carelessness and at the sight of this gorgeous woman before her.

“Now who the hell are you and what are you doing in my alley?” The words rolled off her tongue in a mocking tone, with just enough bite to make Rio stutter.

“I didn’t know anyone was out here. I was just trying to get to the storeroom, we’re out of sugar syrup and,” Rio paused, finding herself stumbling over her words in the presence of this intimidating figure.

The blue eyes searched her face, pausing on the ghost of Tony’s anger that still haunted her cheek, before giving her the old up-and-down to take in her full figure. She felt stripped bare by that look in a way that made her chest feel tight. A pleasant embarrassment she hadn’t felt since Tony first asked her to dance all those years ago.

Rio finally finished her thought, “I’m so sorry, umm, what’s your name?”

“They call me Agatha, bunny. Agatha “Mother” Harkness.”

Curiosity blooms

Rio hurried down the alley and down the stairwell into the basement storage room to grab the supplies for Billy. As she re-emerged into the light, she only saw the whisper of Agatha’s purple dress disappear into a nondescript side door in the alley. She hadn’t even noticed the door at first, but she took in the tiny panel at eye height and the way it seemed to almost disappear into the brick wall unless you were looking for it.

“What took you so long?” Billy griped when Rio finally made it back inside. There was a large group of patrons crowding the counter.

“I’m so sorry, I ran into Agatha as I was running out and might have hurt her. I hope she doesn’t think I’m a total fool.”

“Oh, you met Mother! Don’t sweat it, she’s harmless…well, if you’re on her good side anyway.” He laughed at his own inside joke.

“What does she do here?”

“What doesn’t she do here?” He quipped back. “I’ve been obsessed since I first stumbled into this shop three years ago. I was trying to steal some cans of soup for my brother and I when she caught me. Thought I was a goner, but she offered me a job instead. Haven’t left her side ever since.”

Billy finished putting the bottles away and was back on the soda fountain pouring drinks. “Sorry, doll, can’t say anymore! The people need me.”

Rio went back to taking down orders quickly. When she finally checked the wall clock again, she could not believe that it was nearly 4pm. Having previously spent her days at home, running errands, or with friends, she was shocked at how quickly work made time disappear.

She finished the day at the cash register, and Lilia came by to check on her. “How was your first day?”

“I’m surprised that it’s already almost over! That lunch rush is no joke. I don’t know how Billy handled that on his own before.” Rio suddenly became aware of the ache in her legs from standing all day. It was going to take a while to adjust to being on her feet for such a long time.

“Oh don’t let him hear that, he’ll get a big head! We’re just glad you’re here now. I’m very impressed with your work ethic, young lady.” She smiled at Rio and noticed the subtle blush forming on her pale cheeks.

“Thanks Lillia, I’m so grateful to you for giving me this chance.” Rio was starting to feel like she belonged for the first time since she set foot in the US.

When she made it back to her apartment at 5:30pm, she shed her work clothes which smelled vaguely of the sweet drinks prepared by Billy all afternoon, and started to cook dinner before Tony’s imminent arrival.

He made it back about an hour after her and practically fell through the door. With a lunch pail in hand, he walked in like there were concrete blocks on his feet before falling onto the couch. “I don’t think my body is going to survive this.”

“Come on, tough guy.” Rio stepped away from the oven to playfully jab his sides. “Where’s that fighting spirit like Jack Dempsey? Weren’t you the top featherweight boxer at Paradiso College?”

“That boy is long gone. I am just an old man, and nobody told me the docks were going to grind me to a pulp.”

“Old man? You’re 25, Tony, get a grip.” Rio couldn’t help but chuckle at his dramatics.

He rolled off the couch and struggled to his feet. “Not all of us enjoy a life of luxury at home, my dear.” He approached and kissed her softly.

She tensed, feeling guilt blanket her thoughts at the way he looked at her. He believed she was tending to the home, taking care of her plants, cooking their meals. Being the good housewife that everyone expected. How could she lie?

But then she would remember the feeling of his hand on her face and the lack of acknowledgement of it since, and the lie seemed to simply roll off the tongue, “Hey, I was out with Claudia today. That was hard work too! On top of that, someone has to take care of this household, and it surely isn’t going to be you!” She turned back to stir the soup on the stovetop, tamping down the cry of ache from her own sore legs.

She has never had a better night sleep than that dreamless slumber after her first day of work. The next morning, she got up early, hearing Tony leave around 6am. She quickly powered through her chores for the day before she needed to leave herself. She mopped the bathroom, scrubbed the bathtub, hand washed a bucket of laundry, and hung it out on the balcony line. Satisfied with the state of the place, she grabbed her bag and headed out to the pharmacy.

Instead of Lilia at the counter, she was taken aback when she saw Agatha rearranging the cigarette cartons.

“Hello, Mrs. Harkness” She watched her turn slowly and admired the scarlet lipstick that adorned her lips and the prominent brooch that sat over the top button of her collared dress.

“Oh don’t go calling me that now, sweets. I’ll think you’re talking about the devil herself who gave birth to me. Mrs. Harkness is a hard old bag that unfortunately shares my name. I prefer Agatha, but some just stick to Mother, dealer’s choice.” She turned to face Rio and spread her hands on the counter in front of her.

“You here to tend to my arm? I say, it’s still a bit sore from our little kerfuffle yesterday. You could kiss it better?” Agatha threw her a wink and a pout, showing off her bruised elbow.

Rio couldn’t keep up with the pace or the guile of this new person in her presence. There was something so disarming, so unabashedly confident, so…intriguing about Agatha. “I’m sorry?”

“Just razzing you, bunny. Lilia told me you’re the new assistant. Welcome to the coven.”

“Thanks Mrs…Agatha.” Rio stopped herself before speaking out of turn again. She felt electric, like Agatha was lighting up her every nerve.

Agatha’s lips turned into a signature smirk, “Just can’t help yourself, huh? Well, I’m just finishing up in here, then back to it. Tell Billy to come see me when he gets in.” She turned to head out the back door. Rio studied her outfit carefully, impressed at the cut and style. Agatha was a vision in a spring suit with a shepherd check pattern. Its fancy overcollar and belted waist accentuated her curves, while the long matching skirt hit at the mid-calf and Rio felt herself lick her lips subconsciously.

“Wait,” Rio’s curiosity was overwhelming. “Can I ask you something?”

“Depends what you want to know.” Agatha turned and caught the way Rio smiled shyly at her response, as if she had said some dirty joke.

“What’s in that door in the alley? The one along the wall?”

“Hmmm,” Agatha tapped her lips with her fingers. Rio noticed the large diamond ring adorning her middle finger. “That’s for me to know,” She strolled down the shop to the back, “and you to find out.” She yelled out as the door shut behind her.

Rio huffed in response. She went to hang up her coat and hat, then heard Lillia enter from the alley. “Alright there, Rio?”

“Yes, ma’am. Just had a little chat with Agatha when I arrived.” Lilia saw the attempt to veil her frustration. Oh no, what has Agatha done this time, Lilia thought.

“Don’t fret about her. She loves to beat her gums, but try not to take anything to heart. She loves to play with people as if they were toys. It’s all about control - just show her she can’t walk all over you, and you’ll be sorted.”

“But, I just want to know what she does here.” Rio replied.

“Trust me when I say to let this one go, dear. Just for now. I know you’re curious, but let her get to know you, and I’m sure you’ll find out soon. Some things require a little…discretion, if you catch my drift.”

Rio did not catch anything but could take the hint to drop it. “Alright, where should I start today?”

“Got a new shipment of candy this morning, can you stock it on the shelves near the end of the soda counter?”

Billy arrived as she was finishing up her last box. “Hi Billy, Agatha told me that she wanted to speak to you when you got in.”

“Thanks, Rio. I’ll head out back now - catch ya in a few!” He bounded out the door like a zooming puppy. His enthusiasm felt contagious.

She watched him slip back in half an hour later and carry on as usual. “So - what did the boss want?” She questioned him as innocently as possibly.

“Nothing much, just asking if I could stay late today to help her move some boxes.” He kept it short, and Rio felt him itching to say more. He wasn’t making eye contact and was wiping out the same glass that was sparkling clean.

“Is that all?” She put on her best pleading eyes, but he was still staring intently at his task as if it was the most entertaining thing in the world.

“Yup!” He set down the glasses. “I’ve gotta go grab some extra straws from the store room before service really kicks in, be right back.” Billy rushed out before Rio could press any further. She scrunched her face as he avoided any more questioning.

When he got back, they fell into the same rhythm as yesterday, and Rio felt herself lost again to the quickly spinning minute hand. As she walked to the back room to grab her things to go, she saw two new coats hung up along her own.

One was the lightest baby pink, wool, more cape than coat. The other was leather, a masculine cut though too small to fit Billy, with bold pockets on the front. Who were all these people? She couldn’t fathom where Agatha stashed them all away, and what they could all possibly be doing for this tiny pharmacy.

“Vidal!” Lillia called from the front at the cash register and beckoned Rio over as she was preparing to head home. “Friday is payday. It’s not a full week as you only worked two days, but hope this helps.” She deposited 8 dollars into an envelope and handed it over.

Rio looked down at the cash - her first ever earnings. She felt not just relief but pride. She could buy meat from the butcher, actual cuts, not just the off scraps that she had to barter for. She could afford vegetables for the week and maybe even a few apples if she got lucky at the corner market. In just a few more weeks, she would be able to cover their month’s rent if something happened with Tony’s job. She wouldn’t be entirely dependent on him anymore. At that thought, a tear threatened to fall.

Lilia watched her reaction and felt such sympathetic compassion for the young woman. It was barely enough yet to her it was clearly a lifeline to her. “Don’t go spending it all in one place now.” She tried to jest with her as she saw Rio’s emotions begin to spill over.

“Don’t worry, I ain’t a total sap.” She laughed in response and wiped her eyes quickly. She gave Lilia a quick look of thanks before stuffing the envelope quickly into her purse and heading home.

The wizened woman walked to turn the sign on the door to ‘closed’ and heard movement behind her. “Are you getting soft on me, ya old broad?” Agatha had been lingering in the backroom.

“What are you doing hiding out back there like some rascally ragamuffin?” Lillia continued closing out the register and counting the day’s take.

“What do you see in that girl?” Agatha came into the shop and helped stack the counter stools.

“What do you?” She answered in retort, eyebrow raised curiously.

“I didn’t even know you hired her! She practically bumped me off yesterday when she flew out the door without looking. She’s clearly in over her head, and I’d be shocked if she’s ever worked a day in her life.”

“Oh please, I saw the way you looked at her this morning. You see it too. She’s lost, looking for somewhere to belong, somewhere to feel wanted. Not unlike some other lost girl I took in not so long ago.”

“Hey, don’t even compare us! I was never that clueless.” Agatha laughed. She wasn’t ready to admit that there was something about Rio that made her want to know more. “Well, I had some spunk at least. Rio seems as timid as a baby deer. She can barely take a joke.”

Lilia remembered fondly when she first saw a young Agatha almost twenty years ago. She had just moved to town from Boston and came into the pharmacy every week to pick up odds and ends and occasionally indulge in a strawberry milkshake. Lilia’s father was absolutely charmed by the woman and looked forward to her visits. He would fawn over her every word, just like every other man (or woman) who happened to cross her path.

Meanwhile, Lilia thought her to be a bit too chummy for her own good but something in her eyes gave her pause. Agatha put on an unbreakable front with humor and banter, yet Lilia noted the lingering sadness under the surface and unrelenting need for attention, for acceptance.

“Have a little heart, Agatha. I think she’s fighting a battle we know nothing about. This isn’t just any old job to her. I saw that she didn’t want this, she could barely gather the courage to walk into the store. I saw her standing on the corner for ages before she finally came in. But she did, I think she’s meant to be here.”

Agatha played with her nails thoughtlessly as she mulled over Lilia’s summation on her newest employee. “Fine, but she’s not to know what we really do here until I say so. I know your gut is always right, but she needs time and so do I. I need to know we’re not tooting the wrong ringer, that we can trust her completely.”

Lilia shut the register with a satisfying ding and handed the cash to the boss before clocking out herself. “Mother knows best.”

Her first trial

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

The routine of the pharmacy provided a stability in Rio’s life that she didn’t know was missing before. Although she had never felt more exhausted at day’s end, she also never felt more alive. The regular customers greeted her like an old friend each day, and she felt a sense of self-worth that she never garnered from housework alone.

Tony was none the wiser as his work kept him completely occupied from dawn to dusk and wiped him out mentally when he finally made it home. The pay was a bit less than the cigar factory, the hours definitely worse, but the stability was worth the trade in his eyes.

Rio no longer worried about making rent or affording groceries. His wages covered most of their needs, although she usually had to supplement the rising cost of food most weeks, but she was still able to stash a good portion of her cash away.

She tenderly placed the bills in an old wooden cigar box that she brought from PR. It used to store a few necklaces and bracelets that she had collected over the years, but now she looked at it as her emergency plan.

It had been over a month since Tony had a drink of the hard stuff, and he was back to his usual jovial self, albeit a lot more tired. The anger was gone from his demeanor, and yet Rio could not forget. It wasn't an elephant in the room, it was a ghost. No matter how she tried to push past it and see the man in front of her now, sober, hard-working, trying his best to provide for them both, she was stubborn - always had been.

“Mija, if you keep sticking your tongue out at your sister, one day it’s going to stick like that!”

Her mother had pestered her with that threat when she was 8, and of course, being Rio she needed to prove her mom wrong. She kept her tongue out for almost two days straight in protest,

“Theee mamá! Look, it’sss not duck!” Each word barely intelligible.

She slurred out the words as best she could to make her point, satisfied that she had won.

All her mother could do was roll her eyes, “What am I going to do with you? God bless the man who even attempts to win your hand.”

“Hah! No man can win anything from me!” Rio ran off at the thought.

She was the fastest kid in her class, even beating the boys who stood several inches taller. She could jump higher, swim farther, and was the top pick for the neighborhood baseball games played every afternoon after school. She was the only girl they would let play, mostly because every boy knew she would shove them in the dirt if they tried to stop her.

“One day, I’m going to see a real baseball game!”

She would declare to her father at the dinner table, nearly shaking with excitement as she kicked her feet under the table.

“I know you will, mija.”

And he wasn’t lying. In her short life, everything his daughter set her mind to, she accomplished.

She was headstrong to a fault, but he loved her determination and drive. He didn’t know where she would end up, but he never worried that she would make something of herself. He only worried about what kind husband would be able to accept her completely.

Rio knew Tony was a good man. She saw it in the way he held her hand when they walked down the sidewalk together. How he held the door open for her every single time, how he sacrificed his time and his body to provide. But she also now knew that a monster lurked under his skin. An angry, violent beast that could crush her without a second thought.

And she hated how much that made her afraid and timid despite herself. She felt the way she was changing around him. She despised hearing the way her voice pitched up when speaking to him, how she hesitated before speaking where she would normally jest and joke, how she gave in to his wandering hands at night despite the exhaustion that was threatening to bump her off.

“Please, mi vida, I need you.” He would roughly whisper in her ear, and what could she say in reply?

I don’t want this, I don’t want you.

That wasn’t what a woman was meant to say, and she didn’t want to know what might happen if she did. So, she lay there silently, pretending she was the same, that she still felt the same fire for him that once existed. She would feel him move on top of her, enter her, sweat on her, and she would feel - nothing.

Every payday, when she opened the bottom drawer of her wooden dressing table, lifted the spare fabric that obscured her hidden cigar box and added to her growing savings, she finally felt something - she felt strong and powerful.

Like each dollar was another chain of armor that she was molding into place, like together the dollars could form into a hot air balloon and carry her away like the Wizard of Oz, her favorite book as child. She would smile at the thought and allow herself a moment to daydream, before snapping the lid closed and getting back to reality.

At the pharmacy, Billy was training her on how to run the soda fountain. He showed her how to make each drink, where to find all the ingredients, which customers to look out for, how to prepare the simple menu, and how to clean as you go.

No stranger to the kitchen, Rio found it surprisingly easy.

“One rootbeer phosphate for Mr. Jones, a hot butterscotch sundae for Jimmy, and a frosted coffee for Ms. Henderson.” She slid each order down the counter to great effect.

“Wow Rio, you’re a natural!” Billy was impressed by her calm confidence. “No wonder Lilia hired you on the spot, you’ve got a real gift for service.”

“Enough chummy talk, mac. Let’s get these people their orders!” Rio blushed at the compliment and got them back to work quickly to avoid further embarrassment.

At the end of the day, as she was wiping down the fountain, she overheard Billy.

“Lilia, I promised I would go with Tommy to the movie palace to see Robin Hood tomorrow. Can I please have the afternoon off? I’ll work late instead, I swear!”

“I can cover for him” Rio piped up quickly.

“Hot dog! That would be amazing Rio, thank you thank you.” Billy was almost jumping for joy.

“Now wait just a minute young man,” Lilia looked at him sternly, “you can’t just expect Rio to handle the day alone, she’s only been here for a month, and she’s only just learned how to run the fountain.”

“She’s amazing, Lilia, come on. I’ve already seen her handle the lunch crowd like it’s a walk in the park.” He threw out his arms. “It’s just one afternoon!”

Lilia considered the argument carefully.

“Fine, but you’re going to have to go speak to Agatha about how you’re going to make it up. You know she’s not in the business of giving things away for free.”

Billy was out the back door before she could even finish that sentence. Lilia walked over from the register, “Are you sure you can handle it, Rio?”

“The boy’s a good teacher. I think I’ll be fine.” Rio folded up her apron and placed it under the counter.

“If you say so, but don't come grovelling to me if things get too hectic.”

“Never!” Rio laughed casually and bid farewell to Lilia before heading home.

What’s the worst that could happen?

That was her last thought before drifting to sleep that night.

Everything seemed fine at first, she started her shift as usual by helping Lilia open the store and re-stocking the shelves. As she began preparing the soda fountain for lunch service, Lilia received a phone call.

“I can’t. No, you’ll need to sort it out…Jen, you have to handle this, please.”

Rio could just hear the soft conversation as she cleaned the glassware. “Okay, I’m coming, but we need to be fast. I’ll drive the flivver and pick you up.”

Lilia donned her coat and hat and approached Rio quickly.

“Doll, I need to run out to grab some supplies for the store. I would never normally leave you alone, but unfortunately this can’t wait. I trust you. If you need any help, just knock on the alley door and Agatha will come help. I’ll be back in jiffy.”

She was alone. Take a breath.

She tried to focus her thoughts on the moment rather than the panic that was ready to pounce. Lilia’s counting on you, you can do this. She prepped her station like Billy had shown her and prepared for the incoming onslaught. Maybe it won’t be so bad today.

“Where’s Billy?”

“What’s the hold up?”

“Rio!”

“Rio, over here I was first!”

“No, I was first!”

“You forgot my parfait!”

"I need a fork!”

"Where's my order?"

"Rio, I need a refill!”

“Rio!”

“ Rio!! ”

The voices reverberated around the tiny shop and seemed to coalesce right around Rio’s ears. She stared at the impatient customers crowding her workspace. Every order she pushed out seemed to be replaced by ten more, like a hydra with hundreds of heads threatening to squeeze her to death.

“Egg cream, up!” She did her best to shout above the chaos.

I wish Lilia was here.

Rio stared longingly at the door in hopes that her saviour may magically appear at any moment and save her. The bell dinged and she looked expectedly but was let down by the sight of even more customers looking for their soda fix. I don’t know how I’m going to make it.

She wiped her brow as the pressure continued to build, her hands started to shake from the nerves. She was mixing a frosted coffee when her grip slipped and the glass shattered on the tiled floor. The sudden noise finally cut through the cacophony and caused the customers to quiet for a moment.

The sound of clicking heels was thus able to rise above the din of impatience in front of her.

“What in the devil is going on in here?” Agatha’s raised voice completely silenced the entire establishment.

“Well?" She looked at the stunned faces with expectation. "What’s all this racket then?”

The crowd parted and revealed the disheveled Rio at the centre of the hurricane, doing her best to write down orders, pour drinks, and deliver food.

“Agatha! What are you doing here?" Rio stumbled to appear competent though the obvious bedlam was a bit of a giveaway. “I’m fine, I’m handling it.”

“Step aside, pet.”

She rolled up the sleeves of her blouse and slotted in beside Rio behind the counter.

She leaned close and Rio could feel the heat of her breath against her as Agatha whispered, “Take the orders, and let me handle the rest.” Goosebumps prickled across Rio’s arm.

They steadily knocked out each order with a speed and efficiency that she didn’t even experience when working with Billy. Rio would write down each order and pass it to Agatha who would somehow conjure the order in no time flat, as if it were magic. Rio felt the need to remind herself to close her mouth while staring in awe at this woman’s skill.

The way Agatha commanded the crowd like they were under a spell, the way she seemed to float along the bartop handing out orders at record speed, the way she would throw a smile to Rio whenever she handed off a ticket. It was intoxicating being in her presence.

When she finally closed out the last customer and slipped them the final receipt for the day, Agatha turned to her, saying each word with a delicate command, “Next time, just ask for help.”

“I didn't want to bother you.”Rio took a rag and started wiping down the counter. “I thought I could handle it alone.” She couldn’t help but laugh at the absurdity.

“Yeah? And I thought Mrs. Reynolds was one second away from ripping you limb from limb if you didn’t get her chocolate malt out soon!” Agatha let out a small snort of laughter while remembering the scene she had walked into.

That was adorable. Rio’s mind was quickly trying to think of other ways she could hear the little snort again.

“If you had just given me another minute, I could have gotten them under control.” Rio tried to argue.

“Those animals? Ha! You’d have better luck trying to wrangle the animals of the Central Park Zoo!” Agatha shook her head, a few locks of her brunette hair falling from her bun.

“Ah fine, I was out of my depth. Thank you, you saved me.”

“Hey, I was just trying to save my business!” Agatha smiled softly. Even though Rio had nearly started a riot in her shop, she just couldn’t bring herself to reprimand her or tell her off. Even now, looking sheepish and remorseful, Rio still looked utterly charming.

“Well, I’m glad you were here, whatever the reason. I was so behind the eight ball.”

“And how! You can say that again. I was working out back and could hear the cacophony through however many layers of brick. I came in expecting a stick up or something, not just a bunch of hungry fools.”

Agatha moved towards Rio and put a gentle hand on her arm, “Don’t beat yourself up too much. The first time Billy ran the shop by himself, we had to call the fire department to put out a small blaze that started when he attempted to flambé a banana.”

Rio bowled over laughter but immediately missed the warmth of Agatha's touch. “You’re joking!”

Her laughs filled the room, a welcome change from the noise in here just a few hours ago.

“Whose bright idea was it to leave you alone anyway? Where’s that old broad?” Agatha searched around for Lilia.

“She got a phone call around 11 from someone, I think named Jen? She took off in a hurry and said it would be quick.” Rio remembered the hasty departure.

“I’ll have to see about that.”

Agatha went to the telephone and started to dial a number before the front door opened and Lilia strolled in with another woman. Rio took in the gorgeous gold earrings and short bob haircut on this new lady. She was wearing an intricately beaded dress and mary janes, and carrying two large briefcases in her hands.

“Lilia, Jen, where have you been?” Agatha stared them down with her hands on her hips. “You can’t just leave Rio alone to manage the shop.”

“We had a problem with…” Jen glanced at Rio, who quietly went back to mopping the floors, “one of our suppliers.” She finished and gave Agatha a knowing look.

“Okay, let's discuss. I’ll be there in a second.” Lilia and Jen headed out to the alley and Agatha lingered for a moment.

“Good work in the end, Rio.” She grabbed a pen and scrawled down a note. “You’ve got something about you, bunny.”

Agatha reached her hand out and Rio grasped it. She felt her slip the note into her palm without acknowledgement.

“See you around.” And with a wink, she was gone.

Rio took a second to calm her nerves. She couldn’t understand what it was about Agatha that flustered her so. Every time she spoke to her, it was like her lungs forgot how to function properly, every breath felt labored and manual. Her skin seemed sensitive to every stimuli and her blood seemed to pump at a rapid rate through her veins. Is it hot in here all of a sudden?

She glanced down at the note in her hand. Agatha’s looping script matched her personality perfectly - composed, elegant, yet slightly on edge.

“Saturday night, 10pm. Knock twice on the alley door, at the prompt - reply with ‘a door appears.’ Wear your best dancing shoes.”

Rio read it twice, confused at the contents but knew it must be important.

Whatever went on through that alley door, she was about to find out.

Chapter End Notes

Thanks for reading.

Next up, we finally go down, down, down (the alley door).

Down, down, down

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

After work on Friday, Rio went home and waited for Claudia. She knew Tony was going to be out late as was his normal knock off tradition of poker with the other men from the neighborhood. She knew he would be back around 9pm at the latest, so she had a few hours at least to prepare for her own night out.

Claudia finally arrived at 5:45pm. “How was work?” Rio asked.

“Just forty more years to go.” Claudia deadpanned back, hanging her coat on the coat rack.

“You could say that again,” Rio smiled then continued, “On a lighter note, I could use your ever helpful advice.”

Claudia’s eyes lit a little despite the dim from a day of hard labor, “Oh yeah? Tell me more!”

“I have an invite to a night out on Saturday, but I don’t have a clue what to wear.”

“What kind of night out?” Claudia eyed her inquisitively. “Are we talking about the theatre, dinner, dancing, or…something else?”

“That’s the thing - I’m not really sure…” Rio fussed with a loose thread on her sleeve. “All I know is that I’m meant to wear dancing shoes, and I’m going to need a hell of an excuse to explain to Tony why I’m going out at 10pm.”

“And who, may I ask, extended this invitation to you?”

“My boss,” Rio began, “but I don’t think it’s for work. I think she wants to show me something.” She tried to keep it vague as even she didn’t really know why Agatha had offered her this fascinating invite.

“Grab your things, we’re not going to solve this here!” Claudia picked her coat and purse back up, glad that she hadn’t kicked off her heels just yet.

“Where are we going?” Rio quickly ran to her room to grab some of her money and a more appropriate coat for the chill of a night out in March.

“The place that has everything, darling - Macy’s.” Claudia pulled Rio out the door and over to the nearby subway station. They rode downtown, and she led them to the pinnacle of department store shopping.

“Where should we begin?” Claudia twiddled her fingers together as if plotting a heist. “Let’s start with the dress and build around that.” She headed towards the women’s department on the second floor.

They browsed the racks and racks of dresses but none seemed quite right for Rio. She only had a few casual dresses that she cycled through each day and had never had the money to afford something from a store like this. The amount of choices was overwhelming.

“Check this out, Rio!” She held up an emerald green shift dress with a hanky hem that would probably hit just below Rio’s knees. It was sleeveless, which would be a first for her wardrobe, and had elegant beading on the side gathered design.

“How lovely, I’ll try it on at least.”

She took the dress to the fitting room nearby and changed. Her white slip was visible underneath the evening gown, and her stockings were the wrong colour entirely, but she admired herself in the mirror with surprise.

“Let’s see then!” Claudia called from outside.

Rio strutted out to show off, and Claudia had a small gasp when she took in the dress. “Just call you a tomato, because you’re ripe for the picking!”

At that, she almost did resemble the red fruit with how deeply colored her cheeks turned. “You’re terrible!” She said covering her face with her hands.

“You’re going to need to carry around a bat to swat away all the men who are going to be whistling your name. That dress is a killer! You’re buying it - no arguing.” Claudia clapped in finality.

“Now we just need some more appropriate undergarments, proper dancing shoes, and a matching coat.”

They settled on some sturdy black T-strap heels and a jade shawl to cover her exposed shoulders. Rio chose to forgo a corset, “There’s not much to strap down anyway.”

Instead, she picked out one of the new bandeau bras and a step-in silk chemise that would not be visible under the dress that was much shorter than her others. Black stockings and accompanying garter belt were the final touches. Plus Rio didn’t want to blow too much dough all in one trip.

“I hope you know what you’re getting into,” Claudia warned as they left the store, “because you’re going to turn some heads in this get up.”

Am I making a mistake? Rio wondered to herself. She was going out alone, no Tony. She had never been out on the town without him, but after a month of working and gaining independence she didn’t feel as nervous as she expected. There’s a first time for everything.

As they rode the subway back, Claudia asked, “Where are you going to say you’re going anyway?”

Rio held tightly to her Macy’s bags and contemplated the answer. She still wasn’t sure what excuse would make sense. “Open to suggestions.”

“How about I tell Miguel to take Tony to the Central Park Casino? He knows a guy who works the door there and can get them in.”

“Gambling? He just got over one vice, I would rather he didn’t pick up another.”

“Be real, doll. You aren’t going to find many places open that late that aren’t speakeasies, gambling houses, brothels, or other seedy hubs.” Claudia certainly kept her honest.

Rio sighed, “I suppose it beats the alternative.” She paused then, “okay, see if Miguel can convince him.”

“Something tells me it won’t take much convincing!”

They made it home before the men, and Rio put away her new purchases in her dresser, which Tony never looked in anyway. Claudia walked into her bedroom with a long, green bakelite necklace and beautiful dangling gold earrings.

“Are these real?” Rio ran her fingers over the earrings.

“You can pretend they are. Pretty good, huh? Miguel got them from a pawn shop for just a buck, but they look like the real thing. I think they’ll go great with your look, and the necklace is the icing on top.”

“Thanks Claudia, I couldn’t have done any of this without your help.” Rio hugged her roommate. The excitement for the upcoming night was already building within her.

“Don’t mention it,” Claudia pulled away from the hug, “The only thing I ask is you give me all the juicy details when you get back!”

“Deal.” Rio shook her hand.

Saturday night approached with fervent anticipation. Rio took care of some grocery shopping in the morning, did a few buckets of laundry, and had some time to read the latest mystery novel she had picked up at the bookstore.

Tony approached around lunchtime, “Guess what?” He came to sit beside her on the couch, “Miguel is going to take me out to the casino tonight.”

“Oh really?” Rio feigned surprise and tried to hide her smirk as Claudia’s plan unfolded before her.

“It’s probably going to be a late night, so don’t wait up.” He kissed her cheek. “I promise not to get up to too much mischief.”

“You better not!” Rio warned. “Don’t go gambling away our savings either.”

“Eh, I’m not much of a gambler, you know me. I’m more just interested in what goes on in there. I’ve heard some fellas talk about it at work, but it's all very hush hush.”

“Okay but Antonio” She said his full name for emphasis. “Please don’t drink.”

“Yes, of course. Don’t worry.” He tried to soothe her fears. “We’re heading out around 8pm, not sure what time we’ll be back.”

“Alright, be careful,” she said, “I may be heading to early morning service at 8am, so try not to wake me when you get in.”

Rio hoped the lie of church service would be enough cover but hoped she wouldn’t have to actually make good on it.

After dinner and listening to the Yankees game on the radio, the men took off on their big night out, and Rio started prepping. She dressed quietly in her room, luxuriating over the feel of the nice fabrics that were so different from her normal clothing. She rolled the rayon stockings up each leg and clipped them onto her garter belt. She let the new dress fall down her body like water - smoothing out each wrinkle with her hands.

The new shoes fit like a dream and Claudia’s jewellery matched like they had planned it ahead of time. She used combs to wave her hair, which shortened it from its normal length right above her shoulder, and parted it on her left side to create an elegant curly bob.

To complete the look, she applied a dab of pink rouge to her cheeks, a smoky dark eye shadow, and a heavier-than-usual eyeliner. She searched for her trusty red lipstick but couldn’t find the tub in her dressing table anywhere. Guess, I’ll skip that for tonight.

She decided to leave early to give herself time to get there, having never walked it at night before. “I’m off, Claudia! Wish me luck.” She grabbed her leather envelope bag and made for the door.

Claudia came out of her room, and her eyes bulged at the sight of Rio.

She whistled slowly, “You look incredible. That dress is the berries! Don’t do anything I wouldn’t do.”

The streets of Washington Heights and Upper Manhattan felt sinister at this time of night, but Rio knew the route like the back of her hand. She passed a few unsavory characters along the way and was thankful for the electric street lamps that exposed anything that may have frightened her in the pitch black of night.

When she arrived at the familiar street of Westview Pharmacy, she looked around for a sign of where to go next. She only saw a few people milling about. Men returning home from late shifts, young couples off to the clubs in the main strip of Harlem, and groups of women searching for some place to show off their dance moves.

Rio rounded the building and approached from the back street, straight into the back alley behind the shop. She didn’t see anyone else back here and it was very dimly lit, only getting light from the upper windows reflecting the streetlamps. She approached the alley door and remembered Agatha’s note clearly in her mind.

Knock, knock

She rapped twice and heard nothing. She waited a moment and was ready to give it up, upset that Agatha had fooled her, when the small hatch on the door slid open with a sudden flourish.

“Tame your fears” A female voice whispered quietly but clearly out the slit.

Rio gulped. It felt like a directive specifically for her.

“A door appears.” She replied calmly just as the note had said.

“Welcome” The voice replied as the door swung open towards Rio. She stepped through.

“You must be Rio,” An Asian woman extended her hand. “Names Alice.”

She was wearing wool tweed knee-length knickers paired with knee high socks, like a male golfer, a khaki shirt and that striking leather jacket Rio had spotted a few days ago. She had never seen a woman dressed in such a manner outside of a sporting context, but it seemed to suit her personality and the nature of what appeared to be her job.

Rio shook her hand firmly, impressed at her grip. “Nice to finally meet you Alice.”

She took in the small landing room they were in. It was tiny, exposed brick on all the walls with a single lightbulb overhead. Nothing but a chair for Alice, a cabinet on one wall, and a large staircase leading straight down.

“Agatha told me you were coming tonight. Just head down the stairs and you’ll see.” Alice motioned her forward.

“Thanks, hopefully I’ll see you later.” Rio replied before carefully walking the wooden steps down, down, down.

She tried to imagine where she was in relation to the alley. This was clearly a basement below the shops next door to the pharmacy. She wondered how Agatha had commandeered the land from them, or did she own other buildings too?

At the base of the stairs were three doors, one for each wall. She hesitated, unsure which way to go, when she heard noises coming from straight ahead. She opened the door in front of her and froze at the sight. She had expected a small storage room, and instead found herself in a grand room about the size of her community gymnasium. It could probably hold at least 200 people comfortably and must be underneath the width of the pharmacy plus three or four neighboring buildings.

Immediately to her left, a long, curving wooden bar with chromium accents extended the length of the south wall. The back bar was completely mirrored, which made the space feel even larger than it was, and it was covered in arched shelves with glassware of all shapes and sizes and empty bottles lining the wall. The ceiling felt low but elegant crystal chandeliers hung throughout the space and provided a warm light.

Deep, dark wood paneling covered the walls while silk curtains hung as decoration and green palms flourished along the edges. Sconces lit the room, providing just enough light to see but not overexpose it. The lack of windows also gave the feeling of perpetual night, like anything could happen within these walls.

Built-in booths with leather seating lined the sides, along with small cocktail tables and chairs. In the center of it all was a brilliant dance floor with intricate parquet flooring - the wood clearly worn from years of usage. It all led to a modest stage at the opposing wall, with a large piano and bandstands standing stage left, all framed by two large columns. Various paintings seemed to cover the remaining space on the walls, adding to the charm and cozy feeling within. Rio took in every detail in shock and awe. This wasn’t just some dingy basement, this was a swanky dance hall.

How was all of this just sitting under her nose the whole time? Agatha ran an illegal speakeasy?? How did she not know?

The questions piled up in her mind at a rapid rate.

“Didn’t know if you’d have the guts to make it, bunny.” Agatha sauntered out from behind the bar to meet Rio, her hips swinging like the pendulum of a grandfather clock.

“Surprise, my lady.”

Agatha stopped for a moment when she finally took in the full sight of her. Her eyes tracking every detail of Rio’s body.

“Wow, somebody got all dolled up - check you out!” She grinned mischievously and Rio beamed back, arms outstretched.

She did a little twirl, loving the way her new dress fanned out around her, “They say dress to impress.”

“And you certainly have.” Agatha couldn’t seem to stop staring at her legs. Rio normally wore more modest dresses and skirts to work, and this sudden flash of skin made her forget herself.

When her gaze finally crept back up to Rio’s face, she narrowed her eyes, “I think there’s just one thing you forgot.”

Agatha walked back behind the bar, rummaged in a small bag, and returned holding a gold tube of lipstick. “May I?”

“Of course” Rio pushed her lips out in anticipation as Agatha twisted the deep red lipstick until it was just visible.

Then, she reached her right hand and gently touched the young woman’s jaw, holding Rio’s head steady while her left hand slowly applied the colour first to her top lip then along her bottom with equal precision.

Each agonising slow motion sent a rush of adrenaline through Rio’s bloodstream and caused her throat to dry up, making each attempt to swallow almost painful. She didn’t realize she was holding her breath until Agatha pulled away. She had been mesmerized by the quiet concentration in those blue eyes as they stared at her own lips.

“Perfect,” Agatha said as she stepped back and admired her handiwork.

“Here, you can blot it on this handkerchief.” She handed over the white fabric square.

“Thanks for that.” Rio put her lips around the handkerchief, her thoughts abruptly wishing that she was putting her lips somewhere else instead.

What the hell?

“I have so many questions about this place.” She pushed out those intruding feelings and re-focused on her current setting, she didn’t know where to begin.

“I’m sure. But tonight, I just want to show you a good time. You work too hard, Rio. Everybody needs a break once in a while. When’s the last time you had careless fun?”

Rio tried to remember and couldn’t. She thought of her time in America since arriving - anxiety, stress, fear, Tony, the list went on. “Oh wow…I’m a total loser.” She laughed to hide her embarrassment.

“Total loser? I think you’re totally lying.” Agatha swatted her playfully. “You’ve been busy. Life can hold you down sometimes.” She sympathized and touched her shoulder tenderly now.

“Tonight will be a bit of work and play. I’ll show you how we run things, but we can also let loose.”

She nodded, “I can only imagine what goes on down here.”

“Honey, just wait and see. Doors open in an hour, let me show you around before things really get hopping.” She grabbed her hand and led the way.

They walked around the club, and Rio’s neck couldn’t keep up with her eyes, her head swinging this way and that to take it all in. Agatha led them to the imposing bar first.

“The stage might be the main draw, but this is the real star of the show.” She ran her fingers along the bartop delicately, as if it were a jumpy house cat.

It was a brilliant walnut color with intricate carvings beneath the high counter. Rio studied the woodwork and noticed the shapes of birds throughout the paneling. Recessed woodland birds appeared to fly across carved trees on the front of the bar. She leaned down to touch the shape of a large crow with wings outstretched and head cawing up, and she traced along the shapes of a flock of small birds flying across the top of the forest landscape.

Chrome lined the railing and drew the eye immediately, reflecting the chandelier light like subtle stars. The bartop was a lighter color as it had been worn down by faithful customers over the span of decades. The drag of an arm as it reached for a glass, the wear of hands rubbing the wood while waiting for a bartender's attention, the indents of elbows braced down to hold the weight of an incoming mistake.

It was as if she was reading an epic novel just by looking at this singular piece of furniture - the stories were pouring out like the drinks that normally flowed from its recesses.

There seemed to be a key component missing.

“I know it's a bar, so…where’s all the booze?” Rio had scanned the length of it and peered behind the counter, yet she could not see any sign of alcohol.

“You do remember the laws, right?”

Agatha walked behind the bar. “The reason we’ve lasted this long is because we are careful.”

She reached for the mirror at the back wall and it dropped forward slowly to reveal a hidden alcove of deep shelves set into the brick. Large bottles of liquor took up every available space inside. Rio caught the sly smile as Agatha turned around to show off.

“Wow, no kidding.”

Agatha motioned her around to stand next to her and banged twice on a very specific corner of the bar. One of the side panels fell open to uncover even more full bottles that were stacked within the inner structure of the bar itself.

“Let’s just say, we keep things as well-stocked as possible.”

“But, where does it come from?” Rio had to ask the most obvious question.

The sale of liquor had been banned for two years in the states, and the amount of bottles here suggested Agatha must have a decent supplier somehow.

“I have my ways.” Agatha grabbed a bottle of amber liquid and brought it up to show Rio. “Have you ever had a shot before?”

“I’ve only ever tried wine and that was in church.” Rio admitted quietly, feeling shy.

She was nervous and trying to hide it. The thought of drinking felt wrong, bad, scary. Seeing its effects on Tony had put her off the drink permanently in her mind. What if she became angry too? What if it made her mean? What if…she liked it?

“I’m not going to force you, but I hope you’ll try it. This is the best whiskey that money can buy - straight from Kentucky.” Agatha poured two shots into the tiniest glasses Rio had ever seen.

She pushed one over. Rio looked at the little glass curiously and held it lightly with her right hand. Just one couldn’t hurt.

“On three, throw it back quickly. Ready?” Agatha grabbed her own glass and focused on Rio’s eyes. Her stare was intense and Rio felt the room fall away. All she could see was those piercing blues staring her down.

“One”

Rio felt her pulse start to race.

“Two”

She took a quick breath in.

“Three”

They both downed the shots in a single gulp. Rio felt the liquid burn her throat instantly and felt her eyes bulge.

“Ay dios mío!”

She leaned her head back and stared up at the ceiling grabbing her neck. “Are you sure that wasn’t gasoline?” She coughed while trying to laugh.

Agatha scoffed, grabbing her chest in faux upset. “How dare you? This whiskey is the cat’s pajamas! You don’t want to know the trouble it took to secure just this single bottle.”

“Whatever you had to do - it wasn’t worth it.” Rio threw back some sass.

“Well, well, well, it certainly woke you up. What have you done with the timid little bunny I’ve come to know?” Agatha appraised her with glee.

“Ah, can it. That was the worst thing I’ve ever tasted.”

“You get used to it.” Agatha winked. “Come on, let me show you the rest of the place before the crowds get here or before you get properly splifficated.”

She pushed Rio lightly out from behind the bar. “This way.”

They walked back towards the door that Rio came through from the stairs.

“See that light?” She pointed to a triangular wall sconce next to the exit door. It was distinctly different from every other in the space. It was larger, red in hue, and the light pointed down instead of up.

“If Alice spots any trouble coming our way, she flashes it three times on and off. It gives us at least a minute or two to put it into high gear and clear any trace of alcohol as best we can.”

“Does that happen often?” Rio looked at her with worry.

“Thankfully no. Just once or twice in the past year, but nothing came of it. A slap on the wrist is all. It might surprise you to know that I’m very good at talking my way out of a bad situation.”

“No! You?” Rio’s sarcastic streak continued.

Agatha let out her little snort again to Rio’s delight. “Yes, anyway, we also have a few loyal customers who happen to serve the boys in blue and give us the heads up when raids are scheduled.”

“Convenient”

“Very”

She opened the main entry door, and they were back in the landing zone at the bottom of the stairs. She took them into the door to her left.

“This is the coat and corset check.” She motioned to the booth and adjoining closet space which must be under the length of the stairs.

“Corset check?” Rio asked.

“Have you ever tried dancing the Charleston in a corset?” Agatha tilted her head down with a quizzical look. Rio shook her head quickly.

“And on the other wall there are the powder rooms. Nothing fancy but a necessity. Come on.” She pulled her back out to the landing room. They went through the last door on the other wall.

They were now in a dark hallway, only one small ceiling light provided any relief. Rio thought they must be directly behind the bar now.

“This is a spare storage hall and an escape route for bar staff if things go sideways. This place used to be a saloon back in the day and was owned by the Italian mafia. There are at least 5 exits out of the club to the street, and those are just the ones we’ve found. It comes in handy given my line of work now.”

“The mafia? How did you get your hands on this place then?” Rio ran her hands along the bricks of the wall and moved to sit on the many large crates lining the hall.

“I don’t think we have the time for the whole story, but it’s mostly Lilia’s neverending network of connections in this city that secured the space. I was just working upstairs and had a certain knack for pouring drinks that she thought I might be better suited pouring something besides milkshakes and soda pop.

Plus, I had just lost my husband, barely had two pennies to rub together, and was desperate for some cash to keep afloat.”

“I’m sorry - about your husband. I didn’t know you were married.” Rio looked over at Agatha who was looking down at the ground, kicking some dust bunnies along the hardwood.

“Old news at this point. Went to war, didn’t come back. Not much more to report.” She set her jaw as she pushed the memories aside. “Want to see something really amazing?”

Rio felt like there was more to address. She had no idea that Agatha was a widow. Every moment she spent with her felt like turning another page. She hoped she would never reach the end of this story.

“Show the way” She decided against pushing further on the husband story, for now.

Agatha pulled a ring of keys from her pocket. Knocked once and had to use two separate keys to open a door at the end of the hallway.

“Jen, it’s me!” She announced as they entered the backroom.

“Gosh, you frightened me for a second there. I wasn’t expecting any guests.”

Rio took in the striking woman she first saw the other day with Lilia. As opposed to her polished appearance, she was now clad in shabby denim overalls over a white long-sleeve shirt. She had a sturdy headband on to keep the hair from her eyes and was wearing a pair of work gloves.

The room was about the size of two small bedrooms put together but felt even smaller due to the low ceiling. There were two big vents on one wall that must have emptied up to the alley. There was also a stack of suitcases and briefcases stacked in one corner, which Rio recalled Jen carrying on the day she first saw her.

What she noticed first though were the two large copper contraptions that took up the majority of the space. They seemed identical and each was connected to smaller pots by spiraling coils of shining metal. There were large kegs collecting something that dripped from the spouts of the coils.

“Agatha,” Jen said her name like it was a warning, “what is the new girl doing here?”

“We need more help, and her name is Rio.” Agatha said.

Jen sucked her teeth, holding back a retort. She turned to Rio and removed her glove to extend a hand, “Pleasure to meet you officially.”

Rio shook her hand and said, “Likewise, Jen.”

“Since you’re here already, might as well show you what goes on. These are moonshine stills.” She patted one of the copper pots with a soft whack.

“I’m a 5th generation moonshiner. My family has been brewing this recipe for over two hundred years, and it never fails. It will knock you on your ass, but that’s where Agatha comes in with her fancy cocktails to cut the strength. One of the perks of working under a soda fountain loaded with sugary mix-ins, I suppose.”

Agatha added, “Jen’s shine is the best town. Not many clubs would buy from her - the racist bastards - but the first time I tasted a drop of this stuff, I asked her to come work for me.”

“Can I try some?” Rio was intrigued.

“Pump the breaks, hot stuff. If you thought that whisky earlier was strong, this will blow your brains out.” Agatha’s laugh echoed in the small room. “We’ll work up to it, don’t worry.”

“Okay, Mother” She relented with a roll of the eyes.

“Thanks Jen, we’ll let you get back to work. Doors open in about half an hour, are you staying for service tonight?” Agatha asked as she backed towards the door.

“Don’t I always?” Jen put her glove back on and waved. “See you out there, boss.”

The two walked out of the still room into the hallway then through a side door which took them straight back behind the bar.

“This place is a maze!” Rio was losing track of direction with all the doors.

“That’s the point. The harder it is to navigate, the harder time the fuzz will have trying to catch us. I just have one more place to show you, come along.”

They now walked over the large dance floor and towards the stage. Agatha led them up the steps on the right, onto the raised platform, and then backstage. It was dark behind the velvet curtains but Agatha seemed like she could navigate every inch of this club with her eyes closed.

She grabbed Rio’s hand without a second thought. “Watch your step.”

She pulled her into one of two doors back there and flipped a light switch.

“These are the performer dressing rooms. We try to have singers, bands, or dancers every weekend evening. People come for the booze, don’t get me wrong, but they stay for the entertainment.”

“What sort of people come here?” Rio’s imagination drifted to the news stories she had seen in the paper of derelicts, gangsters, and all sorts of unsavory characters that frequented the thousands of speakeasies in town.

“Probably not the sort you’re thinking of.” Agatha caught the surprise on Rio’s face as she seemed to read her mind.

“We cater to a…special crowd, to put it lightly. It’s invite-only, and I take security very seriously. I wanted this to be a place where folks could - “ She paused, searching for the right words.

“Be themselves. People who might not feel safe in most places.” Agatha explored Rio’s face for any hint of understanding.

“Like Jen?” Rio offered innocently, looking towards Agatha for clarity.
