“Yes, that’s part of it.” The boss was contemplating something, but Rio didn’t know what.

She saw her glance at her watch.

“Oh drat, time slipped away from us. I’ve gotta get changed quickly, can you wait out by the bar for me? I’ll be out in a jiffy.”

Rio wandered back out to the main hall and sat on one of the lonely barstools.

Agatha closed the door as Rio walked out. She rifled through the spare gowns she kept in here as backup when she didn’t have time to run home and settled on one of her favorites. A moss-green cotton number, heavily decorated in dazzling glass beads. The beads created a tiered effect across the skirt to mirror the scalloped hem, and a decorated band sat at her natural waistline to draw attention to the center of her body.

She pinned her hair back and added a green jewelled hair comb. As she looked in the mirror to touch up her make-up, she thought about how much more to say to Rio. She didn’t want to scare the poor girl, but something in the way she looked at her, Agatha felt that she wasn’t as innocent as she seemed. She’s going to find out soon anyway. I’ll have to watch her closely.

With a final swipe of her lipstick and a spray of perfume, Agatha walked back out.

Rio heard her coming down from the stage and spun around on the barstool. Whatever she was about to say didn’t come out. She didn’t know if it was the heat of the whisky shot or something else entirely that was making her face feel like she was burning up.

Agatha, normally a bastion of confidence, felt flustered under Rio’s shameless gaze. Does she even know what she’s doing to me? She can’t think that’s a normal way to stare at another woman’s legs, for Christ’s sake. She fanned herself with her hand as best she could.

“Cat got your tongue? You’re not the only one who cleans up nice.”

“You look amazing.” Rio’s voice was low, dangerous.

She’s trying to kill me. Agatha thought. And she doesn't have a clue.

“I know. Now get ready, once the doors open, this place gets crowded very fast. I’ll be behind the bar or mingling with the folks on the floor. Jen will be helping serve drinks to the tables and Alice mans the door. You’ll see Herb who manages security down here and handles anyone who gets too plastered, and Billy’s off tonight so Darcy is running the coat check and helping me pour drinks. Finally, there’s Sharon, the stage manager, who manages all the talent.”

“What do you want me to do?” Rio still wasn’t sure why Agatha had brought her into the fold.

“You proved your skill upstairs, and I need another bartender down here. Eventually.” She rounded the bar and started pulling the bottles out.

“Sit back, kick your dogs up, and just watch Mother work.” Each word hit Rio in the chest with unexpected force.

Rio turned as a stream of people started to flow through the door like a dam had opened. She rubbed her hands together in anticipation.

Here we go.

Chapter End Notes

Ended up combining together two draft chapters into this one, hope you enjoyed!

Happy Holidays :)

Primal night

Chapter Notes

A little change in POV about halfway through this one ;)

See the end of the chapter for more notes

“Hello Suckers!” Agatha’s voice cut through the room without the need for a microphone. “Come on in and leave your wallet at the bar!”

She threw her head back in a delicious cackle as the room erupted in cheers and laughter from the crowd of adoring customers. They clapped, they raised their glasses, and Rio watched every person vie for the attention of their glorious host.

And Agatha lapped it up. It was like watching a dying seedling get its first taste of water after a drought. Rio watched her suck the energy from the crowd and feed on their adoration like it was the most delicious meal on earth, like their love was the medicine she needed to stay alive.

She then scanned the room for the first time and did a double, then triple take. Men adorned in evening gowns, women wearing ties and suit jackets, people off all types wearing wigs and the most beautiful costumes she had ever seen. Up was down, down was up. Her eyes felt like they were going to bounce out of her head, she couldn’t take in all the sights and sounds in front of her.

Where am I?

Rio’s mind was racing. Maybe this was a bad idea.

Should I leave? I should leave, right?

But what would I say? What excuse could I give? Should I say that my boyfriend is waiting for me?

No, no, that sounds like a lie. Maybe, I can say I don’t feel well - that that shot isn’t sitting well in my stomach. Yeah, maybe she would buy that.

Ugh, she might just think I really am a total loser.

No, I can be relaxed. Yup, completely fine with guys in gowns and dames in tuxes. They aren’t doing anything bad, right? It’s just…different.

She locked onto Agatha to ground herself. The big boss was working the room like she owned it - because she did. And god, they love her. She greeted each person with warmth and knowing. Regardless of what they were wearing or who they were with, she didn’t pay it any mind.

“First time?”

A voice brought her out of her fixation, and Rio spun back around to face the bar. “Sorry?”

“I don’t recognise you. Is this your first night at The Hidden Gate ?” The woman pouring drinks leaned close to be heard.

“Yes, I’m Rio.” She took in the beautiful woman with prominent circular glasses on and bright, red lipstick. “I work upstairs with Lilia.”

“Ohhhh, you’re that new girl that Agatha prattled on about. Welcome to the show, I’m Darcy. I can only work a few weekends a month as I’m currently studying political science at NYU, so I wasn’t sure if I was going to get the chance to meet you.”

Rio whistled, impressed, “Why do you work here then with brains like that?”

“It’s her, obviously.” She nodded towards the center of the room and Rio didn’t even have to look to know who she was referring to. “Agatha is magnetic. She makes you feel like you belong, which can be challenging for a lot of us.”

“Us?” Rio furrowed her brow.

Darcy tilted her head and motioned around her, “Look around, doll. You must have noticed. This isn’t your normal bar crowd.”

Rio looked over her shoulder just as the horns of the big band rang out and couples took to the floor to foxtrot. She saw two handsome men in black tuxedos walk together, hold each other, and dance as a pair.

She had heard about these sorts of people before but only in passing.

“Watch where you’re going, you pansy!” Tony yelled out as a slim, young man once accidently bumped him as they walked down the street.

“Tony, was that necessary?” Rio had dropped his hand and questioned.

“Guys like that need to learn a thing or two.” He replied.

She hadn’t known how he had identified the stranger as a “pansy” but she could tell from his tone that it was not a good thing.

She recalled her uncle, Sal, calling one of her cousins a “sissy” when he had pranced around in their auntie’s high heels as a joke to make all the other kids laugh. Her cousin’s face fell as he kicked off the shoes and ran off in anger.

“I’m not having any of those freaks in my house.” Sal had emphasized and all the men grunted in agreement as if they all knew what he meant, and maybe they did. Rio didn’t.

“But…” She started to ask but wasn’t sure what she even wanted to know. “How do they find this place?”

“Agatha has her ways, and word tends to spread pretty quickly. There are pockets of Harlem, Greenwich Village, and spots uptown that attract a group of people who live a lifestyle that’s outside the norm. These folks are just looking to party like everyone else, but it’s less…accepted at your everyday club. So, where do these folks go?” She left it open-ended and Rio filled in the blanks as much as she could.

“Here, Rio,” Darcy said, “You look a bit thirsty.”

She pushed a small glass of bright yellow liquid with a garnish of lemon peel across the counter.

Rio raised the glass to her lips and delighted in the taste. “Wow, this lemonade tastes so unique. It’s so sweet.” She had another large sip.

Darcy laughed and decided to bite her tongue. Every newbie needed a little razzing, “Yeah, lemonade! Let me know when you want another - on the house!”

“Thanks Darcy.” Rio happily drank the glass and enjoyed the music from the talented band and the buzz of the crowd around her.

She had never been to a bar before. It wasn’t allowed in Puerto Rico when she was growing up, and by the time she landed in America, Prohibition was in full swing. Alcohol had never appealed to her, especially not after seeing how it could change someone, and she had never had the desire to seek out the many speakeasies that dotted the city.

A young flapper fell into the barstool next to Rio. “Hey, doll face. What’s a girl like you doing drinking all alone?”

“Oh, I’m not drinking any more booze tonight, and I’m not alone. I’m with Agatha.” She finished off her drink, none the wiser.

“You’re with Mother? How’d you score the High Pillow herself? I’ve been trying for months to catch her eye. She never gives anyone the time of day.” The girl leaned back against the bar and motioned to Darcy who threw up a one second sign as she was busy with a rush of new arrivals.

“I’m not - Agatha and I aren’t -” Rio stuttered her words, feeling a bit light headed.

The girl smiled and flashed her perfectly straight teeth. “Will you do one shot with me? Pretty please.” She pouted her lips.

“Why?” Rio couldn’t tell what this girl wanted from her. She was erratic with a scary beauty but obvious recklessness.

“It’ll loosen you up a bit. You seem tense and that just won’t do here.”

Rio figured she was already out late, in an illegal bar, and surrounded by what appeared to be hundreds of homosexuals. “Fine! Why not?”

Darcy eyed the new girl, “Careful, Florence. This one works upstairs, so she’s property of Mother. You don’t want to go there.”

“Don’t get sore at me! I’m just trying to show her a good time is all. Two shots of Jen’s finest, please.”

The bartender poured two shots of moonshine, and Florence passed one to Rio, careful not to spill a single drop. “Bottoms up!”

They downed the shots and Florence slammed her glass into the bar. “Woooo! I bet that stuff could power a car engine.”

“Am I still alive?” Rio croaked out. She felt like she had swallowed a firework - the burn down her esophagus felt all consuming.

“Get her another lemonade, quick!” She pointed at Rio’s empty glass.

She giggled and passed the refilled glass to Rio before heading off to one of the nearby booths. “Enjoy the night, sweetie.” She blew her a kiss and was gone as quick as she came.

Rio shrugged her shoulders and she watched her walk away, “Thanks, I’ll try.”

As she finished off her second glass in a record time, she placed it on the counter, “Is it getting hot in here, Darcy? I feel like I’m burning up.”

She was having trouble focusing her eyes. All the lights and moving people kept catching her attention, and the sound of music was overwhelming.

“It tends to warm up as the space fills up…are you alright?” Darcy asked, feeling wary. She should probably cut her off now. That amount of liquor in that amount of time was asking for trouble.

Rio stood from the bar suddenly. She faltered on her feet for a second before steadying herself on the stool and proclaiming loudly, “I want to dance!”

She felt a warmth spread across her chest like a hug, her limbs felt restless, her anxiety now overshadowed by the immense desire to move her feet. Agatha told me to wear dancing shoes, after all. The jazz music was flowing through her, and the dance floor called to her irresistibly.

She was up and off before she could even hear Darcy’s panicked voice call out, “Rio, wait!”

She was floating towards the center of the room as if the music was summoning her. The trumpets blared out the melody of an uptempo jazz number that brought the crowd out to Charleston on the floor.

Rio got right in the middle of the action and showed off her moves solo. She was no stranger to the dance, being a frequent guest at the local community dance hall every few weeks with Tony. But, she had never danced alone. He had never let her, always the lead, always spinning her around the room like she was his puppet.

He was a fine dancer, much better than the American boys that Rio saw attempting to swing their partners around. But, he held her a bit too tight and lacked any creativity or flow.

Normally, she would be too self-conscious or worried about what people might say, but tonight, for some reason, she didn't care. As her arms moved in time with the intricate twisting steps and rhythm of the music, she felt the crowd parting in a circle around her.

People were clapping the beat and cheering her on as she cranked up the intensity and the musicians built to a crescendo. Suddenly, there was nobody else near her. She was channeling the music through every movement, and everybody stopped to watch.

The drums felt like a heartbeat, and she hit every beat in perfect time. Her new dress was the perfect dance partner as it swayed and flared with each turn, allowing her legs to kick out and impress the growing crowd.

Her heels twisted and toes turned inwards and outwards as she exaggerated the motions and closed her eyes. She had never felt such freedom before. The pulse of the song wove through her every move like she was feeling every note as a command. There were no sweaty hands to hold, no man leading her in whatever direction he wanted to go. She completely surrendered to her own whims and the direction of the music.

She threw in a small salsa break to the hollers and whistles of onlookers - her hips rolling like waves and her arms painting arcs in the air. The salsa was like home in her body, the moves so familiar and ingrained that she didn’t even need to think. It was the first dance she had learned as a child and one she knew she would love forever.

The crowd was mesmerized by this newcomer. Every man and woman was watching Rio move across the dancefloor with jealous envy, predatory desire, or both. And as the song approached its conclusion, Rio’s vision finally unblurred to sounds of applause, and she caught one pair of eyes completely locked in on her, a familiar pair of blue eyes, and they looked hungry.

Agatha always imagined that death would come for her in a blaze of glory. She would have dreams as a child that she would go out in a gunfight or horse chase or be burned at the stake in front of a crowd. Probably the product of her voracious appetite for adventure books.

She never thought it would come for her in own club. Certainly not in the form of a red-hot, brunette bombshell with moves to rival Fred Astaire or Josephine Baker and the legs of a goddess.

She hadn’t seen Rio leave the bar. Agatha had been schmoozing with a couple of regulars in the popular corner booth near the stage. The dance floor was packed as usual whenever Chick Webb’s band came to play. What was unusual was the circle that was forming around a single dancer.

She rarely paid mind to the dance floor antics, but her curiosity got the better of her.

Agatha excused herself from the conversation to check out what was happening. She had never seen a dance circle in the club. Most of her guests were too absorbed in their own little worlds to take notice of who else was dancing around them. Who could they possibly be watching?

Crowds normally parted when she approached, but this time they were all too busy enraptured with this mystery dancer to see Agatha coming. She gently pushed her way through the layers of people until she arrived at the edge of the circle, and her heart stopped.

She had to put two fingers to her neck to check that she still had a pulse because she swore that her life had ended right then and there. This wasn’t some random stranger - it was Rio. Her eyes were glued to Rio’s body, and she couldn’t even perceive the music that echoed throughout the room.

All she could see was Rio’s legs, Rio’s arms, Rio’s smile, Rio’s knees, Rio’s eyes. Every fluid step, every sway, every kick threatened to consume Agatha, and she welcomed her demise.

What the actual fuck?

That was the only thought that could even fight to exist in Agatha’ mind. Everything else was pushed out by the singular experience of Rio.

She couldn’t even pick her jaw up off the floor and felt like some ridiculous broken nutcracker with her mouth hanging open. It was spellbinding.

She was not used to someone else dominating a space the way she normally did. Everyone’s eyes trained on somebody else - she was a part of the crowd this time.

And then, of course, Rio just had to throw some salsa dancing because she obviously must have wanted to punish Agatha. And if this was punishment, then Agatha was ready to get on her knees and beg for more because it was the most divine ache she had ever experienced. She watched her hips roll, and Agatha forgot how to breathe.

When everyone else was clapping as the song ended, Agatha was a statue.

Clap, god damn it, move your hands.

She tried to will herself to move, but her eyes were engrossed in one thing, and one thing alone. No other part of her body was allowed to function yet. She was ready to devour Rio if given the opportunity but her own limbs refused to move.

Luckily (or unluckily) for her, Rio was the one who bounded over, high on adrenaline.

“I’m so thirsty!” She panted and put her arms behind her head to stretch, unaware of the way people were now staring and appraising her. Every man and woman was sizing her up.

“What have you been drinking?” Agatha leaned in and could smell the heavy scent of booze on Rio’s breath. I’m going to kill Darcy.

“Just lemonade. Oh and some pretty-, uhh, some girl bought me a shot of moonshine.” She was starting to slur her words.

Agatha gritted her teeth. The feeling of jealousy rising at the thought of someone buying Rio a drink. “What girl?”

“Ummmmmmmm…I forget. Fanny? Nooo. Flora? Ummm, let’s ask Darcy, she would know.” Rio skipped over to the bar like a jolly child.

Agatha put her hands on her head and tried not to die of embarrassment. She followed her to the bar in a brisk walk.

“Darcy” Her voice cut like a knife. She crooked her finger and beckoned the bartender with a no-nonsense gaze.

“DARCY! Did you see me dance?” Rio had thrown her top half onto the bartop. “I loveeee dancing.”

“Yes, Agatha?” Darcy arrived and tried not to smile, her eyes flicking to the inebriated form spreading out her arms on the bar.

“Do you want to tell me how this…” She motioned her hand in a spinning circle over Rio, “happened?”

“Well, it started with one drink and then one became two and -”

Agatha cut in sharply, “She wasn’t meant to be drinking at all!”

“Agatha, Agatha, watch this!” Rio jumped up and did a little spin in the air.

“Why is she tanked, Darcy?”

“Sorry boss, she just looked like she could loosen up. Then, Florence bought her a shot of Jen’s stuff and it all went off the rails.”

“You know how strong that is! What else were you giving her?”

“Just some Bee’s Knee’s cocktails. She said they tasted like lemonade.” Darcy shrugged.

“Yeah, lemonade and 80 proof gin!” Agatha slumped onto the stool. This was meant to be a casual introduction to the bar, and now Rio was knee deep in it.

Relax, Agatha. People get drunk every night here, no big deal. Nothing bad’s going to happen.

She felt an arm wrap around her shoulder and a voice whisper in her ear, “Dance with me, mami”

Okay something bad might happen.

And she felt Rio trace her hand down Agatha’s shoulder and along her arm before grasping her hand and pulling her to stand. “Por favor, Agatha. Pleaseeee”

How could I say no?

“One dance, and count your lucky stars. I never normally dance with the customers.”

“You know I’m not just another customer.” Rio piped back and led them to the floor.

The band was playing a gentle, lilting waltz. Couples were spinning around the room in perfect harmony.

“I don’t think you’re in a state to lead.” Agatha held her right hand high awaiting Rio’s.

“I love it when you take control.”

Rio placed her hand and moved her other to Agatha’s shoulder as she caught her boss rolling her eyes.

Their bodies were close. Agatha could feel the excessive warmth of Rio through her dress and bit her lip and closed her eyes for a second to settle her nerves. They were about the same height, but Agatha had on slightly higher heels as she had not expected to dance. So she looked down at Rio who was studying her with glassy, beautiful eyes.

“Try to keep up.”

Agatha used her left hand, which was sitting along Rio’s waist, to guide them through the practiced steps of a casual waltz.

They glided across the dance floor, swaying and rotating in perfect step with each other and the band. Their faces were so close, and Agatha could feel the slightest brush of Rio’s cheek each time they spun.

“You’re so pretty” Rio muttered the words quietly as if she hadn’t meant to speak them aloud, but Agatha could hear every word as if she had shouted it to the room.

“You’re drunk, bunny.” Agatha whispered back, smiling.

“That doesn’t make it less true.” Rio had the audacity to smirk.

“Tell me that in the morning and maybe I’ll believe you,” Agatha responded, “if you even remember this.”

She didn’t want to get her hopes up. It wouldn’t be the first time that a gorgeous woman had whispered sweet nothings in her ear at the club, only to go home to her husband and her normal life, forgetting it ever happened.

“I could never forget you.” Rio hummed along to the tune and showed off a genuine smile. Agatha melted at the sight.

The musicians played the final note of the song, and Agatha let go of Rio to her disappointment.

“I’m starvingggg.” Rio grabbed her stomach comically. “All this dancing - * hiccup* - has worked up my appetite.”

“Dancing, ha! I think it’s your stomach screaming for food to tame the liquor.” Agatha laughed.

She checked her watch, it was just past 1am. “Come on, I know a spot that will taste like heaven to you right now.”

They walked off the dance floor and stopped at the bar quickly. Agatha waved at Darcy, “I’m going to get her something to eat to try to sober her up. Hold down the fort for me, I’ll be back soon.”

She grabbed their coats and all but dragged Rio from the basement club and up the stairs.

“See you Alice!!” Rio waved enthusiastically at the door woman, who waved back and then looked at Agatha’s blushing face.

“Bye, Rio” She held in the laugh and waved at her boss. “Be safe you two!”

And they were out in the world again. The safe bubble of the speakeasy now below them and the cold night hit Agatha quickly. Rio was unphased, stumbling down the alley with a silly grin on her face.

“Where - you - going with me?” She got out her words with some effort.

“You’ll see.” Agatha grabbed her elbow and steadied Rio, leading her out to the main street. They walked a few blocks in comfortable silence. Rio was in her own drunken world, staring up at the sky in wonder.

Agatha pulled her into another back alley, and they approached a line of people, similarly dressed in their best glad rags. Other New Yorkers either just starting their own nights of debauchery or ending them. It didn’t take long and soon they were at the front of the line at a hole-in-the-wall shop.

“Two cheese slices, Frank. And a bottle of cola.” Agatha slid a quarter onto the counter.

“No problem, Mother. What are you doing out so early? Isn’t your place open tonight?” He started serving up the extra large slices of pizza.

“Yeah, just taking care of one of my rookies who had one too many.” She nodded at Rio who was pressed against the glass case, staring at the pizzas on display like they were precious diamonds.

“We’ve all been there!” He passed their slices over. “Don’t be a stranger, Agatha.”

“Thanks, Frank. See you!”

Agatha handed the pizza slice to Rio. “Eat!”

“Feed me.” She begged.

I wish.

“Haha, very funny. Feed yourself.” Agatha took her own slice, lifted it up and attacked it from below as they walked back out to the street.

“MmmMMmmmM.” Rio took her first bite.

Oh god, she’s moaning. Why did I think this was a good idea?

“You like it?” Agatha looked over to see the look of ecstasy on Rio’s face.

“This is incredible. I want to eat this every day for the rest of my life.” Rio was already halfway through her pizza. She was relishing each bite like it was her first.

“Ohhhh, this cheese is unbelieveableeeee. MMMMMMmmmmmmmMMM”

She needs to stop moaning. Right. Now.

“Frank makes the best slice in the neighborhood. Now finish up and drink your soda, I’ve got to get you home.”

Rio’s eyes widened like she had just woken up from a dream. “Oh no. Oh noooo.”

“What? What’s wrong??” Agatha’s mind raced, hoping Rio wasn’t hurt or about to spew.

“I can’t go home like, like, like this. My boyfriend will go nuts if I show up, uh - drunk! What am I going to do?” She quickly finished the pizza in hopes it might sober her up faster.

Agatha stopped walking for a second and took in the look of fear on Rio’s face. The way the joy of the night seemed to drain from her face at the cold sting of reality.

This might be a bad idea but…

“Why don’t you sleep it off at my place? I have a very comfortable couch.” She posed the question before she could think of the consequences.

“You sure? I don’t wanna be uhhh…bother.”

“It’s no bother at all. Alice and even Jen have spent many a night on my couch. I live just around the corner.” She headed toward her apartment.

She couldn’t sense her companion near her and turned around to see Rio fidgeting alone, stuck in place. “Are you coming?”

Rio couldn’t think straight. Between the copious amounts of alcohol flowing through her bloodstream, the huge slice of pizza now weighing down her stomach, and the intoxicatingly confusing feeling of Agatha’s presence, she felt like she was in a washing bucket being cranked around like laundry.

She threw her hands up in defeat, simply unable to think it through coherently.

“Wait for me!” She ran ahead to catch up.

Wherever Agatha would go, she would be sure to follow.

Chapter End Notes

I borrowed Agatha's opening quote from a real woman, Texas Guinan, who was one of the few female speakeasy owners of the 1920's and a huge character.

Thanks for reading!

Darkest hour

Chapter Notes

TW: Domestic Violence

This is the final incident of it in this story.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Rio trailed behind Agatha down the dark street until they approached a large, all-white, seven-story stone building.

“Good evening Ms. Agatha.” A doorman tipped his hat as they approached and held the front door open.

“Evening, Carl. Thank you.” Agatha breezed by and motioned Rio inside.

“Ohhh, so you’re rich rich.”

Rio glanced back at the doorman and marveled at the lobby area of the building. The ceiling was arched throughout and white to match the exterior. Subtle hexagonal black tiles dotted the floor and cozy seating areas occupied the corners of the sizable room. This was another world from the run-down tenements where Rio lived.

“Shhh, lower your voice.” Agatha blushed and kept them moving quickly towards a hallway to the left. She guided Rio with a light touch on her lower back.

“Who else lives here?? Charlie Chaplin? Greta Garbo?” Rio’s eyes were wide at the opulence in front of her.

Agatha pushed the elevator button and stared blankly at Rio, “Really? Do you live under a rock? They wouldn’t be caught dead living in just an apartment.”

“WOW! You have an elevator inside your building?” Rio’s mouth nearly fell open, she thought back to the five flights of stairs she had to climb every single day to get home.

The doors opened and the elevator attendant opened the metal grate. “Good evening, Ms. Harkness and…”

“Rio!” She exclaimed without a care in the world.

“Sorry, Raymond. Excuse her…enthusiasm. It’s been a night.”

“Understood.” He nodded as the elevator kicked into gear. “Floor 3, madam. Have a good one.”

They exited to a large hallway, and Agatha walked immediately to the left to a small set of steps in the corner. She approached the door with a large #4 on the front and unlocked it.

“This way, my tiny dancer.” She motioned for her to enter.

Rio walked up the stairs into a small foyer that opened into a large parlor. The floor was immaculate with dark-stained herringbone hardwood, which matched the tone of the wainscotting that lined every wall and reached halfway up to the ceiling. The upper walls were covered in an elegant white wallpaper with delicate buttercup yellow flowers in geometric patterns.

A large, ornate red oriental rug took up the majority of the space, and a stunning set of light pink velvet armchairs and sofa were arranged in front of a tiled fireplace with an imposing wood mantle. A large radio stood along the far wall by the window that was framed with draping velvet red curtains.

Agatha kept walking into the room and passed through dark french doors into the dining room.

“Keep those legs moving, I’ll give you a spare pair of pajamas from my bedroom.”

From the dining room and through a small archway, they entered a tight hallway. Rio could see the small kitchen at the end, a bathroom on her left and a door to her right, which Agatha opened to reveal what looked to be the sole bedroom.

“Take a seat, let me just find these for you.” She opened one of two closet doors and opened some of the drawers beneath the hanging clothes. There were at least a dozen elegant gowns and several coats and jackets.

Rio sat down gently on the double bed and tried to absorb the details of Agatha’s private space. She felt like she had been let in on a secret and wanted to know everything. The furniture matched the dark wood aesthetic of the rest of the apartment. It all looked well crafted and expensive from Rio’s point of view.

There was a dressing table with a large mirror opposite the bed, and Rio noticed the make up arranged along the top in precise rows. A jewelry box also occupied the table and had a dainty painting of a bouquet on top of it. Warm light emanated from the matching lamps on the bedside tables. Rio flicked her finger along the tassels hanging from the lampshade nearest to her.

“Ah, finally, here they are.” Agatha grabbed something from her drawers and turned around.

Rio jumped up from the bed and took the clothing with a hearty, “Thanks.”

She started to pull her arm out of her dress without thinking, and Agatha rushed over, “Whoa there eager beaver, you can change in the bathroom over there.”

“Oh yeah, one second.” She stumbled across the hall to the bathroom and closed the door clumsily. The room started to spin as she faced the mirror. She tried to look at her reflection but it was like her vision wouldn’t cooperate anymore. The night’s transgressions were finally coming for their revenge.

What’s happening?

Rio’s mind was swirling, and she grabbed the sink to steady her balance. I don’t…feel…good.

She felt her stomach lurch and dropped to her knees in front of the toilet next to her. She vomited and retched as she felt the sting in her throat from the toxic mix of strong liquor and stomach bile.

“Rio, are you okay?” Agatha knocked on the door and opened before Rio could respond. “Oh my gosh.”

Her eyes widened as she took in the hunched figure on her bathroom floor. She moved immediately to kneel next to her and grabbed a towel to help wipe her mouth.

“It’s okay, honey.” She rubbed her back gently. “It will pass.”

“Have I been poisoned?” She heaved again, and Agatha stood quickly and ran to the kitchen. She returned with a glass of water.

“Here, drink this. It will help.”

Rio downed the glass and slumped onto the floor. “Let me die here.”

“Hush now, you’ll be fine. Come on, let’s get you up. You just need to sleep it off.” Agatha reached for Rio’s arm and helped lift her to standing, despite Rio’s groans.

She walked her to the living room and sat her down on the couch. She left to go grab a pillow and some spare blankets, and Rio was all but passed out when she returned.

“Rio?” She whispered.

“Hmmm?” Rio sleepily responded but didn’t open her eyes.

“Are you alright?”

“Better now that you’re here.” Rio’s words were barely a whisper.

Agatha’s lips curved up and she helped lay her down gently on the couch and tucked her in with a blanket. She hoped she would be warm enough since she hadn’t even changed into the pajamas, but at this point, she wasn’t going to strip her down.

In my dreams . She smiled at the thought and looked at the sleeping figure in her home.

What am I going to do with you?

Rio was already in a deep sleep, the alcohol acting like a dose of morphine that quickly knocked her out. Agatha stared at her for a moment and took in the gentle demeanor of her sleeping face. She was trying to reconcile the Rio she knew from the pharmacy - diligent, reserved, with a hint of bite to her humor, and the Rio who emerged with some coaxing from a bit of giggle water - fiery, sarcastic, uninhibited.

Alcohol tends to enhance characteristics that lie dormant in a person, so Agatha pondered how the two sides of Rio worked together. A puzzle for another day. She thought while yawning. The clock above the fireplace read 2:45 am - time to turn in.

The morning sun hit Rio in the face like a cold splash of water.

“Huh?” She sat up and looked around. This isn’t my room. Wait, this isn’t my house…

She threw back the blankets and looked down. She was still wearing the dress from last night, and as she went to stand she flopped back down on the couch.

Arrrghhh, why does my head feel like it’s full of cement??

The pounding in her head reminded her of the booming bass drum from last night. Dancing, twirling, Agatha’s eyes on her, Agatha’s arms around her.

She grasped her temples and tried to soothe the tension. Her mouth tasted something awful, yet even in the misery of her current state, she remembered the joy and freedom she had felt for the first time in a long time.

“Good morning, sunshine.”

Agatha entered the parlor wearing a two-piece silk pajama set and a black quilted coolie coat with intricate green and purple floral designs on the front and back.

“How do you look so chipper?” Rio rubbed her eyes and smeared the makeup that still sat on them. She groaned as she looked down on the black mess on her hands.

“I’m an early riser, and I know how to hold my booze.” Agatha replied. She placed a glass of water and two aspirin in front of Rio. “Here, this might help.”

“Thanks,” Rio took the pills and fell back against the couch. “What time is it?”

“Just after 8am. So you really haven’t slept long.”

“8am! Oh no, I need to get back now.” Rio rose and faltered on her feet.

Agatha grabbed her elbow to keep from keeling over. “I don’t know if that’s such a good idea. I hate to say it, but you look worse for wear.”

“No, my boyfriend is probably going crazy wondering where I am. I may have failed to mention where I was going last night.”

Rio walked to the bathroom briskly and started to wash her face as best as she could. She hoped that Tony was still sleeping and had also had a late night last night. Maybe he wouldn’t have even noticed.

“Do you need to borrow a dress? I probably have a spare that would fit.” Agatha offered.

“No, it’s okay. You’ve done so much for me already. I just need to get going. Thanks for the night, it was amazing. Really. You’re amazing.”

“I’m sorry.” Agatha leaned against the bathroom door.

“For what?” Rio wiped her face with a towel and rinsed her mouth out with water.

“I should have kept a closer eye on you. I shouldn’t have let Darcy give you those drinks, none of this would have happened.” She stared at the floor, unable to look Rio in the eye.

“Don’t start with those horsefeathers. I don’t regret a single second.” Rio stood next to her boss and placed a hand on her shoulder. “Well, I could have done without the vomit, but everything else…”

Agatha laughed, “Go on then. Will I see you at the shop on Monday?”

“Unless this headache bumps me off!” Rio grabbed her purse, shrugged on her coat, and exited the apartment. When she reached the street, she had to get her bearings, she wasn’t really sure where she was or how she got here.

She started walking west for a while until she reached an intersection and saw a familiar corner store and realised she was just around the corner from work. She set off quickly back to her apartment and made it back in record time.

As she climbed the steps, she heard the yelling by the time she reached the second floor.

Oh no.

She steeled herself as she trekked towards the rising aggression.

“Where the fuck is she, Claudia?” Rio heard his voice as she unlocked the front door. “She ain’t here.”

She walked in and saw Tony pacing in the kitchen and Claudia seated in the dining room. Miguel must have gone to work a weekend shift. They both turned as the door opened.

“Look, there she is. Now you can finally calm down.” Claudia gestured to Rio.

“Calm down? Don’t start that. How could I be calm when mi novia is out all night and comes strolling in dressed like some…some streetwalker?!”

Rio’s head was still banging. She closed her eyes to try to transport herself back to the quiet of Agatha’s apartment. The warm feeling of her presence and space enveloping her in protection.

“RIO! Where were you?” Tony stomped over to her and grabbed her bag and threw it to the ground.

“Tony, give me a second.” She took a moment and opened her eyes to see the man she once loved so dangerously close that she took a small step back.

“I’ve been waiting all morning. I woke up, and you weren’t there. No note, no nothing, so I think I’m due an explanation.” His breath was shaggy, his frustration pouring out.

“I…I went out with…” All of her lies were getting tangled. He still didn’t even know she had a job. She couldn’t say she was with her boss.

“She was out with Dorothy and Marie from downstairs. They asked me and Rio if we wanted to go to a new ballroom in the Bronx, but I wasn’t feeling well yesterday, so I pushed Rio to go alone.” Claudia cut in trying to cut the tension.

“Yeah, I just went out dancing. And then one of the other girls we were with got really sick. I went to her apartment in Harlem to take care of her because everyone else had to leave. And I certainly have enough experience caring for a drunk.” Rio moved to step around him towards the living room.

He caught her around the upper arm and dug his nails in hard.

“Ow, Tony! What are you doing?”

“You’re lying.”

He increased the pressure and saw the look of fear flash across her face. “Where did you get that dress? I’ve never seen it before.”

Claudia moved to stand and pushed the dining chair back. “Let her go!”

“Are you using my money to buy frivolous shit for yourself? I’m slaving away every single day, busting my balls to earn money for us, and you waste it to look like a common tramp!” He pulled her close, hand still firmly wrapped around her arm.

He took a deep inhale through his nose. “Have you been drinking, too? Are you fucking kidding?”

“No! I swear.” Tears started to pour from Rio’s eyes. Her stomach churned from both hunger and sickness, and she tried hard to remain present despite the haziness in her brain.

“STOP LYING! You think I don’t know the scent of hooch on someone’s breath?” He spun her and pushed her body with his full strength. All his anger exploded into a final thrust.

Rio remembered reading about Amelia Earhart a few years ago in the paper and being so taken by the idea of a woman aviator. The thought that humans could really fly through the sky was mind boggling. She would imagine what it felt like to soar through the clouds and leave the Earth behind. It must feel so freeing, so heavenly.

She didn’t think the first time that she flew, it would be in her own living room, propelled by the enraged hands of her partner.

Her body hurled through the air with a sickening grace, arms and legs shockingly still. It was like her limbs hadn’t caught up to what was happening. Her left arm cracked on the corner of their wooden coffee table and her face collided with the solid oak arm of their sofa. It was such a small space that contact was inevitable.

“Rio!” Claudia ran towards her in a flash - the sound of the dining chair falling behind her.

Tony stared at the scene like he hadn't just caused it. His eyes were wide and crazed, still pumping with anger. As Rio failed to move, the weight of his action finally dropped on him.

“Rio?” He sputtered, voice shaky, lungs heaving.

She hadn’t lost consciousness, but the pain was pushing her to the very limit. She tried to spin her body but her arm wasn’t working properly, and she tasted blood in her mouth. She must have bit down on her lip at the collision. Her headache was now a full migraine, a relentless pressure expanding from within her skull. She tried opening her eyes and saw Tony make a small move towards her.

“Get out of here, you nonstop sociopath! Leave us, cabrón!” Claudia screamed at him, her throat raw as she tried to tend to the moaning figure on the ground.

He exited with nothing but the sound of a slamming door, and they could hear the heavy steps pounding down the stairwell.

Rio thought of the way Agatha had rubbed her back when she was on the bathroom floor last night. How she had soothed her softly, the feel of her hands, the scent of her perfume. It brought her momentary comfort.

“Rio, doll. Can I get you onto the couch?” Claudia softly spoke to her.

“Yeah, I think so.” She eased her legs up slowly. Luckily they seemed mostly unharmed, her arm seemed to take most of the impact. It was already swollen, and she clenched her teeth as she eased onto the sofa.

“Oh no, your face.” Claudia reached out and traced her cheek with a whisper of her fingers. Rio could feel her cheek and eye radiating warmth.

“I never thought I’d regret the wood-framed furniture…until now.”

Claudia swatted her shoulder, “How could you joke at a time like this?” She sniffled and wiped her tears on the back of her sleeve. She pulled out a handkerchief and wiped the tears and blood from Rio’s face also.

“Sorry for dragging you into this, Clauds. You didn’t need to see this.” Rio started. “I…shouldn’t have lied to him, I shouldn’t have gone out last night.”

“No, don’t blame yourself. Never blame yourself for this. He is responsible and that’s that. You don’t deserve to be a punching bag to some man who gets sore the second you have an independent thought.” She fretted over Rio’s arm, unsure how to help.

“Let me see if any of the neighbors have ice in their icebox. I think we need to put something on this. It’s not looking so hot. Wait here.” She stood and ran out the door.

Rio leaned her head back and regretted the motion. Her head was an all-consuming cacophony of pain. She tried to lift her left arm, but immediately yelped as she saw her fingers tremble and felt the flare of ache shoot through her.

In less than 5 minutes, Claudia swung the door open holding a dish towel wrapped around ice. “Here, hold this to your arm.” She handed it over.

The relief was welcome but only dulled the pain. Rio hissed when it made contact with her skin.

“I think I need to take you to the doctor. That arm looks bad, Rio.”

“No! What would I tell them?” Rio always hated the doctor. She hated feeling poked and prodded, and they never listened to what she had to say. She didn’t want to deal with the way they would pretend to care when she explained what happened. “I’ll rest today, and I’m sure it’ll be fine by this evening.”

“I don’t know…” Claudia nervously eyed the injury but didn’t want to push. “If it’s not better by tomorrow, we’re going, okay?”

“Fine.” Rio nodded. “Thank you, amiga. I mean it, I don’t know what I would have done if you hadn’t been here.”

“Don’t mention it.” Claudia turned on the radio and flipped through a magazine that had fallen on the floor. They sat in silence and listened to the weekend programming to zone out. Soon, Rio’s eyes drooped and the tiredness from the past 24 hours finally settled her.

She woke up a few hours later in a daze to the smell of soup cooking on the stove.

“Hungry for lunch?” I’m just heating up some Campbell’s chicken noodle.” Claudia called over her shoulder.

“Starving.” Rio tried to pipe up, though her voice felt a bit rough and still burned from last night. She wasn’t sure when she had fallen asleep again. The entire morning had been a shit show. The angle of the shadows in the room told her it was mid-day, lunch time.

She stood and shuffled to the dining table and sat down.

“Ay bendito, your eye!” Claudia’s eyes went wide when she approached with the two bowls of soup. She saw the burgeoning, extensive purple bruise that had made a home across Rio’s left eye and cheek.

“How bad?” Rio winced at the thought.

“I don’t know how you’re going to go out for a while.” Claudia passed a bowl over and started tucking in to her own.

Rio lowered her head to the table next to her bowl. “How am I going to go to work like this?”

“No way, you can’t!” She scoffed at the idea, pointing her spoon in Rio’s direction.

“You’re going to have to take tomorrow off at minimum. They’re going to ask a lot of questions that I don’t think you want to answer.”

Rio sighed and raised her head again as her stomach rumbled. She ate the soup slowly while trying to think of yet another lie to explain this latest drama

“Sooooo….” Claudia stared down into her bowl like she was trying to read tea leaves. “What are we going to do when that man of yours comes back?”

Rio raised her bowl with her good arm and drank the last of her soup. She hadn’t realized how hungry she was and remembered with a smile that her last meal was that incredible slice of pizza at 1am.

“I don’t know…” She looked down at the angry swelling on her arm and tears formed in her eyes. How did I let this happen again?

“I’ve got a friend at work - she lives in a women’s boarding house. They might have a spare room..” Claudia approached the topic carefully.

“But - I came to America to be with Tony. I can’t just - I can’t just leave him. I don't have anyone else.” Rio felt the tears fall and watched them splash in the remnants of the bowl.

“Rio.” Claudia stared at her with soft eyes. She reached over and took her hand. “He’s not safe.”

“If I hadn’t -”

Claudia jumped in to cut her off, “No, don’t do that.”

“But, I shouldn’t ha-” She tried again, desperate. She wiped her running nose and went to wipe her tears then winced at the pain on the side of her face.

“It doesn’t matter what you lied about. He threw you across the room like it was nothing, like you were nothing. Nobody deserves that.”

Rio tenderly stroked her swollen arm, deep in thought. “I have some money that I’ve stashed away, but it’s not nearly enough to support myself.”

“I can loan you some. Whatever you need to secure a place, I know you’ll pay me back.”

“I couldn’t take your dough. I’ll ask the boss if I can work nights or more shifts.” Rio thought back to Agatha’s offer to help in the club. If her apartment was anything to go by, the money from the speakeasy was better than good.

“Offer stands anyway. You know I’m here for you.” She clasped her hand and then rose to wash the dishes. Rio nodded and passed over her bowl.

She went to lay down in bed and take another nap. It felt like she was deep in sleep debt and was trying to make up the deficit. As she drifted in and out of dreams, she would recall bits and pieces of her night out with Agatha.

The way she had looked at her when she was dancing. Oh gosh, that look. She felt herself flush but wasn’t sure if that was from the memory or the heat of the swelling. She thought of Agatha’s warm apartment - impeccably decorated and effortlessly put together just like her. How she had welcomed her in like she was an old friend. How she had cared for her when she had no obligation to. It made Rio’s insides feel soft and she smiled to herself.

I need to make it up to her somehow .

She must have drifted off again because when she woke up it was dark. The bed was empty next to her, thankfully. Tony must have found somewhere else to go for the night. She pulled the blankets up and felt at peace enough to go back to sleep again.

In the morning, she woke to shooting pain in her arm. At first she thought she had just slept on it and made it numb, but she looked down at the dark blue coloring now splotching across the surface of her forearm and cringed. She entered the bathroom off the living room and almost jumped at the sight of her reflection.

The red swelling on her face had given birth to a similar color scheme to her arm. The purple and blue painted a canvas of pain across her cheek, under and over her eye, and down her jaw. She looked like she had been walloped by a champion boxer or barrelled over by a Model T.

She heard Claudia outside the bathroom, “How are you doing, Rio? I’ve got to head off to work, are you alright?”

She knew if she opened the door that Claudia would take one look at her face and force her to go to the doctor, so she turned on the bath faucet and called out, “I’m okay! I feel better than yesterday anyway. I’m not going to work, don’t worry. I’ll see you when you get back tonight!”

“You sure?”

Rio could feel Claudia debating whether to open the door or not. There was a long pause.

“Yes, claro que sí. Go on before you’re late.” She kept her voice calm and even. Then heard her roommate walk out the door, and she was alone.

She lowered herself into the bath and relished in the water. It was a welcome reprieve from the pain, but she worried about what to do about work.

I can’t go to the shop like this, they’ll never understand. What would Lilia say? What would Agatha think? Should I call to tell them I’m not coming?

Wait, I don’t know the shop phone number!

I’m sure it's fine, they’ll probably think I’m sick or something. Agatha was there when I threw up. She felt embarrassed at the thought but figured it was a valid excuse.

I’ll go tomorrow and clear it up.

Today, I need to figure out what to do next.

Chapter End Notes

Happy New Year! I'm very grateful for this wonderful TV show that brought me back to fanfiction and writing.

I really appreciate the support from all you readers, thank you!

Familiar by thy side

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

After Rio had left her home, Agatha made herself some toast and slathered on a bit of Lilia’s homemade raspberry jam. She flipped through the paper carelessly skimming the daily news.

Officials seize liquors worth $50,000 on board James Shewan’s yacht in Miami

Yanks lose first contest to the Cards, despite Babe Ruth’s home run

Woman kills her husband, who had beaten her, after drinking bout; Construction superintendent shot with his own pistol. Woman held for murder. Where the dead man got his whisky “Not pertinent” Detective Captain says.

Pastor denounces dancing; Dr. Bailey fixes 10:30pm as the limit for young folks’ parties

“Oh, now you come out?” She mused and lifted her eyes from the paper.

A small black cat stepped into the dining room and leaped onto the dining table. Its brilliant yellow eyes were trained on the leftover crust on the plate.

“Where were you hiding, kitty? How come you didn’t want to meet mama’s new friend?” She scratched the cat’s head playfully.

“Were you under the bed?” Agatha picked up her cat, Ebony, and stroked her in her lap, enjoying the comfort of her beloved pet.

“You missed out. Rio is…” What is Rio? Or more importantly, what is Rio to me?

She contemplated her connection to this woman who brought out something new in Agatha. There had been others, sure. Other women who caught her eye from behind the bar or on her nights out at other joints around town. Even one or two that had made their way back to this very apartment for something more.

She was no spring chicken in this department, but Rio was different.

“Rio is special.” She settled on the descriptor though it lacked the magic she hoped to convey.

The way she struggled to breathe around her, and how she lived indefinitely in her thoughts was different. She had loved her husband but it had been a love of obligation. As she stroked Ebony, her mind wandered back in time.

When she was young, there were no other options. Back home in Boston, there was no other road to take. So Ralph had been fine, good even. A nice, gentle young man who had pursued her endlessly at church. Her mother had approved, pushed her to be with him and that was that. It was an escape from the far-reaching grasp of her mother’s home, and she thought she could imagine a life with him.

They were married before she even turned 20, just before the turn of the century, and a few years later they moved to New York as Ralph got a job constructing what would become the subway. He worked long hours, which left Agatha to her own devices to explore her new city. For all that she felt she lacked in love for her husband, she felt in spades for the hustle and bustle of the urban metropolis that surrounded her.

She loved Ralph like she loved fresh laundry or a home-cooked meal. It was pleasing, nice, familiar. But the streets of New York were passionate, dangerous, unpredictable. It fed the part of her soul that yearned for more. The escape from her miserable childhood and monotonous everyday life.

They had tried for children, as was expected, but nature’s cruelty afflicted them and no child was to be. The doctor’s couldn’t pinpoint a reason, just a callous, “sometimes it doesn’t happen.”

Lilia had been another saving grace. The pharmacy attendant who saw her every other week and spoke to her with kindness and interest. When she offered a job to Agatha in 1909, she jumped at the chance - a new distraction from her mundane home life. And she was good at it, exceptional really. She found that she could charm even the most ornery customer with a wink and grin, could manipulate cruel men with her gaze, could conjure delicious creations from any ingredients.

And so her life went. She built a community at the pharmacy and had a friendly circle with her neighbors and the wives of Ralph’s coworkers. She was content and enjoyed nights out at the dance hall, catching shows on Broadway, and indulging in restaurants in Manhattan. It wasn’t electrifying or dramatic, but it was stable and agreeable.

Everything was fine until President Wilson declared war on Germany and threw the US into the Great War in 1917. Agatha thought it wouldn’t affect her, Ralph was already 38 by this point and the draft age topped out at 30. She watched the young men around her disappear quickly, the city losing its vitality with every draft card that went out. Then, a year later, the age range expanded to 45. By the end of the summer of 1918, he was shipped off across the sea to aid the Allied forces.

“We regret to inform you that your husband, Private Ralph Boehner, died on September 21, 1918 of pneumonia complications from the influenza pandemic.”

Roughly half of the US soldiers who served in Europe died from the flu, not from combat, and when Agatha received the blunt telegram outlining Ralph’s death, she was both grateful that he did not die in agony and maddened that it all could have been avoided if he hadn’t been drafted in the first place. She was alone; she was free.

Three months later Congress would ratify the 18th amendment, prohibiting the production, transportation, and sale of alcohol, and her life would change once more. Lilia had been cleaning up the basement space for years, so when she proposed they revitalise it into a fully operational bar and club, Agatha saw it as the perfect distraction and opportunity. They spent a year renovating the space with the help of a handy team of neighborhood kids like Billy who had nothing better to do and retired pharmacy customers who would do anything Agatha asked just to spend more time with her.

When the hammer fell in January 1920 and Prohibition went into full effect, The Hidden Gate was open and waiting for the thirsty customers who needed their fix, and Agatha was behind the bar, ready to give it to them.

Looking down at Ebony’s purring face, she wished for a second that she could experience the pure empty bliss of her cat’s life instead of the complicated web of her own.

She set the cat on the floor and walked to the kitchen to clean up her breakfast. She walked into the living room and folded up the blanket from the couch. She could smell the subtle hint of Rio’s perfume still lingering on the fabric, spicy-sweet with notes of bergamot and soft floral bouquets. She lifted the blanket up to her nose and inhaled deeply.

It reminded her of their waltz together on the dance floor and the close proximity they shared. The feel of Rio’s body so close, her face just a slight turn away. She hoped Rio still remembered the good moments they had and not just the sickness and inevitable hangover.

After taking care of the house, she headed out to run a few errands before another night at the bar. When she arrived at 9pm and descended the stairs, she heard Jen already hard at work in the back room. She walked over and entered the room.

“Well, hello there stranger. Where did you disappear to last night?” Jen asked as she poured the buckets of corn into the mash pot.

Agatha’s lips twitched but she held back the smile, “Oh you know, just looking out for my fabulous staff.”

Jen laughed loudly, “Ha! Yeah, it seemed like you were very intently looking after one employee in particular.”

“Careful, Jen.” Agatha warned and watched her turn on the boiler to heat the pot.

“I call it like I see it, boss.” She raised her hands to the sky. “You’re dizzy with that dame, aren’t you?”

“I’m hot. Is it hot in here?” Agatha grabbed the collar of her dress and pulled to try to get some air.

“Don’t try to claw your way out of this one, come on tell me everything.” Jen cranked the heat as the water boiled, and she stirred the corn mash mixture.

“What? Rio interests me, that’s all. She’s interesting!” Agatha fanned herself, unsure if it was the heat of the room or the heat from thoughts of Rio.

“Yeah, I’m interesting but you don’t look at me like I’m a slice of fresh, decadent cheesecake. Like you want to eat me and lick up every single crumb with your tongue.”

Agatha blushed a deep red at that, “Oh my god! Jen!”

“I don’t judge! Given the proclivities of our customers, how could I? But, be careful with Rio, Agatha. She’s got a boyfriend from what I hear from Lilia, and I don’t know if she’s part of ‘the scene’, you know?” She flicked off the flame and started cooling down the product before adding in the malted barley.

The temperature in the room finally started to drop and Agatha welcomed the change. “I haven’t even done anything yet!”

Jen looked at Agatha with a no-bullshit glance. “Mother, we all saw you two traipsing around the hall yesterday. You two were waltzing like you had been dance partners for decades. That wasn’t just an innocent pair of acquaintances. You looked happy, really happy. You both did.”

Agatha flashed all her teeth in a wide and contagious smile, her eyes crinkling, “Really, you think?”

“You’d have to blind to miss the fireworks sparking when you look at each other, it’s almost sickening.” Jen finished stirring the mix and added the yeast. She got up to get the fermentation barrel and started readying the mixture for its next stage.

“Alright, alright. I’ll let you finish here. I’ve got to get the front set up anyway.” Agatha made for the exit, eager to escape the heat, both from the room and her nosy friend.

“Is Rio coming tonight?” Jen asked before she could leave.

“You didn’t hear? Darcy was slipping her cocktails all night, and she even did a shot of your special elixir! So she was well corked. I’d be shocked if she could even get up this morning.” She decided to keep it close to the chest that Rio had stayed at her place last night.

“Hot damn! Hope she’s alright, poor doll. What a first night. Guess I won’t have to worry about accidently walking in on you two necking in some back room tonight then.”

“You’re evil.” Agatha muttered before walking out finally.

“You love it!” Jen called behind her.

The club opened at the usual time and the guests arrived looking for their hit of booze and good times. Agatha worked the bar and kept the drinks coming quick and strong. A local jazz quartet with an up-and-coming star trumpeter was scheduled to go on at midnight.

“I heard that I missed out on quite the show last night.” Billy rounded the bar and donned his apron.

Agatha barely paused from shaking the cocktail in her hand, “And where did you hear that?”

“Everyone’s talking about it! People keep coming up to me and asking if I know who the mystery dancer is. A brunette, new, total knockout, legs for days, queen of the dance floor.”

Billy looked to the boss for answers and saw her avert her eyes and grin. “Agatha?” He asked cautiously. “Who was it?”

“Well - you know how I invited Rio to the club last night…” She shrugged bashfully.

“No way!”

“Blame Darcy. She had the grand idea to pour her one too many cocktails, and how was I meant to know that Rio was a dancing dynamo once she got a bit of liquid courage?”

“I can’t believe I missed it!” Billy pounded his fist on the bartop.

Agatha finished off the drink she was making when two regulars sat down at the bar. “Hey Dottie, Hi Beth. What can I get you two?

Dottie leaned onto the bar, “You can get me the phone number of that lady dancer from yesterday!”

Agatha tried to keep her face neutral, “Couldn’t tell you, doll.”

“Don’t play coy with me! I saw you dance with her, and everyone knows that Mother never dances with no one.” Dottie wagged a finger.

Agatha bit her tongue but relented slightly, “Nobody has ever stopped the entire dance floor with their moves before. How could I resist?”

“What’s her name? At least give us that.”

“Sorry, my lips are sealed. I’m sure she’ll be back another night, ask her yourself.” Agatha turned around to grab another bottle of booze.

“You’re no fun! Well, I’m patient. I’ll be first in line to shake a leg with her the next time she shows her face here.” Dottie got up and pulled her friend away.

Billy looked up from concentrating on his task, “See, I told you. She is the talk of the town.”

Agatha groaned. Of course, the one woman who finally held her attention was also the hottest commodity uptown. It was still early in the night, she braced for the incoming questions and tried to tap down her growing jealousy.

“Mother, what’s the low down on that dancer?”

“Agatha! You must tell me where to find that brunette flapper. I’ll show her a night out that she won’t soon forget.”

“Is she single?”

“She’s one of us, right? Would she give me a shout?”

“Mother, mother! Can you give my phone number to that new girl? Pleaseeeee.”

She was reminded of Rio on her first day manning the soda fountain alone, but there was nobody coming to save her. The questions and pestering continued up until last call when Agatha finally shooed the stragglers back up the stairs.

“I can’t wait to ask Rio about this tomorrow.” Billy was brimming with excitement. “She’s famous!”

The next day at 10am, Agatha finally rolled into the pharmacy. She walked in from the back and hung up her coat and bag. She opened the door to the main shop and looked around expectantly. She saw Lilia at the register near the front door and Billy was prepping the soda fountain.

“Lilia, where’s Rio?” Her heels clicked as she crossed the floor in her confident stride.

“No show. Very unlike her.” Lilia replied.

Agatha furrowed her brow, “Did she call or send a telegram?”

“Nothing. You didn’t scare her off, did you? She was a great worker.”

Agatha thought back and remembered how sick she was, “She wasn’t feeling too good after her night out. Maybe she is still under the weather.”

“Hope the poor dear is okay.”

“Do you have her number? I can give her a ring on the blower.” Agatha was trying not to sound too eager.

“She never gave us one. Not sure her address either. I only know she lives in Washington Heights with her boyfriend. Emphasis on the word boyfriend.” Lilia eyed her boss carefully.

“I know. Can’t I worry about my employee? I just wanted to check on her.” Agatha tapped her fingers on the counter while deep in thought, but short of knocking on every door in the neighborhood (which was crazy, right?), she would just have to wait.

Lilia shook her head, “Be careful. I’ll let you know if she shows up.”

Agatha waved to Billy and went out back to the club. They were closed Mondays and Tuesdays to give the staff a break and to allow Jen time to prep and make enough moonshine. They supplemented their homebrew with a network of suppliers from Lilia’s contacts. Whiskey flowed up from the South, while rum poured in from the North. Despite the laws, the people demanded their liquor and there were still plenty of ways to get it.

Supply chains were constantly under threat, so they had to be on high alert and ready to change suppliers on a dime. In times of dire need, their designation as a pharmacy allowed them to exploit a handy loophole and get an exemption for medical-grade whiskey, but the taste was something awful.

The mob controlled most of the smuggling into and out of the city, so Agatha had to be extra careful about who she trusted. Most speakeasy owners were men, specifically men of a certain upper class who catered to the wealthy of Gotham, so she was also at a disadvantage there. While the police might look the other way for the aristocrats and high rollers, they wouldn’t hesitate to bust and arrest a single woman and her loyal gang of degenerate homosexuals.

She helped Jen prepare the latest batch to get her mind off Rio, but the worry was growing with every minute. She hoped that Rio wasn’t mad at her, that she hadn’t scared her off like Lilia had suggested. Hopefully it was just a lingering hangover and not something worse like rot gut or alcohol poisoning.

She didn’t have that much, did she? No, it was just a few drinks. She hadn’t been drunk before. She’ll sleep it off. She’ll be back as good as new tomorrow. Calm down!

“I don’t think I’ve ever seen you this quiet…ever?” Jen looked at Agatha with a curious gaze.

“Huh?” She turned, snapped out of her anxiety spiral.

“Wow, something has got your all turned about. I’ve known you for how many years? And you’ve never been so flummoxed. I think you should go home before you hurt yourself or more importantly, the alcohol. This process isn’t forgiving for the distracted.”

Agatha paused and realized she hadn’t been paying much attention. “Yeah, maybe you’re right.”

Jen gasped, “Now I know something is off. You would never admit that I’m right about anything!”

“Very funny, Jen. I think I’m just distracted. I’ll see you tomorrow.” She shook her head and took off. She grabbed her coat from the shop and peeked in quickly as they were busy with customers. No sign of Rio still.

It’s fine. She’s fine. She tried to reassure herself and headed home to relax.

Rio was restless at home all day. Where she used to be perfectly happy at home, now she felt bored and useless. She busied herself with chores as best she could but her bum arm burned when she tried to use it. She tried reading some of the forgotten novels that she had purchased months ago but her mind drifted to the pharmacy. What were they doing now? How was Billy handling things? Did they miss her? How was Agatha?

Her anxiety jumped every time she heard someone climbing the stairs in the building. Tony still hadn’t come home, and she knew it was only a matter of time. He was meant to be at work today also but all his clothes were here.

The sun started to set and the front door opened. Miguel and Claudia walked in together and greeted Rio, who was laying on the couch.

“Evening, Rio - oh my gosh!” Claudia dropped her bag straight on the floor and scrambled to kneel next to the couch. She reached out to swipe Rio’s hair from her face.

“Rio…this looks bad. How’s your arm?” She slowly pulled away the blanket covering her and gasped, covering her mouth.

She turned quickly to Miguel, “Papi, go next door and get a pail of ice from the Rivera’s. Ándale!”

He took off out the door and Rio started, “Claudia, it’s okay. Don’t fuss over me.”

“No, Rio, this isn’t just some scratch…”

“I know.” She flopped her head back on the throw pillow she had been laying on.

Miguel flew through the door holding the bucket of ice. He passed it to Claudia and tried not to stare at the broken figure before him.

“Gracias,” She said. “Now go get the stuff you’re meant to.” She nodded to Rio’s room.

“What stuff?” Rio questioned, trying to sit up straight but Claudia’s hand stopped her.

“He spoke with his friend Melvin, who works at the docks. Tony needs some clothes and his wallet. He’s staying with a friend for a few days, so Miguel said he could grab whatever he needed.”

Rio sighed in relief. At least she wouldn’t have to face that demon tonight.

“You need to go to the doctor tomorrow. No fighting me on this, I’m serious.” Claudia looked at her with stern glare.

“Okay, I will.” Rio relented. “Thanks, Claudia. Even if you’re a pain in the ass sometimes.”

“Just for you.” She laughed. “Put this ice on your arm, and go to bed!”

The next morning Rio was up with the sun and got dressed quickly before her roommates woke up. She was out the door by 6:30am to avoid any further questioning and prying. She walked the familiar pathway to the pharmacy.

Rio needed a doctor but didn’t know where to go. She hadn’t been to see one since moving to this country and figured Lilia would know what to do. She knew several doctors swung by the shop to pick up various medicines, surely one of them was trustworthy and affordable.

The door was locked when she tried it. Glancing at her watch it was still 30 minutes until opening at 7:30am, but Lilia normally got in early. She put her hands on the glass and looked into the dark store. She knocked and saw a head of grey curls pop around from the back room. Lilia walked over and unlocked the door.

“We’re closed, come back in -” Her next words were cut off as she took in the sight of Rio. Her eyes swept over the bruises that splattered her face and Rio could hear her sharp intake of breath.

“Rio.” Her voice betrayed her shock. “What happened?” She put an arm around her and shuffled her inside and shut the door.

“It was an accident. I think it looks worse than it is.” Rio was quiet as Lilia put both hands on the sides of her jaw and inspected her face. Her quiet gaze made Rio rock on her heels uncomfortably.

“Why are you here?” She hurried behind the counter to the tinctures and pulled out a small jar from the cabinet.

“I need to see a doctor, but I don’t know any. I thought - I thought you might know one.” She watched Lilia pull over one of the counter stools and gesture for her to sit. She sat down and glanced at the jar labeled “arnica treatment” in Lilia’s hands.

“Yes, I can take you to my own doctor. He is usually free in the morning. Just sit still for a second.” She applied a bit of the arnica to Rio’s face. “This will help reduce the bruising.”

“What will I tell the doctor exactly?” Lilia capped the jar and gave her knowing look to Rio, trying to broach the topic with ease.

“I fell down the stairs.” Rio said softly, her voice tinged with tears.

“And did these stairs have two fists?”

“No, it wasn’t like that.” She tried to hide the panic. “It was - It was a mistake.”

“Rio -” She started, “this is a fiction you told yourself and tell yourself still. Is this the first time?”

Rio remembered the slap, the very thing that drove her to this job. She shook her head.

“Are you hurt anywhere else?” Lilia looked her up and down, searching for clues.

“My arm.”

“Can I see?”

Rio painfully removed her coat and lifted her arm with effort. Lilia’s eyes widened, and she touched the bruising carefully, taking in the damage with her perceptive look.

“This isn’t good. Have you put any salves or ointments on it?”

“Just some ice.”

“Let’s go.” She helped Rio back into her coat and grabbed her own purse, then locked the door. She walked at a brisk pace, and Rio had to hustle to keep up.

They made it a few blocks then stopped outside a brick building with a health symbol on the door. Inside was a small waiting room with just a few chairs. There was nobody else seated. Lilia took a chair by the office door and Rio sat next to her. The office door opened and a tall, bald man wearing a head mirror and white coat walked out.

“Dr. Yensin” Lilia stood to greet him.

“Lilia? I wasn’t expecting you today. Was I?” He shook her hand.

“No, thankfully not this time. I have a friend, Rio, who needs some help.” She gestured to Rio, then whispered “Some domestic discord.”

He nodded and waved Rio to come into his office. She took a seat on the large leather chair in the center of the room. He sat on a small stool nearby. Lilia waited outside.

“Hello, Rio. Nice to meet you. How can I help?” He asked attentively. His kind eyes assessed her face with interest.

“I fell on my arm and face, and my arm is still extremely painful.”

“Let’s have a look.”

She showed him the injury, and he gently examined the arm. He rotated it slowly and tested her pain. He had her bend and move it in various ways, while writing down his observations in a small notebook.

“It doesn’t appear broken, but the bone is damaged. It is sprained. I’m going to put it in a splint to help it heal, so your arm will be immobile for at least two weeks.”

Rio huffed, How am I going to keep up at work with just one arm?

She sat still while the doctor fitted wooden splints along her forearm and wrapped it in bandages and cloth strips to keep it steady.

“Try to keep it elevated while at rest, and come back in a week so that I can check on it. Okay?”

She nodded.

“Okay, I’m sure Lilia can give you something for any pain you have. She is a magician with herbal medicine. And I’ll see you soon.”

Back at the pharmacy, Agatha was pacing again. She had arrived early expecting Lilia as usual but found the shop locked and the lights out. Luckily, she had her spare key in her bag. She saw that the register drawer was open and empty and one of the stools was out of place, so someone had been here this morning.

She got to work stocking some of the shelves until she heard the ding of the front door. She turned and her heart stopped.

Rio.

She couldn’t see anything else. Her vision zoomed into one thing alone - the bruised and battered face coming through the door.

“What - What the hell?” She tore across the room like a tornado.

Her hands grabbed Rio’s shoulders for refuge, her eyes scouring every broken capillary, noting every swollen patch of skin.

Purple was always her favorite color, but seeing it dye the beautiful tanned skin on Rio’s face, she wanted to hurl or scream or both. Rio could hardly look her in the eye, the blank expression broke her heart even further.

She snapped at Lilia when Rio failed to respond, “How did this happen? Who is responsible?” Her tone exuded venom mixed with fear.

“Agatha, don’t forget yourself.” Lilia moved further inside and pulled Agatha away from clutching Rio. “Come with me. Rio, take a seat at the counter. We’ll just be a moment.”

She led them to the back room and closed the door. “She doesn’t need a mother right now. Don’t look at her like a broken baby bird.”

Agatha couldn’t stop walking circles around the small room. “I just saw her the other night, Lilia. She was okay and now she walks in looking like - like that - and I…what…” She ran her hands through her long hair that was down today.

“She hasn’t told me, but I can guess.” Lilia offered.

“Is she in trouble?”

“Trouble in the home, from the looks of things.”

“I’ll kill him.” Agatha all but growled. Her anger was a volcano on the verge of eruption. “I swear to god, if I see that man…”

“Steady there, killer. I know I have a lot of sway with the fuzz, but I think a murder charge might be pushing it.” Lilia put a hand on her shoulder to stop her pacing.

“That’s not just a little slap. Look at her face!” She gestured wildly in exasperation. She was having trouble breathing normally or focusing on anything but the pain Rio must have felt. “She looks like she took on an entire gang and lost.” Agatha felt her voice start to tremble.

“I took her to the doc. He’s going to take care of her. There’s not much more we can do, you know the police don’t give two shits about ‘family problems.’”

Agatha sighed, feeling helpless. “Do you still have a spare bedroom?”

“Yes, my sister moved in with her husband three months ago.”

“Please, can you offer it to her? You know I would ask her to stay with me but I only have the one bed. Please.” She tried not to sound as desperate as she felt. She kneaded her hands to keep the tension at bay.

Lilia contemplated the request and saw the distress on her boss’ face. Agatha never asked for help, even when she was drowning in stress. She was fiercely independent to a fault.

“I’ll offer it, but I have a feeling Rio is as stubborn as you.”

“Thank you. Truly, thank you.” She felt her panic start to subside but the anger remained in her veins. She vowed to make this man pay, whatever the cost.

As Lilia reached for the door handle, Agatha spoke flatly, “Do you still have contact with Wanda?”

The older woman froze, “Agatha, no.”

“Just where I can find her. I’ll do the rest, you don’t have to be involved.”

Lilia turned slowly. “Are you sure you want to go down this road?”

They stood in silence, a quiet duel before Agatha spoke up, “Please.”

“It’s been a few years, but last I heard you could find her in Hell’s Kitchen. They own a hall across from Pier 88 - that’s all I know.”

Agatha nodded and Lilia lingered for a moment as if she were about to say more but decided against it.

She stayed seated for a moment at the table in the back and eavesdropped on the conversation out front. She heard Rio decline the offer to stay at Lilia’s (of course) with an excuse that she was fine, that she could handle it, that she just wanted to work.

Agatha rested her head down on the table. She kept seeing Rio’s broken face in her mind every time she closed her eyes. She needed to get the image from her brain. She needed to protect her.

Rio was trapped in a twisted spell by a raging man, now Agatha just needed to figure out how to break her out of it.

Chapter End Notes

The newspaper quotes from the beginning are direct quotes from a single New York Times issue in March 1922. It was so interesting to see the real stories of the time.

After seeing several comments about Tony, I've decided to take the story for a slight detour down the darker side of the Prohibition time.
