She knew it was near work, but all the buildings blended together. She could remember the lobby well but the exterior was a mystery besides its stark white coloring.

Her right arm ached from the weight of her suitcase as she rounded another block. Surely, she should have passed the building by now. She looked left and right down the tree-lined street, everything was unfamiliar. Finally, she turned the corner on the next block and saw the stone building that seemed right. She approached slowly, trying to think of what to say to the doorman to let her in.

Oh hi, remember me? I was that sloppy drunk girl from the other night who showed up with Agatha. Can you let me in to see her?

She shook her head and contemplated going back. She turned and started walking away, but she didn’t have a dollar to her name. She couldn’t even afford a night at a dodgy motel, so she turned around again and summoned her courage.

“Excuse me?” She approached the man standing outside the building.

“Yes, ma’am?” He nodded with a friendly smile.

“I am here to see my friend. I think she lives in this building. Agatha, Agatha Harkness?”

“Is she expecting you?”

“Well…” She hesitated. “I was just in the neighborhood and wanted to drop by.”

He glanced down at her suitcase and her discolored face, “Let me give her a ring, one moment.” He entered the lobby and used the telephone on the wall. After a few agonizing minutes, Rio saw him coming back out.

“She’ll be down in no time, please sit inside.” He held the door open for her and gestured her in.

It looked like an upscale hotel, not just some apartment building. There were fresh flowers in several vases on the wooden display table along the wall. It was so far away from the life she knew.

The elevator dinged, and she heard the metal grate open and frenzied steps echoing toward her.

“Rio!”

“Sure.” Rio fired back as they made their way to the dining room and she heard Agatha’s charming snort behind her. She sat at the rounded wooden table and admired the crown molding and intricate ceiling medallion that held the imposing circular alabaster pendant light.

She looked towards Agatha and wiped her face with the thick (probably very expensive) napkin on the table.

Rio leaned back in the dining chair and let her arms fall to her side, sighing. “I don’t know where to start. I had dreamed of America for so long and what it would be like, what I would be like here, and none of it was true. Everything that he promised me was a lie.”

Agatha sat quietly, her elbow on the table, holding her head up as she stared at the woman across from her.

“Tony was my first boyfriend, first love. Sounds so ridiculous now to say it, but I thought we were going to be together forever. He cared for me so deeply. When we were younger, we would daydream about leaving the island and starting our life in Nueva York - a place where anything could happen. He would tell me how he was going to buy us a place in Brooklyn, how we would get to see the greatest jazz singers in the world, how he would take me to a Yankees game. I was naive.”

I watched so many women in my life capitulate to hot-tempered men, and I always promised myself I would pick better. Yet, here I am.”

Agatha looked down at her table and replied “It happens to the best of us. I’ve worked the bar for two years now, and the stories I hear would make your skin crawl. “Ralph? Ended up being the pandemic that got him anyway.”

Lilia was the only one in the shop when Rio arrived on Wednesday morning for her shift. She was stacking a new shipment of lotions as she walked in.

“Morning, Lilia.”

The woman looked up and smiled at the new arrival, “You look happy this morning. Love the hair. Have a good sleep?”

“You could say that. I stayed with Agatha last night.” Rio grinned and played with her new locks.

“Oh really?” Lilia hoped Agatha knew what she was doing.

“I mean, she let me stay over. I packed my bags and left Tony. The last straw broke when I got home yesterday, and I didn’t know where else to go so I ended up at Agatha’s.”

“Well you know you can stay with me, right? I still have a spare bedroom in my apartment. Rent will be very affordable as I have a nice arrangement with the building owner.”

“That would be great. Let me think about it. I don’t want you to get sick of me!”

“If you start picking up shifts downstairs, I probably won’t even see you very often to be honest. Plus I’m easy to live with. I’ll hardly bother you.” Lilia finished opening the boxes and started sorting the merchandise.

“Okay, sounds amazing. I’ll let you know.” Rio started to help sort the goods and the two fell into easy conversation.

“Rioooo!” He sang her name and held the note with attempted vibrato. The two women rolled their eyes in unison.

“You never told me you could dance.” He shot back with a smile.

“Who didn’t? The entire club was buzzing with gossip on Sunday night. You’re the talk of the town! Everyone is lining up to cut a rug with you.” His excitement was overwhelming, and the thought that hundreds of people knew about her was frightening.

“How am I meant to show my face there again, especially with this hideous bruise?” She rubbed her face with anxiety.

“Umm, if you walk in with this new hairdo and move like you did last weekend, you’re going to be just fine. You’re gonna need a personal bodyguard to keep all your fans off you. Let me know if you’re hiring.” He laughed at the mental image.

He saw her retreating into herself, “Hey, seriously. Agatha can help with face powder and rouge. She’s even shown me how to use them before.”

Rio curled an eyebrow with interest and Billy defended his statement, “What? Can’t a man look pretty sometimes?”

She laughed and got back to work. It was challenging to move about lunch service one armed, but she managed okay and was grateful she could still write the orders with her uninjured hand. She did her best to ignore the stares from customers on her face and splint.

When pressed, she would throw out an “I’m so clumsy!” or “You should see the other guy” to cut the tension and ease the questioning. The look of relief on their sincere faces was always immediate as if the threat of the truth was just too much to handle.

By quitting time, Rio was ready for a break. She was cleaning the counters when Agatha walked in.

“Hey Rio, are you up for a shift at the club tonight? I’m sure Billy would love the help with service - I need to help Jen with production.”

She was feeling tired already but desperately needed the cash, “Yup, of course. What time?”

“Come by at 10pm. Pay is double what you make up here plus the tips are generous. No need to dress to the nines this time, just a nice dress and shoes you can stand in.”

“See you at 10.” Rio gave a quick nod then walked to the back room and motioned for Agatha to follow. As the door closed, she said, “Lilia offered me her spare bedroom again, and I think I’m going to take it. If you don’t mind…”

“No stress, I want you to do whatever you think is best. And I only have one room, it’s not - practical.” Agatha was glad that Lilia was so generous, though a part (a very large part) wished that Rio would stay.

“Can I stay tonight? I’ll gather my stuff tomorrow. If I’m working tonight, I’d rather have a familiar place to sleep."

“Yup, not a problem. Here’s my spare key, you can head to the apartment now to rest and get ready. I’ll see you later.”

Rio thanked her and left. Lilia walked into the back room before the door could even swing shut.

“Did she tell you about staying with me?” She asked.

“Thank you for offering it again.” Agatha nodded.

“It’ll be nice to have company. Did she really show up at your place last night?”

“Yeah, she was a wreck. This guy has done a real number on her. I can’t wait until he gets what's coming.”

“So I take it you went to see Wanda then?” Agatha could sense the disapproval in Lilia’s question.

“Don’t worry ya pretty grey hairs. I can take her.”

“I’m sure you can, but those two never work for free. What are they getting from this?” Lilia crossed her arms.

“Just booze. Four barrels, four bottles. That’s it.”

“It’s never that simple. Wanda’s on a power trip to gain control of the city, why wouldn’t she ask for something more?”

Agatha shrugged in an exaggerated fashion with her arms. “How should I know what goes on in that redhead’s sick mind?”

Wanda and Vision commanded the Sokovian gang that controlled Midtown Manhattan. As opposed to gambling and bootlegging, they specialized in the political machine to gather power and exert control, though they ran a network of speakeasies and clubs to bring in the cash. They paled in comparison to the Five Families and Irish Mob in scope and size, but Vision ran his operation with exacting direction and authority.

However, Wanda was the real master behind the curtain. Though she fronted as just another mob wife, or moll, all direction came from or through her. Vision may appear as the mob boss, but Wanda was the actual puppet master.

Agatha had first encountered the couple only a year ago. She and Jen had visited a new bar, the Cabinet of Mysteries, to meet up with a new contact that Lilia had arranged. A bootlegger from Minnesota that had a fleet of delivery vans rigged up to smuggle copious amounts of whiskey from Canada.

They had only been sitting at the table with him for 15 minutes when rough hands had grabbed both Jen and Agatha, hauled them into the building's kitchen, and tied them to some chairs in the enclosed pantry.

“We don’t tolerate these sorts of meetings on our premises.” A woman’s voice rang out behind them as they were facing the wall of produce.

“We didn’t mean to offend, ma’am.” Jen uttered, glancing sideways at her companion, who was seething.

“You don’t just get to tie us up like pigs, toots.” Agatha snapped.

“You’ll find I can do pretty much whatever I want, dear. This is my house.” The redhead rounded the chairs and stood tapping her foot in front of them, arms crossed. Agatha could feel two large figures looming behind them as well - extra muscle.

“Oh, nice to finally meet you, Glamour. I see how you got your nickname.” Agatha took in the appearance of the redhead. She had heard rumors around town about her and her husband for months now. They were intimidating all the club owners, marking their territory. Her perfectly styled scarlet locks, the jewelled headband, the black beaded chiffon evening dress. She was picture perfect, stunning.

“Nice to see Mother outside her hen house as well. Now, tell me. Why you were attempting to woo one of our best suppliers from right under our nose?”

“This is a free country, isn’t it? I didn’t know you had a chokehold on every bootlegger in town.” Agatha couldn't conceal her temper.

“Just this side of Manhattan. If you stay up in Harlem, we won’t have any problems, see?” Wanda stepped closer to Agatha and fiddled with her hair. Agatha strained against the ties on her wrists and ankles.

“I don’t appreciate being played with like a toy, Wanda.”

“We’re sorry. Really. If you let us go, we’ll go back uptown. This was just a big misunderstanding.” Jen tried her best to talk some sense into the situation. There was some game going on between her boss and this new woman that she couldn’t quite understand.

“Is that right, Agatha? Just a misunderstanding?” Wanda ran her finger along Agatha’s jaw and held her by the chin - not with malice but hard enough to make her point.

Agatha stared her down, unwilling to budge, but she felt the fear in Jen and didn’t want to drag this out. “Yes.” She spoke the word as if it pained her to do so.

“Yes…and?” Wanda was testing her. She had let go of her face and was now leaning against the shelving, staring her down.

“What the fuck do you want from me?” Agatha knew the Sokovians craved power and loathed competition, but this felt personal.

“I want you to say you’re sorry, like your good little friend here.” The condescension poured out of Wanda’s mouth so easily.

“I’m not.” Agatha didn’t break her gaze with the woman in front of her. She wasn’t going to let her win.

“Pietro, Carl, untie Jen, and let her go. Leave the two of us. I need to have a private word with this one.” She watched her men lift Jen and take her away, then it was silent as the door shut them in.

“You want to have your way with me now, buttercup?” Agatha quipped with a laugh.

Wanda was caught off guard for just a moment. “Wh-what? No, I..you’re pretty bold for someone tied to a chair.”

“Some call me charming.” Agatha pushed out her lips in a delicious pout. She felt like Wanda was trying to exercise control to prove a point.

“I’m sure. Now just tell me you’re sorry for trying to snake my bootlegger, and we’ll let bygones be bygones. You can go back to your place and forget you ever messed with the Maximoffs.”

“And if I don’t?”

Wanda walked to the corner of the pantry space and knelt down to the bottom shelf. She pulled up a heavy metal device with a hand crank. She took the chair Jen was sitting on and affixed the twisting clamp to the seat. Agatha now realised it was a meat grinder. Her heart stopped.

“Hey!” She tried in vain to pull against the restraints. “I was just razzing. I thought we were playing!” She couldn’t keep the quiver of genuine fear from emerging in her voice. Her eyes kept flicking between the grinder and the redhead.

She watched Wanda kneel and test the crank. She heard the metal gears turning slowly.

“Glamour…Wanda, please. I’m sorry, okay. I’m sorry! We didn’t know this was your club, I promise.”

“Oh, now you’re sorry. Interesting.” Wanda lifted the chair with its new sinister upgrade and placed it right next to Agatha.

“Please, hon. Please. What do you want? I’ll do anything. I-I need my hands. Don’t-” She was desperate now. The cold hard stare from her captor was scaring her.

Wanda slowly untied one of Agatha’s bound wrists and held it with surprising strength. She guided it to the meat grinder and held it at the top of the hopper.

“Tell me that I won.” Wanda started turning the crank again.

Agatha bared her teeth like an angry pitbull. “You won.” She snarled.

Wanda’s grip on her wrist did not ease. She started moving it down towards the chewing metal of the grinder.

“YOU WON!” Her voice strained and filled the small room.

The grinder halted. Wanda let Agatha’s hand fall back to her side, a wicked smile covering her face as she glanced down at the sweating, frightened woman below her. She paused and soaked in the feeling of control.

She leaned close to Agatha’s face, “This isn’t a game. This city’s at war, and you’re not ready. Either stay in your cute little lane or tough up, buttercup. And if you ever need a hand from us, it’s going to cost you.”

Agatha walked away from her first real run in with a gang in shock. She vowed to never let it happen again.

Since then, she built up the wall around her operations and herself. She made inroads with the fuzz to keep them off her back. She hired Alice for protection after seeing her take on three men in a bar brawl. Her and Lilia kept their suppliers happy and loyal, they kept their customers coming back for more, and they carefully avoided the power struggle between the warring gangs in New York.

She wasn’t interested in power, not like Wanda. She wanted power in the form of money, independence, freedom. She wanted to carve out a niche for people like her to feel safe and welcome. It wasn’t about domination.

“How are we going to make up for that lost supply of alcohol?” Lilia snapped her fingers and pulled Agatha from her memory.

“Yeah, umm, I’m going to help Jen tonight make a double batch. But we might need to see if the Lee brothers have any extra bottles from their last run. I don’t know if we’ll make it to Friday night.”

Lilia sighed heavily, “I’ll make some calls. This better be worth it.”

Rio walked the short journey to Agatha’s apartment and let herself in with the spare key. It felt familiar coming into the space now, and she felt a tug of sadness that this was her last night here.

She shed her work outfit and threw on her house dress to relax. Alone in Agatha’s domain, she wandered the space with curiosity. In the parlor, she studied the painting above the fireplace. A dark and moody landscape on a cloudy evening. She recognised the scene from Macbeth, when he meets the three witches who announce that he will be king.

Her eyes swept along to the bookcase near the windows, and she ran her finger along the spines of novels - several by Jules Verne, Edith Wharton, Arthur Conan Doyle. She was impressed by the range and the collection. There were a few small framed photographs on top of the shelf. One of Agatha on her wedding day with who she assumed must be Ralph. One of Ralph in his military garb, looking stoically at the camera. One of the younger Agatha and Lilia outside the front of the pharmacy together.

She smiled at the memories and wished she could hear the stories behind each photo. Undoubtedly, Agatha would have endless tales to regale about each one. She shuffled over to the radio and turned it on. Al Jolson’s April Showers flowed from the speakers a fitting number as spring was quickly approaching in the city.

“Though April showers may come your way,

They bring the flowers that bloom in May…”

She swayed softly to his crooning voice and relaxed on the couch to just listen to the music. Her eyes closed as the music washed over her, and she drifted off for a quick nap. When she woke up a few hours later, little Ebony was curled along her side.

“Hi there” She whispered and petted the cat carefully, trying not to wake her. “Thanks for keeping me company, little one.”

The clock read 8:45pm. “Gotta get ready, sorry sleepyhead.” She eased up and walked to the bedroom. Going through her suitcase, she only had two dancing dresses, and she had already worn one on her first night at the club.

She looked towards Agatha’s closets. Hmmm, would she mind if I borrow one? I doubt they would even look good on me. Maybe just a look. She opened the door on the right and took in the numerous colored gowns on hangers. Wow .

She rifled through the dresses and stopped on a gold number with an open back and oval neckline. There was a prominent bow along the waist and multiple points on the bottom hem. She turned to the door as Ebony strolled in, “What do you think?” She held up the gorgeous gown. “Do I dare?”

The cat meowed.

“I’ll take that as a yes.” Rio laughed to herself and tried on the dress. She wasn’t expecting it to fit perfectly but it slid against her body like it was made for her. She looked in the dressing table mirror and admired the view.

She had decided to forgo her step-in slip and opted for a brassiere and bloomers instead. Her new hair was easy to style. She just used a bit of gel to add subtle finger waves around her face, then applied a light amount of eyeliner and lipstick, hoping Agatha would assist with covering the bruise before the night began.

“Do you think your mama will like this?” She showed off her look to the cat who was stretched out on the bed.

Ebony glanced her way with her yellow eyes before shutting them once more, giving away nothing. Rio rolled her eyes. Why am I talking to a feline?

She spritzed herself with her signature scent L’heure Bleue that her cousin had gifted her as a goodbye present and decided to head out early. “Bye kitty!” She called as she walked out the door.

It was dark now and had to be at least past 9pm. She knocked twice on the door and Alice greeted her warmly.

“Hey Rio, welcome back. Didn’t know if we’d see you again after that first night.”

“I think I learned my lesson about booze. I’ll take it much easier from now on.” She held the bannister and made her way down the stairs.

“Love the haircut by the way! Very stylish.” Alice called down after her.

Rio walked through the club door and saw Billy behind the bar chopping limes.

“Ummmm…stop everything. Who’s that stunning vision that just walked in?” Billy dropped his knife and his jaw as he took in Rio’s outfit.

“Close your mouth, kid. Are you sure it looks alright?”

“Are you kidding? Agatha’s going to go goofy when she sees you. I would kill to pull off a dress like that.” He admired all the details in the gown.

“Where is our fine boss this evening?” Rio tried to change the subject.

“She just walked backstage to go grab something.”

“I’ll go see where she wants me.” Rio walked across the hall.

Probably horizontal, Billy thought to himself and held in a laugh.

She walked up the stage stairs and behind the curtain. It was dark backstage, but she was easily able to see the glow of light under the door to the first green room. Without thinking, she opened the door and caught Agatha in a state of undress.

Her boss was in a white corselette, which helped obliterate her curves to fit the silhouette of the day, over a light yellow silk chemise. The light waist girdle had two garter clips on each leg to keep up her sheer stockings. She was already in her heels, and the sight of the whole getup made Rio’s mouth run dry. She fumbled to close the door.

“Sorry! I should have knocked!” She tried to back out of the room and moved to cover her eyes.

“Come in, it’s fine. I was just worried it was Billy for a second.” Agatha waved her in and felt her heart jump into her throat. She took in the sight of her own dress now draped around Rio’s body. The gold dress was one of her old favorites, but it was a touch too snug. It seemed to fit Rio’s form like it was tailored for her figure, even the wooden splint on her arm couldn’t detract from her beauty. She held back from fanning herself.

“I can come back.” Rio muttered as she tried to hide her flushed cheeks.

“Since you clearly have good taste in fashion. Help me pick a dress, I’m at a loss!”

She took in a deep breath and walked back into the room. She tried to keep her attention on the clothing but couldn’t resist the temptation standing beside her. Agatha was like the forbidden fruit, and Rio was fighting the urge to grab a bite. She let her eyes slide down the exposed legs on display and admired the supple skin of Agatha’s thighs, the curve of her knee, the muscles in her calf.

The boss flicked a glance at Rio and saw the way her eyes were travelling down her body. She caught the way her tongue subtly licked her lips. Maybe I’m not the only one feeling a bit frustrated. She considered the thought.

“Sorry I didn’t ask about borrowing your dress. I just…didn’t have anything nice to wear.” Rio apologised.

“Keep it, honestly. I usually always just wear something from here anyway. Speaking of, which one would you pick for me?”

“What about this one?” Rio had composed herself and held up a sky blue Grecian-style dress.

“It’s been a while. Can you button me in?” Agatha stepped into the number. It had a stylish draped cape back, and she moved her hair to the side to allow Rio to help close the clasp at the top.

Rio steadied her hands and affixed the dress easily. She could feel the warmth of Agatha’s skin on the tips of her fingers but quickly pulled away.

“Wow, that dress looks incredible on you.”

“Honey, everything looks good on me.” Agatha twirled in a flourish and sat in front of the brightly lit mirror to tie up her hair.

“So, should I just shadow Billy tonight?” Rio asked.

“If that’s alright. If you feel too tired at any point, you can head home. Otherwise, we close at 3am.” Agatha started applying her makeup.

“I actually want to ask…could you help me cover this bruise? I’m tired of the questions, it makes me feel stupid.” She dropped her head.

Agatha twisted in her chair and lifted Rio’s chin, “Don’t talk about my friend like that. She doesn’t deserve it.”

Rio smiled bashfully. “Why are you so nice to me?”

“I told you - you deserve it. Now come sit, I think there is some great face powder back here that the performers use.” She shuffled through the dressing table drawers and found a large round container.

“It’s not magic but will probably cover it enough.” She applied the powder as gently as possible.

Rio watched the blue bruise slowly disappear. She could still see the shadow of the painful memory, but it was good enough to fool the average passerby.

“Thanks, I feel like a new woman. You’ve really given me a total makeover - face, hair, clothing. How can I repay you?”

“I’m sure I’ll think of something.” Agatha said with a smile. “I was curious, what was your old address?”

“What? Why?” Rio got nervous at the thought.

“No, nothing bad. I was just going to have Alice check in and make sure Tony is still going to work, not planning anything suspicious against you.”

“Like what?”

“You’d be surprised what a freshly dumped, drunk man is capable of.”

Rio thought it was over. She hadn’t considered that Tony might do anything further. She had planned to never see or speak to the man again. “Uh, it's apartment 25, 370 Fort Washington Blvd.”

“Don’t worry. I just like to make sure my people are protected.” Agatha put a hand at the small of Rio’s back and led her out. She catalogued the address in her head for later.

They strolled back out to the main hall, and Rio went to help Billy with the prep while Agatha disappeared into the back to help Jen.

“Can you prepare the garnishes? Or would you rather clean the glasses?” Billy asked.

“I can do the garnishes. My good hand still works.” Rio took the paring knife from him and kept slicing the citrus.

“Mother did a good job with the powder. You can hardly tell anymore.” He said as he started pulling the liquor from the hidden cabinets.

“Yeah, I’m so grateful for her help, for everything she’s done for me.”

“Get in line. I would probably be caught up in a gang or dead if she hadn’t brought me into her fold. Tommy and I were living in a boy’s home. Our parents abandoned us at birth - I guess two babies was just too much to ask. Anyway, we ran away at 13 and were sleeping on the street. We stole food to stay alive and one day, I tried stealing from the pharmacy.

She took me into the back and asked where I was staying, where my family was. She set us up with a family she knew, the Kaplans, and they’ve taken both Tommy and I in. They’re like our parents now. She hired me, let’s me work down here, and I can save money to go to college like Darcy. I owe Agatha everything.”

The more she learned about her boss, the more she was surprised. Agatha was endlessly interesting. She was like an intricate tapestry woven from the finest thread, complex and beautiful.

The two of them finished the prep as they heard the loud cascade of people descending into the club. The bar was quickly surrounded with thirsty patrons, vying for attention.

Rio watched Billy handle the never-ending line without difficulty. She would pass him limes, olives, mint, straws, glasses - anything he asked for, and take note of the steps to prepare each request. Gin rickey, sidecar, martini, Mary Pickford, old fashioned, highball. It was like a whole new language she needed to learn.

As the crowd moved from the bar to the dance floor, she tried to keep the area clean and tidy. As she was washing a few glasses, she heard someone tapping on the bar behind her. She turned and saw a platinum blonde sitting on one of the stools. She was casually tapping her nails on the bartop, a subtle and suggestive invitation, and her eyes glinted at Rio.

“The mystery dancer returns. I see you’re not too busy, can I steal you for a little twirl?” The woman was straight to the point. Rio admired her winged eyeliner and perfectly curled hair.

“And who is asking?” Rio was now facing her, intrigued at the boldness of the request.

“Friends call me Dottie, but you can call me whatever you want, doll.”

She wasn’t used to such shameless flirtation, especially not from a woman. Men had asked her to dance many times in the past, but Tony was always around, always quick to shut them down. She felt unsettled but couldn’t say she disliked the exchange.

“Do you use that line on all the bartenders?” She decided to join the game. A little flirting never hurt nobody.

“They could be so lucky. I saw your moves the other night. I bet you can keep up with that pace off the floor as well.” Dottie was clearly enjoying herself. She reached out across the bar and touched the splint on Rio’s arm. “Will this slow you down?”

Rio heard the challenge in the question. She knew she was being played but couldn’t let this woman question her abilities. “Billy, I’ll be right back.”

Her fellow bartender overheard the whole conversation. He was giddy at the prospect of finally seeing Rio dance. It was all he had heard about for days now. He wondered if she could possibly live up to the hype.

Rio stepped out from behind the bar. She was stone cold sober this time, but dancing was a part of her DNA. The band tonight was rocking - an eight-piece jazz band with a full repertoire of the latest hits. She walked with a purpose to the dance floor, confident Dottie was trailing behind her. She could feel the blonde’s eyes raking across her body as she led the way. The other customers took notice of her as well as they recognised her from her previous turn on the floor.

The band finished the foxtrot rhythm and immediately picked up a hot jazz number. The drummer hammered out the beat with impressive speed as the rest of the instruments joined. She extended her good hand out to Dottie who leaned down and gave it a quick kiss before grabbing it with ease.

Rio raised an eyebrow at the action but pulled her partner in and led her through quick synchronized steps before spinning her out again, so they were side by side. The two moved through the classic Charleston motions, their arms swinging and legs twisting in perfect time. Dottie was surprisingly nimble on her feet. She kept up with Rio’s syncopated movements and had her own special flair.

They were a delightful contrast to observe - one dark haired, moving with sensual sparkle and playful creativity, and one light haired, dripping with sexuality and vibrant exuberance. Rio smiled at her partner and twirled her around the floor.

Meanwhile, Billy was in awe of Rio. He watched from behind the bar at the way she kicked out her legs, how she moved her body with such practiced mastery, even with an injured arm. He suddenly thought of Agatha and the protectiveness she seemed to have over Rio, and he darted out the door behind him into the hall and knocked on the distillery door.

“Mother! You’re going to want to see this.” He called out loudly to be heard over the music. It took a second before he heard steps coming toward him.

“There better be some serious trouble out there.” Agatha opened the door with a huff.

“It’s Rio. She’s dancing again.”

“With who?” Agatha had already pushed past Billy and was entering the hall. I hope she’s not drunk again.

“Dottie. You should have seen it - she was laying it on so thick. I think Rio fell right into her trap, she’s not used to a vamp like that.”

“Vamp is right. Dottie will suck the blood from any pretty lady who crosses her path.” They walked together towards the floor. Billy was struggling to keep up with Agatha, who was practically running.

The dance floor wasn’t circled around anyone this time, but Agatha could easily pick out her gold dress in the crowd and its one-armed new owner who was cutting a rug with a talented blonde dame. Her jealousy flared at the sight. Rio was smiling from ear to ear, impressed with herself and with her partner’s moves. She was so at home on the dance floor.

Agatha ripped off the work gloves she was still wearing and shoved them at Billy. “Hold these.”

She started counting herself in and waited for the perfect moment. As Rio spun Dottie out with a flourish, she spun in and took the blonde’s place.

“Hey!” Dottie stumbled backwards on her heels as her flow was interrupted by the cut in.

“Sorry, babe. She owes me one.” Agatha shrugged over her shoulder as Rio caught her and held her hand.

“That’s low, Harkness, even for you!” Dottie backed off the floor in anger, pointing a finger in her direction.

“She’ll get over it.” Agatha said to the brunette and tried to keep up with Rio’s moves.

The pace was quick and energetic. Rio spun her halfway so they were facing the same direction, and they kicked out in sync with each other then spun 180 degrees and did the same the other way. Agatha pulled Rio’s body close so Rio was pressed against her front and she put her hands on her waist. She led them both in matching movements, as her right foot went forward so did Rio’s.

Her face was right behind Rio’s head and she spoke, “I don’t remember saying you could dance on your shift.”

Rio turned slightly, the two still moving with the music, “She made me! I had to prove her wrong. She said I couldn’t dance with my arm like this.”

“She goaded you. Are you going to fall for any beautiful woman who asks you to dance?”

“Maybe just one.” Rio did a spin and was now facing Agatha. She took the lead and pulled her close. “I think I like it when you’re jealous.”

“I’m not - No I was just…” She narrowed her eyes with playful anger.

Rio winked and grinned, “Thanks for the dance, boss.” She walked off the floor and left Agatha solo.

“What the hell? Where are you going?” Agatha followed her.

“I’m not meant to dance on company time, remember? Back to work!”

A laugh escaped out of Agatha’s mouth. God, she’s funny sometimes.

Rio walked back behind the bar to join Billy who was still serving a few customers searching for refills. He gave a little round of applause to her as she joined him.

“I was going to talk to you two soon anyway. Jen and I were talking and thought of a way we can all get a big payday.” She knew Rio desperately needed an influx of cash and the bar could also use a little boost after this situation with Wanda.

“I’m listening.” Rio said.

“Me too!” Billy piped up.

“Well, you know the annual Masquerade and Civic Ball at Hamilton Lodge? The competition has grown so quickly that the firemen have to barricade the doors to prevent overcrowding. The owners asked me if we could host a preliminary elimination to help thin the herd, so to speak. We can expect a full house and will have to judge the contest. The real ball had over 200 competitors last year, so they want us to narrow it down to a top 50.”

“Oh my god, no way! I’ve been trying to get in to see The Fairies Ball for years, and it’s always sold out. This is going to be the cat’s pajamas!” Billy was shaking with excitement.

“I’ve never heard of it.” Rio said with confusion.

“It takes place at Rockland Palace at the very top of Harlem, near Washington Heights. They’ve been hosting this drag ball for over 50 years! The best female and male masqueraders show up to try to win the top prize.” Billy explained.

“And now we get to be part of their history. We have about a month to prepare. They want us to host the prelims on the third weekend of April, the night of the 22nd. We’re going to need wayyyy more booze.”

“Are you thinking what I’m thinking?” Billy questioned.

Rio watched the mischievous look pass between the two of them. “What? What are you thinking?” She looked back and forth quickly.

A huge smile broke out across Agatha’s face. “Pack a bag. It’s time to skip the middleman. We’re going on a rum run.”

Chapter End Notes

Shocked that this silly little niche story that was rattling in my head has found any audience at all. I'm mostly writing this because I want to read it, but I'm very grateful to everyone else along for the ride.

I reference a real drag contest that was a huge annual event in Harlem. The Hamilton Lodge Ball is recognised as the first drag ball in US history - it began in 1869 (!!!) and reached peak popularity during the roaring '20s. At its height up to 8,000 people would attend this cross-dressing contest, and it was racially integrated, which was rare at the time. It ended in 1937 when culture began to turn dramatically against the visibility and acceptance of LGBT people. A great reminder that queer people have always been here and have always existed despite efforts to erase us.

Very excited for the next chapter. Time to throw some kindling on to this slow burn.

All that's wrong is right

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Rio collected $10 in tips on her first night working The Hidden Gate, half of her usual weekly wages. At that rate, she could easily afford rent and bills at Lilia’s place and start saving for something more.

She walked back with Agatha to her apartment after the bar closed. The city was still buzzing with energy even at the late hour. Cars and carriages tore up and down the streets, couples lingered on street corners delaying their mutual goodbyes, groups of friends laughed and joked with each other on their way home.

When they arrived at Agatha’s place, they both crashed onto the couch.

“So what should I pack for our adventure?” Rio turned her head to face her companion.

Rio shoved her shoulder over to knock her booth mate. Agatha bumped her back then couldn’t resist the opportunity to capture her lips once more as they connected again.

Their first kiss had been all passion and intensity - the culmination of extended yearning. This one was slow and tender. Every time she smelled this scent in the future it would jolt her back to this moment. The exact snapshot in time when she had her real first kiss. The first kiss to make her question her sanity because how had she lived this long without experiencing this level of bliss.

This time Agatha pulled away first, “I don’t want to pop this bubble.”

“No, I mean, what do we do about..us?” Rio asked innocently.

“I think it’s pretty clear. I’m stuck on you, Rio.” Agatha laid it out plainly. “Just one rule - no more dancing with hot blondes.”

Rio’s smile stretched from ear to ear. She didn’t want to think of the logistics, of how this would work, of what it all meant. She simply nodded enthusiastically and threw her arms around Agatha in a deep embrace.

Nothing else mattered.

Not yet.

On the road

“Are we there yet?” Rio asked aloud to no one.

“The chicken salad sandwich here is to die for.” Agatha pointed it out on the menu.

“What can I get everyone to drink?” An older gentleman in a bowtie stood waiting for their orders.

Agatha laughed at his sweet tooth then looked at the server, “Black coffee.”

“A grape lemonade, thank you.” Rio would hardly admit it, but she loved a fruity drink.

Chapter End Notes

I pulled Jean-Paul Beaubier and Kyle Jinadu from the Marvel Comics/X-men universe. I was just searching for Canadian characters and stumbled on these two who are the first openly gay Marvel comic characters and had the first same-sex wedding in mainstream comic history, which felt very apt.

Apologies if they are totally OOC.

Rio was glad she hadn’t brought gloves because the feel of Agatha’s hand in hers was exhilarating. She had held hands with many girl friends in the past, as was common at the time, but the secret she shared with the woman next to her made this regular gesture feel scandalous.

They approached the staggering, Gothic church from the front, and Rio took in the towering, twin spires, the trio of pointed arches, and the delicately carved statues along the facade. It was not unlike many of the historic churches in the city, so she wasn’t sure why Agatha had brought them here.

That was until they entered the building, and her breath stopped. The ceiling sang to her as if it were a chorus from heaven itself. The soaring, vaulted interior was painted a deep, rich blue and dotted with golden stars, all coalescing to three wide rose windows that flooded the space with reverent light. The floor mirrored the bright blue and gold design, and the stained glass windows bounced colors throughout the space.

Rio felt tears forming in her eyes at the sheer beauty of it all. The intricately carved wooden pews, the twisting, hand-painted columns, the towering statues behind the pulpit. She tried to absorb every beautiful detail, and as she spun in place, she noticed one person wasn’t taking in the view like everybody else.

Agatha was staring at her the way she was staring at the ceiling. Like she was the work of architectural brilliance. Like she had been hand-sculpted over a hundred years ago by the hands of master artists.

And perhaps it was the stunning blues that encompassed the room or maybe the work of the divine, but Agatha’s steely blue eyes were glowing the most blazing sapphire in color. Rio had to fight every urge inside her to run over and kiss those lips with the full force of her veneration and outpouring of awe.

Instead, she strolled over, and Agatha gently caressed the side of her face and wrapped her other hand around the back of her head before pulling her into an intimate hug. She closed her eyes at the feeling, which somehow rivaled the intensity of the visionary masterwork that surrounded them. Agatha sighed into the embrace, and she felt the arms around her like a warm blanket - protective, comforting, safe. She pulled away gently.

“It’s so beautiful.” She whispered quietly. Her eyes tracing the arcs of the ceiling again.

“Yes, you are.” Agatha replied. Her gaze never leaving the beauty of the woman in front of her.

The group spent the rest of the morning sight-seeing in the historic part of Montreal and had a light lunch of sandwiches by the docks.

“How do we kill the afternoon?” Rio asked between bites of her ham sandwich.

“Can we see a movie?” Billy looked to Agatha expectantly.

“I think there is a brand new picture house that is supposed to be a real stunner. I read about it in the paper this morning.” She explained.

Billy took the wheel again and drove them towards the Little Italy neighborhood. They found the Théâtre Plaza easily as the large sign on the roof was visible from streets away.

“Ahhhh!!!” Billy screamed when he saw the marquee of pictures. “They have Nosferatu! Oh my gosh, Tommy was able to catch a one-off screening in Brooklyn, but I missed out.”

“What in god's name is a nosferatu?” Agatha watched the boy jumping in place.

He gasped audibly, “Have you read Dracula?”

Agatha said ‘no’ while Rio simultaneously said ‘yes.’

“It’s a German adaptation of the novel. Tommy had to sleep with the lamp on for a week straight after watching it! I can’t believe it’s showing here.”

“Don’t come crying to us at night if you get too scared.” Agatha warned.

They passed their coins over for three tickets and settled into the velvet seats of the picture palace. The room darkened as the movie began. A pianist sat on the side of the stage to provide music accents, and there was a live narrator to translate the German text on screen.

It was slow at the start, but as the main character entered the castle of Count Orlak, Rio felt Agatha reach over and grip her hand tightly. As night fell in the film and the vampire appeared for the first time, she leaned into Agatha, and they grasped at each other for comfort. She glanced over and saw Billy covering his eyes with his sleeve.

She relished the feeling of Agatha’s arm around her. Despite the horrors unfolding on screen, she loved that she could openly hold Agatha in public like this. Billy was cowering in his seat as the vampire went to attack the wife and drink her blood. She reached out and offered a hand, which he grabbed desperately. The two women shared a quiet laugh at their sweet companion.

As the curtains closed and they exited the cinema, the sun hit them with full force. Luckily it didn’t cause them to disappear in a puff of smoke like Count Orlak, but it felt just as violent.

“I may have made a mistake.” Billy admitted as they walked to the car.

“You think? I thought you were going to have a heart attack in there when the monster appeared.” Agatha’s laugh rang out on the street.

Billy held his hand up in defeat, “You gotta admit that was pretty scary though, right? Rio?”

“I liked it.” Rio said. “You were right - I’ve never seen anything like that before. The company wasn’t half bad either.” She playfully elbowed Agatha.

They drove back at around 3:30 pm to check on the progress of their car and its new cargo.

“Agatha, mon chaton! What timing. The team just secured the last case in your vehicle. It should be all set.” Jean-Paul was overseeing the meticulous operation on the warehouse floor.

“Perfect!” Agatha clapped her hands. “And how much were they able to fit?” She casually walked around the car, inspecting every detail. Jean-Paul’s team was the best in the business. She couldn’t see any of the alterations or hints that anything had changed.

“100 gallons, which should yield at least 500 bottles. A mix of our top selling whisky and rum, so it should more than satisfy a crowd. Each case is nailed shut and secured tightly, so you shouldn’t need to worry about driving extra carefully.” He slapped the hood with gusto.

“And what’re you asking?”

“$400 even, for the drink and the service.” He said. Agatha knew she was getting a discounted mate’s rate but wasn’t about to complain. She was a reliable customer and repeat buyer, plus she was damn good company.

She could make more than double that by selling this at the club either straight or in cocktails. She opened her bag and pulled out the bills, passing them over quickly.

“Merci, merci. I always appreciate your prompt payment. Will you be back soon?” He pocketed the money.

“Undoubtedly.”

They all shared one last dinner together. This time Jean-Paul donned the chef’s hat and presented a hearty cassoulet. For Rio it was reminiscent of her abuela’s asopao de pollo, a similar rich, meaty stew.

She looked around the table and was once again struck with gratitude that her life had taken a new, unforeseen detour to this present. She could have never predicted that she would be sitting in Canada (of all places) with a woman as stunning as Agatha (who actually liked her) and three homosexuals (who are not strange or evil). Life was truly unpredictable.

They left at the crack of dawn as soon as the sun crested the horizon. Agatha took the first shift like last time to get them going, and this time Rio sat in the back as she wanted to lay across the seats to rest.

The Studebaker was holding the weight shockingly well. It sat a tick lower than normal, but its six-cylinder engine gave it the juice to maintain high speeds despite the added pounds.

“Can I work the drag ball night, Agatha? I can stay as late as you need me. I can even help with setup - whatever you need.” Billy had clearly been thinking about this.

“I was counting on your help. We’re going need all hands on deck to be fair. I think it might have to take place over two nights to be able to accommodate all the contestants plus all the onlookers. I’m going to need to help Jen make even more batches. We’ll have to call in some favors.” She was thinking through all the details to pull this off.

If all went well, the payoff was going to be massive. They were going to set a cover charge to get in, plus a few extra dimes on top of all drink prices, plus the expected tips. This would certainly help Rio get back on her feet and help the rest of them top up their piggy banks.

They were about an hour and a half on their journey when a loud bang reverberated throughout the cab of the car, and everything tilted.

Oh fuck.

Agatha had popped a tire before, but never while illegally transporting excessive amounts of smuggled liquor from over the border.

Rio jolted awake at the sound and leaned over the front seat, “What happened? Is everything alright?”

“We’ve blown a tire. I’m going to pull over.” Agatha slowed the car and pulled off to the grassy edge. Luckily there was almost nobody else on the road at this time of morning.

She got out and inspected the damage. The back left tire had popped and was completely flat.

“You have a spare, right?” Rio was standing beside her looking at the pathetic remains.

Agatha brought a hand to her hair and grasped at the strands while letting out a sigh, “No, unfortunately not. We strip the car to make room for as much alcohol as possible. Looks like that’s one calculated risk that did not pay off.”

It wasn’t busy on the road yet, but Agatha didn’t want to gamble. The police frequented every route in and out of their northern neighbor, doubly so since the Prohibition laws went into effect.

“What do we do, Mother?” Billy looked anxious.

Rio watched Agatha and saw her mind ticking along at a million miles per hour. Her fingers were moving in the air like they were playing invisible saxophones - the nervous energy literally flowing out of her.

“We passed a mechanic about a mile back in Keeseville. It was right off this road, you can’t miss it. Do you think you can make it there, Billy? They should have a spare. Ask for 30 inches for a Studebaker 6. Got it? Take this.” She passed him a $10 note.

He nodded then took off at a jog in the direction which they had come.

“Is he gonna be alright?” Rio watched his retreating body fade into the distance.

“He’s got a good head on his shoulders. I trust him. Let’s get back in the car, it’s dangerous standing on the side of the road.” Agatha opened the passenger door, and they both slid in.

A silence fell over them, only intermittently interrupted by the zoom of a passing car or truck.

“Agatha?” Rio looked tentatively over to the other woman, who seemed lost in her own thoughts.

“Yes, honey. Are you okay?”

“Yeah, it’s just…I’m scared when we get back.” She paused for a second. “What if Tony comes to the shop again? What if he tries to find me and…and hurt me?” She felt so small as she uttered her fears aloud.

“Look at me.” Agatha put both hands on either side of Rio’s face. “That man - no, that boy - is never going to hurt you again. Ya hear me?”

“But…”

She felt Agatha’s fingers caressing her scalp. “Nope, no but’s. I promise you; you won’t have to worry about him again. He is gone from your life.”

“How?” Rio couldn’t understand. Tony was relentless when he set his mind to something. She just never imagined she would be that something.

She felt Agatha’s gradual pull on her neck and the soft joy of a subtle kiss on her lips. The older woman whispered between pecks, “Trust me. It’s taken care of.”

And she knew she should ask what that meant or press for more details, but every time Agatha kissed her it was like every train of thought left the station at once.

She leaned forward to press against the awaiting lips with fervor, but just as soon as it began a siren wailed behind them, and her heart dropped like a brick.

They looked at each other as if time had stopped and heard the police car pull up behind their broken down hayburner.

“Stay calm.” Agatha squeezed her hand and opened the door. “I’ve got this.”

She all but ran towards the cop car. “Oh officer, thank the lord you stumbled upon us! We’ve had some dreadful luck this morning.”

Rio was still in the car but covered her mouth to hold in the laughter at the exaggerated southern accent that Agatha was putting on.

“I see that, ma’am. Is your husband in the car?” The police man was in his 40s, bland, forgettable.

“My dear husband.” She pretended to dab her eyes with her sleeve. “He passed in the war and we miss him somethin’ awful. My friend, Rosemary, and my son, Beauford, were just visitin’ my Auntie Dolores in Canada. She is a real fine lady. Anyway, we were headin’ back down to Georgia this morning when this dadgum tire went and blew its lid!”

“Where’s your spare?” The officer looked at her curiously. Rio hoped he was buying the act.

“My poor Beauford is about as useful as a steerin’ wheel on a mule, the sweet summer child. He left it at home thinking it was just for decoration! Luckily that boy can run faster than a hot knife through butter, so he’s off to buy one from the fuel stop. Shouldn’t be long now, sorry for taking up your time, sir.” Agatha was laying it on thick. Rio was impressed.

“Are you sure? I can take a look for you.” The man started to crouch and examine the busted tire, completely unaware that he was mere inches from copious amounts of hooch hidden in the base of the car.

“Oh no! I’m sure you’re busier than a moth in a mitten, officer. We’ll be on our way in no time. I’m fixin’ to get moving as soon as Beauford runs his little hide back here.” She tried to usher him away from the car as quickly as possible.

“Thanks so much for stopping, sir. You’re a real doll.” Agatha flashed her smile and turned up the charm.

The policeman smiled back, oblivious to the way she was working him like a baker works a piece of dough into submission.

He was about to walk away when he turned again. “Let me just have a quick check in your trunk. Did you look in every compartment?” He put a hand on the trunk handle.

As he started to open it, Rio stared through the back window in fear. He was a moment away from potentially busting them. Any practiced man of the law would notice the curiously high false bottom to the trunk space. She looked to Agatha who was staring wide eyed, her normal dominance and control faltering.

Rio’s hands were shaking, but her body was moving before her mind could protest.

She collapsed out of the door and threw herself on the ground.

“Whoaaaaa!” She tried her best to sell it, taking a note from Agatha’s acting book.

The police officer immediately ran over to check on her, “Miss, Miss, are you okay? What happened?”

“Ri-Rosemary!” Agatha yelled out, catching herself as she remembered the fake name she had picked.

Rio was not confident enough to even attempt any accent work, “Where am I?” She rasped out the question as she turned her head slowly to look up and check that the cop had come over.

“You just fell out of your car, miss.” He helped her sit up on the grass on the side of the road.

“Ah, I was feeling light-headed and then the next thing I knew I was lying on the ground!”

“Have you eaten anything this morning?” He took her elbow and eased her up to stand.

“We got straight on the road, officer. I was so keen to leave early. My mistake.” Agatha answered as she tried to hide her impressed smirk.

“There’s a rest stop just a few miles ahead. I suggest you stop there as soon as possible. Women have much more delicate constitutions, you know?”

Agatha had to fight every urge to roll her eyes straight back into her head at the condescension. “Bless your heart, thank you for the advice, sir.”

He straightened up and pushed his shoulders back, very pleased with himself, then tipped his cap. “You both be safe now and get some food for that girl as soon as you can. Have a nice trip.”

Rio and Agatha slid back into the car, holding their giggles until the copper was well on his way.

“Were you an actress in another life? That was amazing!” Rio was grinning, the adrenaline of the encounter still pumping through her.

“That performance? That was nothing! I think I was a bat of the eyelashes away from getting us a police escort all the way down to the city.” She laughed easily. “What about you? You saved us with your fainting spell. That was genius!”

“It was all I could think of to stop him!” Rio shrugged her shoulders. “I have nothing on you. I’m just glad you use your powers for good because wow, you’d be a force to be reckoned with if you ever decided to go to the dark side.” Rio said.

“What makes you think I haven’t already joined the underbelly?”

“You care too much. I haven’t known you for long, but the way you look out for me, for Billy, for Lilia, for everyone at the club. I don’t think you could be evil.” Rio extended an arm out to touch Agatha.

“You always see the best in me.” Agatha smiled back. It was only about another 10 minutes before they heard the sounds of shoes hitting the gravel and looked behind them to see Billy approaching with a large tire rolling alongside.

Even with the cool temperature, sweat was dripping from his brow and down the sides of his face. He was panting and held onto the side of the car to steady himself.

“We don’t have anything to drink besides booze…” Rio grimaced.

“It’s gonna have to do.” Agatha unscrewed one of the bottles that Jean-Paul had gifted them. “Take a few sips, kid. You need the fluids.”

“Aaack, I don’t think that’s helping!” Billy was no stranger to alcohol, but he rarely partook - only an occasional cocktail if Agatha made it for him - never straight whisky.

“That’ll perk you up.” Agatha laughed then rolled the sleeves up on her sweater. “Help me change this, and we can get moving again.”

Rio watched the two of them change the tire with speed and precision. Luckily, they still had a jack and a wrench in the car. In no time, they were back on the road.

“Okay, note to self, next time don’t forget the spare!” Agatha announced to nobody, and they all laughed. At least they had a memorable story to tell.

Chapter End Notes

Couldn't resist throwing in a Nosferatu reference given the original release year matched with the story. I also recommend looking up a picture of Montreal's Notre-Dame, I don't think I did it justice with my description.

Thanks again for reading! Next chapter we learn some of the fallout from Wanda's actions.

All that's foul and fair

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

They made it back just after 1pm on Sunday, and the city felt frenetic compared to the quiet of the open road. Agatha pulled up to the street behind the club alley and parked the car.

“Head home and get some rest. Meet me back here at 9 tonight so that we can unload this under some cover of darkness.” She explained.

“See you!” Billy took off down the street to his house.

“Where does he store all that energy?” Rio wondered.

“Who knows? Are you okay to work tonight also? Sundays are usually pretty busy.”

“I’ll be here. Don’t miss me too much.” She hugged Agatha and went back to Lilia’s.

Agatha locked the Studebaker, checked and then double-checked to make sure it was secure and walked to her apartment. The last thing they needed was someone stealing the outcome of all their efforts.

She got off the elevator and opened the door. It was dark inside, the curtains were all drawn.

“Ebony, I’m home.” She called her cat as she placed her bag down. She had asked her neighbor, Iris, to check in and feed her while they were away.

She flicked the light switch in the dining room and must have jumped three feet off the ground.

“Jesus fucking christ!” Agatha put her hands on her knees to catch her breath.

“Welcome back, Mother.”

Sitting at the dining table was the dangerous, beautiful redhead that tormented her nightmares, stroking Agatha’s black cat with her velvet-gloved hands.

“Wanda, what the fuck are you doing in my house?” Agatha searched the room for any other surprises, but it appeared the intruder was alone. She also glanced for anything that could be used as a weapon but came up short.

“Is that how you greet all your friends?” Wanda asked. Her voice was soft but cutting.

“We’re not friends.”

“Ouch. And here I thought we were getting along so well, especially after this job I just completed for you.” Ebony jumped off the foreign lap and wandered over to her owner. Wanda swiped the cat hair from her black wool serge frock.

“It’s done?” Agatha hoped the Tony problem was finally a thing of the past.

“You conveniently failed to mention that he lived with two other people, and that they would put up a fight…” Wanda leaned back in the dining chair.

“What?” Agatha held onto the top rail of the chair in front of her as if it could provide any stabilization. “I swear I had no idea.”

Wanda quietly observed her prey. Her eyes seemed to see through Agatha like she was made of glass. She loved to watch her victims sweat.

“Are you sure?” She pressed sweetly.

“Honestly, I thought he would be alone. Please.” Agatha’s gaze fell on the leather bag sitting beneath the table - that wasn’t hers. She felt increasingly tense.

Wanda rocked her head side-to-side in contemplation. “You know…I think I believe you.”

Agatha released a heavy sigh, “Thank you, truly. I’m sorry for any trouble he caused. I will-”

The mob boss held a hand up, silencing the next words that were about to come. “Save it. We need to discuss what you owe.”

“I’ll have my team deliver the hooch tonight. Just name a time and place.” Agatha hated the power Wanda yielded over her. She resented the fear that still sat in her chest when speaking with this woman.

“Price has changed.” She spoke flatly, no room for argument.

“But…” Agatha stopped herself this time before continuing.

“Your small favor ended with my brother fracturing his nose and one of my other men is now a few screws loose in the head after he was knocked unconscious. Liquor just ain’t gonna cover that.”

God, things really didn’t go to plan. Agatha braced herself for what she was going to have to give up.

Wanda thought for a moment, “I know.” She pointed to the woman across from her. “You are going to host me, my husband, and all of our organisation at your club. No other guests - completely private event. Drinks on the house and the best singers and dancers you can book on the stage.”

Agatha grimaced. There went her big pay day.

“When?” She tried to keep her cool.

“Don’t worry, doll. Vision’s out of town for a month. He’s making some new connections in Chicago.  And then we’ll have some business to sort out when he gets back. So, let’s say mid-May. I want to make sure you have enough time to really go all out. This better be the greatest shindig The Hidden Gate has ever seen.”

“I never leave a lady disappointed.” Agatha was going to have to pull off something spectacular to impress Wanda. The drag ball in a few weeks would be a perfect test run.

Wanda licked her lips, “I expect not. I know where you live, where you work. I just have one nagging question.” She stood from her chair and approached the tense woman across from her. “There’s one thing I can’t understand.”

Agatha watched the redhead walk over and steadied her breathing. Her nerves felt like they were tap dancing, bouncing around restlessly and distracting her mind.

Wanda stood in front of her and raised her hand to move some stray hairs off Agatha’s face. The familiar gesture was an unwelcome surprise. She then leaned in toward her ear and of every question, taunt, or insult that Agatha had expected to hear, this one floored her.

“Who is Rio?”

Agatha’s hand shot up and caught Wanda’s wrist that was still stroking her hair. She gripped it as tight as she could.

She spit out the next words with all the vitriol she could manage, “Keep her name…out of your mouth.”

The anxiety in her body had morphed like a tormented butterfly and emerged as pure rage.

Wanda blinked rapidly, clearly caught off guard. But as she processed the response, a twisted smile expanded across her face.

“Well...I think that answers that.” She yanked her arm out of Agatha’s grip with some effort and rubbed at her wrist. “If I knew you liked them young, I would have tried a little harder a few years ago.”

Wanda winked and wiggled her hips just enough to catch the older woman’s angry gaze.

“There’s something wrong with you.” Agatha shook her head. One second Wanda was threatening Rio and now she was…flirting with her? This was a very dangerous game, and now she had dragged her lover into it.

“Am I not broken enough for you?” Wanda pouted. “Do you only want projects you can fix? Is that it? This girl was getting walloped by her man, so then you get to swoop in and play hero.”

“We’re not discussing her.” A flash of hatred flickered across Agatha’s face.

Wanda bent to pick up her bag and put her coat on, “Everyone says you’re fun, but I’m not seeing it. Hopefully, this isn’t indicative of the type of party you throw.”

Agatha led the way out, “I promise you’ll be more than satisfied.” She swallowed her resentment as she opened the front door.

“Now there’s something I don’t doubt.” She quickly landed a hearty peck on Agatha’s cheek, who bared her teeth like a wild animal at the intrusion. “You’ll be hearing from me.”

The door shut, and Agatha let out an exhilarating growl into her empty home, her hands curled into tights fists, her arms holding her rage. She went into the bathroom to get a glass of water and caught her reflection. The bold red print of Wanda’s lips marked her cheek like a brand.

That fucking bitch. She pawed aggressively at the imprint with wet hands and tried to swipe away every trace of the interaction.

As the lipstick disappeared, she was left with only the raw reality of the situation. She now had to host the entire Sokovian gang for a night at the club, so she would both lose all potential profit from a typical operating night and compensate for all the alcohol they were bound to consume, plus the entertainment costs.

She splashed water on her face to cool down. On top of all that, Wanda somehow knew about Rio and knew that Rio was someone she cared about. Fuck.

Wanda was infamous for her torture methods. Hell, that was why Agatha had hired her to take care of Tony in the first place. Everyone in town thought it was Vision who harbored the cruelty and pain that propelled their gang to power, but Agatha knew that all these men were blind to the capabilities of Wanda.

She was the one who could break down any goodfella, and her usual method involved exploiting their emotional vulnerabilities or romantic connections. She wasn’t above beating a man’s girl to get him to squeal.

I need to be smarter. I need to keep Rio safe. Agatha looked at herself in the mirror and repeated the phrases like a mantra.

First step, change my locks.

Rio arrived back at Lilia's apartment and dropped her bag.

“Hey kiddo, how was your trip?” Lilia was sitting in the lounge, reading a book.

Rio walked over and took a seat in one of the armchairs. “Amazing, I loved it. Jean-Paul and Kyle were so welcoming and nice. Montreal was stunning.”

“I haven’t been in decades now. I’d love to see it now. Any trouble on the road?”

“A flat tire, which almost turned into a whole debacle. Luckily, Agatha could charm the pants off anyone.” Rio softly smiled at the thought.

“Why am I not surprised?” Lilia closed her book and looked up. “Also, someone came to the shop on Friday morning looking for you.”

Rio felt her shoulders stiffen.

“It wasn’t that man from before.”

She relaxed slightly, “Who was it? I don’t know many other people.”

“A young woman, close to your age, looked Puerto Rican as well. She seemed pretty distressed at the time, but she ran off when I said you wouldn’t be back until next week.”

“Claudia…” Rio’s leg was bouncing nervously. “My old roommate. I should go check on her, make sure she’s alright.” If Tony laid a hand on her, so help me.

She grabbed her cloche hat and took off to her old neighborhood. Before long, she was outside the building and climbing the long walk up to the apartment. Immediately, she noticed the new door - a temporary bit of plywood, holding the space for what used to stand in its place.

She knocked carefully, afraid it might fall over.

“Who is it?” She heard a small voice call out but the tinge of fear was audible.

“Claudia? Qué pasó? What’s going on?”

“Rio! Ay bendito, I thought you were…” She opened the door and looked out cautiously. “Come in, rápidamente.” Rio quickly stepped in.

She looked at her old living space and took in the damage. There were large, horrifying bloodstains on the hardwoods, one of the photo frames on the wall was smashed, one of the dining chairs was missing. She looked at her friend who had a sizable bandage across her neck.

“What happened…” Rio was at a loss for words. She couldn’t imagine what had caused all this.

Claudia moved to the couch, and they both sat. “It was last Thursday. We were all here eating dinner and out of nowhere someone kicked the door off its hinges. Two men and a woman stormed in, and I screamed. They were holding weapons, but Tony and Miguel were fearless. Tony socked one and Miguel stabbed the other with a fork and kicked him down to the ground.”

Rio was in shock. Who would want to attack them like this?

“I thought we had a chance, but the evil puta with the red hair grabbed me and held a knife to my throat.”

“No!” Rio gasped.

“She told the men to stop or she would kill me. I felt the blade on my skin, and she started to dig it in. I was so surprised. I couldn’t even feel the pain.”

“Ay dios mío, what happened next?” Rio was gripping Claudia’s hand tightly, holding on to every word.

There was a pause as she watched Claudia struggle with something, “Rio, they were here for Tony…”

“What? What do you mean?”

“The woman said Miguel and I could leave because they only wanted Tony. They had a gun - we should have stayed, but we were so scared. I thought they were going to kill us all.” Claudia was trembling at the recollection.

“No, I understand. What did they do with him?” She was afraid of the answer.

“We went down the street and hid in the Brown’s place. Mrs. Brown patched me up, and we waited a few hours. Then, Miguel ran back first to check if it was safe and called down to me.” She let out a long breath. “Tony wasn’t here. He must have been tied to one of the chairs because it was smashed to pieces, so he must have broken out of it. There was…blood. It was everywhere. I’ve tried cleaning it up but…”

“I’m so sorry. Have you seen him since?”

“He hasn’t come back. Most of his stuff is gone. We don’t know if he took it or those people took it. He’s just…gone.” Claudia said.

Rio wasn’t sure how to feel. It was a weird cocktail of relief, shock, joy, pain, and confusion. Blessings and burdens alike.

“What did the intruders look like? Were they cops?” She asked.

“Definitely not la policia. They were White and had accents from overseas but I couldn't even guess where. The woman was petite, scarlet hair, very glamorous attire - must be well-off. One man was short, stocky build, dirty blonde hair. The other looked quite similar to the woman, but with hair almost snow white in color, very large muscles, athletic.”

“I’ll ask around. I know someone who knows everyone.” Rio hoped Agatha might know who could have committed this crime.

“Be careful, amiga. These were very experienced, very violent people. Keep an eye out…” Claudia wrapped her in a hug, “…in case they come for you.”

As night fell, the road trip gang reunited in the alley as planned. Agatha and Rio immediately embraced upon seeing each other again. Neither aware of the intense experiences they had both endured that afternoon.

“I missed you.” Agatha whispered in her ear, and Rio melted.

“Billy, can you go get Alice? We need some help carrying all this.” Agatha asked, and he ran and knocked on the door to get her.

“Are you okay?” Rio was studying her carefully.

“Yeah, of course. Why?” Agatha’s mind was still replaying her run-in with Wanda. She had breathed a sigh of relief when Rio had made it here tonight.

“You just seem quiet. Very unlike you.”

“A lot on my mind, I guess. Don’t worry. Are you okay? You seem - off.”

“We’ll talk later.” Rio assured her.

Chapter End Notes

I pulled some quotes from Drag Race and also some real descriptions of drag balls from 1920's newspaper clippings. They were huge events that drew thousands of people to pack out dance halls and clubs.

For decades the Hamilton Lodge drag ball was a place of queer celebration, but it ended in 1937 following an election in New York that brought in an unfriendly political administration intent on "fighting vice." Police officers who once provided security for the balls were then tasked with arresting the contestants on charges of indecency, vagrancy, or female impersonation. A sad parallel to the current state of things.
