Rio couldn’t imagine it either. It seemed as far-fetched as an HG Wells story, as unlikely as a woman in the White House or a visit to the moon.

Went out last night with a crowd of my friends,

They must've been women, 'cause I don't like no men.

It's true I wear a collar and a tie,

Makes the wind blow all the while

Agatha spun Rio out and extended her arm. She caught her easily as she twirled back in. They moved in lock step with each other. It was seamless and easy. Rio wished she had worn a suit again. It really was much more comfortable dancing in pants and flat shoes, despite her familiarity with the alternative.

Don't you say I do it, ain't nobody caught me

You sure got to prove it on me.

Say I do it, ain't nobody caught me

Sure got to prove it on me.

The song finished with a perfect sustained note from Gladys, and Rio kissed Agatha softly before ending their private moment on the dance floor.

“Thanks for the dance, sweetheart.” Agatha lifted Rio’s hand and kissed the top of it like they were in an old fairy tale.

They heard Billy clapping behind the bar - their biggest fan. Rio rolled her eyes and went to join him to prepare.

“You two set the bar too high. I want to have what you have.” He said.

“You’re still so young. You’ve got plenty of time.” Rio started pulling bottles of rum from the open cases. “What about Eddie?”

Billy sighed, “We’ve met up a few more times since that night, but…I don’t know. He is so jumpy and hesitant when we’re out together. It’s not the same.”

“Sorry kid. Maybe he just needs some time. It can be tough to come to terms with brand new feelings like this, take it from me.”

Jen came out the side door, “Hey you two, I’ve stacked the crates in the hall for easy access. Moonshine first, then whisky, then gin, rum, and beer. Everything is labelled and organized by value so always pull from the top of the stack first. Got it?”

“Aye aye captain.” Billy saluted her.

“Thanks, matey. I’ll be trying to keep a low profile tonight in the back, I don’t know where the Sokovians stand on color mixing, and I don’t intend to find out. But if you need me, just do the double knock on the back room door.”

Rio nodded, “Thank you, Jen. Hopefully we won’t need anything.”

“Darcy said she would cover the coat check for me, then she’ll handle service on the floor - cleaning up glasses and delivering drinks.” Billy let her know.

“Great. Agatha said she was going to stay at the bar with us. That should keep us safe from any aggressive types.” Rio said.

“Oh thank god.” Billy let out a sigh of relief. “I’m worried, Rio.”

“We’ll be fine. I trust Agatha with my life. She won’t let anything bad happen to us.” Rio reached out and gave him a comforting pat on the back. “Remember the road trip? She would lie to a cop to keep us out of trouble.”

Billy’s laugh broke the tension, “You’re right. I bet it will all be fine.”

They finished the final preparations, and the whole crew did one last sweep of the place to clean any rogue dust bunnies or spider webs still lingering in corners. There were just 20 minutes left before they expected the first arrivals.

Agatha gave the last words, “Remember - stay alert, stay safe, look out for each other. We will get through this together.”

They all clasped hands in a circle, “Let’s do this!” Billy called out and each person let out a cheer.

“I’m grateful to you all. You’re my family.” Rio added.

“I never had kids of my own, but I see you all like my children.” Sharon almost broke them all with her confession. She was usually more of a quiet observer.

“I only come to work every day because of you freaks.” Alice shared.

“Y’all are alright.” Jen relented but everybody knew what she really meant.

“This is our home. We have a duty to protect it. I love every one of you.” Agatha looked at them all with a smile but her gaze lingered exceptionally long on Rio. The two shared the look and their eyes said all the words they couldn’t speak aloud.

Alice left first to go monitor the door and the rest of the group went to their work stations. Herb and the security staff finished their briefing and positioned themselves around the hall.

Rio felt her heart beating in her chest. The first group started entering the club - a mix of young men with their dates. Nobody recognizable yet.

The band started playing, and Agatha was grateful for the soothing melodies of Gladys’ voice.

“Hey toots, get me a gin rickey.” A loudmouth called out to Rio, knocking annoyingly on the bartop.

Agatha watched the grimace on Rio’s face and saw her holding back the biting response that was probably kicking to escape. Instead, she said nothing and made the drink quickly.

“One gin rickey.” She slid the drink over.

“Where’s the smile, dollface? You would look so pretty if you smiled.”

Rio’s hands curled into fists beneath the bar. Agatha wondered if she would draw blood from how tightly she was squeezing. She reached over and tried to get her to release the tension.

“Who’s next?” She called out and some other lad pushed to the front to get his order in. Billy took care of it.

Rio knelt down to get another bottle and Agatha joined her down there. “Hey, it’s okay. Just breathe through it. Ignore these fools.” Rio nodded and gathered herself.

When they stood up, Agatha spotted Wanda entering the club with Vision on her arm. The redhead turned heads in her knee-length fur trimmed coat. She passed it to her husband and revealed her light rose party dress beneath with a triple flounce tiered skirt. Her shimmering diamond necklace accented the dipping neckline.

The woman commanded attention and walked through the room like she owned it. The clicking of her heels was like a terrible countdown announcing her arrival to the bar.

“The place looks real spiffy, Mother. You did well.” She leaned against the counter and motioned about the space.

“Wanda, what can I get you?” Agatha replied, keeping it cordial.

“I want her to serve me.” She pointed to Rio.

Agatha’s eyes flicked to her lover who was looking back with hesitation. Before she could speak, Rio stepped up, “What would you like?”

“Well that’s a broad question. There’s a lot that I would like.” Wanda stared at the young woman. Her eye contact was alluring.

“To drink…” Rio prompted, shifting uncomfortably under the imposing gaze.

“Surprise me.” Wanda ran her tongue slowly across her bottom lip.

Rio turned around and tried to follow Agatha’s advice. She took a deep breath and centered herself again. She grabbed a shaker and mixed rum, pineapple juice, and grenadine. She set a cocktail glass in front of the redhead and watched the look of delight when the light pink drink flowed out.

“A Mary Pickford for you - to match your dress.” Rio said.

“Aren’t you thoughtful? Thanks dear.” She took the drink and sipped it slowly. “Ah, that’s the good stuff.”

“Glad you like it.”

“I’ll certainly be back for more.” Wanda took the glass and took up residence at a nearby table where Vision was already holding court.

“Good work, you handled that well.” Billy nudged her, impressed at her cool demeanor.

“Thanks, she doesn’t seem that scary in person.” Rio confessed.

“She’s good at pretending.” Agatha said dryly.

“Did you see her eyes? I’ve never seen anyone else with green eyes like Tommy.” Billy had been captured by the color, which he had thought was unique to his twin.

“I hadn’t noticed. I was too busy trying not to spill her drink.” Rio shrugged and went to serve the next needy customer.

Gladys was tearing it up on the piano and keeping the crowd busy. Her raunchy songs were laced with double-entendres, and the gang was eating it up. Her powerful voice rose above the drunken rowdiness.

Agatha’s eyes, however, never left Wanda. She watched the woman, who in turn was watching her. The two were locked in a silent duel.

Then someone threw a punch on the dance floor.

Fuck.

Agatha waved to Herb and they both ran out to break it up. She helped him pull the attacker off the other guy, whose nose was now bleeding, and Herb pushed away the other instigators who had jumped in on the action. It seemed like more kept appearing out of nowhere though. She couldn’t even tell what they were fighting about.

“Get off!” She yelled as she finally yanked the last man off.

Pietro turned and smiled dangerously at her. She removed her hands like she had been burned. No.

She twisted her neck violently to check the bar. Rio was nowhere to be seen. Her eyes tracked to the tables. Wanda was gone.

She went to move but Pietro’s arm shot out and grabbed her wrist. “Not so fast.” He declared.

“Fuck off, you grey-headed prick.” Agatha pulled her arm to try to release his hold, but he wasn’t budging. She could feel his fingers pulling at her skin, digging in hard.

“She just wants to have a short chat. Let’s give them some privacy.” He moved them to a table, so it wasn’t so obvious that he was restraining her.

“If she lays a hand on Rio, I swear to god I’ll burn this place to the ground to get her.” Agatha protested and tried to signal any of her staff, but everyone was overwhelmed with other priorities.

Billy was pouring at least ten drinks at the same time, Darcy was mopping up a bunch of spilled glasses, Jen was nowhere to be seen, all the security guards were either escorting people out or keeping them from fighting again.

“Pietro, let me go.” Agatha tugged again but his strength was keeping her in place.

“No can do. Boss’ orders.”

“You’re going to regret this. I’ll scream.” She warned. The minutes were passing slowly, and she wished she could chew her arm off to get to Rio right now. The thought of Wanda alone in a room with her made her feel ill.

“You’re outnumbered, and nobody is coming to save you down here in your own illegal establishment.” Pietro was lapping it up, enjoying the control - a sick smile shined at Agatha. “We’ve got you.”

When Agatha had left to break up the fight, almost all the patrons had run to the dance floor to watch. They were like children, so eager to see violence. It left the bar empty so Rio had taken the short reprieve to run to the bathroom.

“I’ll be right back Billy.” She had called before crossing the room to the facilities.

She had been in one of the stalls when she heard the door open and then the lock click.

“I’ve been waiting to get you alone, Rio.” The voice sent a shiver down her spine. She froze. “You can’t hide in there forever, sweetie.”

She unlatched the stall and stepped out. Wanda was leaning back against the sink. “You really are beautiful, you know?

Rio didn’t know what to say to that, she just stayed silent and watched. She calculated the distance to the door but didn’t think she could make it in time.

“What has Agatha told you about me?” Wanda questioned.

Rio walked past her to the other sink and washed her hands. She watched the figure beside her out of the corner of her eye, “Not much. You head up the Sokovian gang. You’re married to Vision. You have expensive taste and a twin brother.”

“That’s it? Damn, I thought I was much more memorable than that.” Wanda huffed. “Do you know why we’re here tonight?”

Rio dried her hands and turned to face her interrogator, “Agatha asked you to send a message to my ex and things went poorly. She owes you.”

“Simply put, yes. But plenty of people owe me. I take a special interest in Agatha.”

“Why?”

“She’s the only worthy adversary I’ve ever met. There aren’t many women in positions of power in this city. It’s a bore. When Mother strolled in to ask for my help, I remembered what it was like to have fun again.”

“What’s that got to do with me?” Rio couldn’t see where this was going.

“Oh, you’re more akin to the worm on a fishing line.” Wanda reached down and lifted the hem of her dress. Rio’s eyes went wide. She watched her pull an impressive hunting knife from a hidden holster against her upper thigh.

Rio moved towards the door, trying to escape, but Wanda was faster. She threw her back against the door, trapping them both in the room. “Slow your roll, baby. We’re not done here.”

She was running her finger along the blade - playing with the shining metal like it was a toy.

“Please…I’m just - I’m nobody” Rio pleaded with the woman in front of her, but Wanda had a crazed look in her eye.

“No, no. You’re somebody to Agatha. I see how she looks at you, how she fawns over you. Why does she get to be happy and I don’t…” Wanda stumbled for a second and remembered herself. “Hmmm, now where would you like a scar? Along your thigh? Across your ribs? Where will Agatha see it every time you make love? I want a lasting reminder for her to enjoy.”

Rio swallowed and felt it catch in her throat. Her pulse was pounding so hard in her neck, it felt like it was closing in around her. Where is Agatha? She stared at the blade in Wanda’s hands and felt the panic overtaking her brain.

“You don’t have to do this.” She managed to stammer the plea.

“I know.” Wanda observed the other woman with a cold hard stare. “I want to do this.”

She approached with the knife in front of her and was reaching out to grab Rio’s arm when they heard it.

It sounded like a stampede coming down on top of them. A cacophony of yelling and commotion. Glasses smashing. The music stopping suddenly. Running bodies. Chairs hitting the floor.

Shouting.

Screaming.

And then the unmistakable sound of gunfire.

Blood and tears and bone

“Officer Sullivan! Grab a firearm, we’re heading uptown.”

Felix had been on the job for five months now with the NYPD. After getting home from the war, it had seemed like a logical fit. He liked the structure of the organization and the camaraderie of the team. He didn’t want to rot behind a desk for the rest of his life.

However, he hadn’t had to use his weapon and still had flashbacks from the trenches. His job so far had mostly consisted of walking the beat and learning how to file paperwork. His ears still  rang at night when he laid in bed and tried to sleep. His wife would try to soothe him with gentle caresses or by humming a tune, but the ringing never subsided. His dreams didn’t provide any relief either - the endless muck, the stench of rotting corpses, the never-ending shells raining from the sky.

“Sullivan! Come on!” His detective was yelling now, and he snapped out of it.

“Coming, sir.” He holstered his Colt revolver and threw his jacket and cap on.

The chief looked out of his office window at his men scrambling in the precinct. Fuck, fuck, fuck. “O’Rourke, get in here!” He called a passing officer into his office.

“Yes, chief?”

“What’s going on?”

“Didn’t you hear? That new Attorney General was just in - he’s calling on us to raid every speakeasy we can find tonight. They are setting a new quota - they expect 2,000 arrests a week!” The officer exclaimed.

“God damn it. Where are you guys heading now?” The chief was worried. He had made many promises to various gin joint owners around the city and taken his fair share of bribes. They were the reason he had been able to drive a brand-new Lincoln Model L to work each day and afford an apartment in Manhattan.

“Harlem area. AG Buckner said he got a tip off that a gang is hosting a big event tonight at one of the smaller clubs. Apparently it’s too big an opportunity to let slide, so we’re all going.”

“Thanks officer.” He dismissed the young man.

Oh no...Lilia. The chief had a soft spot for the old broad. She was one of the most generous of the club owners, but she also took the time to get to know him. She would send him beautifully written birthday cards and drop off the most delicious moonshine.

He scrambled to think of a way to warn her. He didn’t have a phone number. He didn’t know her home address and surely she wouldn’t be at the pharmacy at this hour. He couldn’t outrun his unit at this point. Damn it. He just had to hope that they went quietly, without a fight.

Felix rode in the back of the wagon with six other rookies. It was his first raid. He normally worked the day shift and had only switched this week to try to earn some overtime. His first child was on the way. He had flashbacks to the frontlines and closed his eyes to try to come back to the present.

“First time, Sullivan?” One of the others saw Felix’s leg bouncing and his shut eyes.

He nodded and tried to calm his nerves.

“Don’t worry. We do these almost every weekend. It’s really simple. We storm the place. People try to run. We grab as many as we can and arrest them. Take them to the station and throw them in a holding cell. The city makes a bunch of bail money, the politicians celebrate their empty win, we do it all again.”

The rookies laughed at the simple explanation. Felix relaxed a bit and gave them a strained smile. They all felt the car slow down and stop abruptly.

The doors opened and the team piled out. There were over 40 officers standing on the street, and the detective in charge cleared his throat. “Okay men, you know the drill by now. We normally aim for the staff since they are the ones technically breaking the law by selling the hard stuff, but tonight this whole place is infested with trouble boys. Grab whoever you can get, and we’ll be able to call it a win. Do not - I repeat, do not draw your weapon unless under fire. The last thing we want is a gunfight down there.”

Felix followed the group as they entered a dark alley. It looked abandoned, but the detective approached a nondescript door and pounded on it. It was quiet for a while. Felix wondered whether they had the right location at all. Finally, after what felt like ages, the small window slid open and shut just as fast.

“Open up, this is the NYPD!”

Silence.

“You have 10 seconds before we bust this door down!” The detective barked.

They watched in anticipation, then the door slowly creaked open. There was nobody on the other side. The sound of music came flowing out like smoke, wrapping them all in its allure.

“On me, let’s go.” The leader flung the door open the rest of the way, and the troop stormed the place, flying down the stairs in a sudden barrage. One of the officers kicked the main door down and the cops swarmed into the hall like ants.

“POLICE, freeze! Hands up!”

“Stop! You’re under arrest!”

The patrons were already scrambling when they entered the club. The doorman must have given them a heads up because people were running for their lives.

Felix felt overwhelmed. There were men and women flying in every direction - he couldn’t focus on anyone fast enough to catch them. People were dropping their drinks and broken glass was all over the hardwood floor. He felt like his shoes were glued to the ground. The band on stage had stopped and now the cavernous space was echoing with chaos.

He closed his eyes to try to get a handle on himself. He tried to imagine the beach - playing in the waves at Coney Island, relaxing in the sun. The calmness of the salt air, the heat coming off the yellow sand.

He opened his eyes in time to see a young man near the stage pull a gun from behind his back and aim it at the nearby officer arresting a young lady.

Felix didn’t say a word. He didn’t even consciously think anything. His hand flew to his revolver. All the months of basic training before he deployed came back to him in an instant, like it was part of his DNA.

He fired the shot.

And all hell broke loose.

Agatha saw the warning light near the door flash three times as she was still held hostage by Pietro.

“We need to go. We need to go right now!” She desperately looked at the man holding her.

“We’re not going anywhere, babe.”

“No! We’re being raided. We need to get everyone out!” Agatha tried to convey the urgency. They had just seconds before the cops showed up.

Pietro looked at her with concern. Then Alice flew through the door, “Run! The cops are here!” She shouted with all her might.

Everyone looked at each other for a moment, wondering if this was for real. But all of the staff immediately booked it. Herb and the security men ran for the nearest exit. Darcy bolted for the side entrance and was gone. Billy immediately went to grab Jen from the back room - he didn’t know if he could make it across to the bathroom to get Rio.

Agatha yanked and pulled to free herself, but Pietro still wasn’t convinced and refused to let her go. “We’re going to get arrested, you fool!” She yelled.

The fuzz sped down the stairs in the record time and immediately started yelling and going after anyone and everyone.

“Fuck, how do we get out of here?” Pietro pulled them to standing.

“Let me go and I’ll show you.” Agatha begged.

“Get on the ground! You’re under arrest!” They watched a cop slap some bracelets on a girl nearby.

“We don’t have time, let me go!” Agatha saw Pietro considering it as his fellow gang members started to succumb to the overwhelming police presence.

She looked over his shoulder and saw a young guy reaching into his pants waistband. “No!” She yelled out but it was too late.

The first shot exploded in the room, and she immediately covered her ears. Pietro had released her when the sound surprised them both. She watched the blood start to pour out of the gangster and was hypnotized by the slow moving river of red, until more shots started going off all around her.

Pietro fired at the cop who shot the boy and other remaining gang members started pulling hidden weapons and throwing lead. The police returned fire, and the place became a battlefield.

Agatha ran for the bar and grabbed the gun that Lilia had given her. It was heavier than she expected and the cool metal felt like ice in her palm. She watched Pietro retreat backstage and decided to follow. She wasn’t going to let him get away unscathed.

At the first shot, Wanda reached out and snagged Rio by the back of her head. She gripped the raven locks with a firm grip and whispered in her ear, “You’re going to get us out of here.”

Rio tried to think carefully. The main entrance was probably surrounded by cops - that’s a no go, despite being the closest and quickest escape. If they could cross the landing into the storage hall, there was a secret exit at the other end, but it was also obvious and the first place the cops would check. She ran through the exits in her mind. The best option was the one backstage in the first green room - it let you out almost a block away on the complete other side of the street.

“I know a way.” Rio muttered out. She could feel the tip of the knife at her back.

“Go.” Wanda pushed her out of the bathroom door. Rio looked around and didn’t see anyone.

She pushed the potted palm in the corner of the room out of the way and opened the hidden door. It led to a secret hallway along one wall of the club. It was tight, so she ducked and Wanda followed her closely into the dark space.

“How many exits are there in this place?” Wanda asked, genuinely curious.

“More than I can count. We’re nothing if not prepared.” Rio said. The hall was barely the width of a person. It was lit by thin cutouts in the brickwork that let light in from the main room. The two shuffled down quickly and could hear the commotion happening just a few feet away. It deposited them out backstage.

The performers were rushing to grab their things and make a run for it.

“Rio!”

She squinted to try to make out the figure calling her name. It was incredibly dark with the curtains drawn.

Billy ran up to her, completely unaware of the threat behind her. She tried to give him a look but it was so difficult to see anything. “Hey kid, you need to scram!”

“I warned Jen then came back here to find Sharon. I didn’t know if anyone tipped her off. She is normally holed up in the green room.” He was too good for this world.

The teen opened up the dressing room that Rio had been going to, and he finally took in the woman holding Rio by her hair. “What the…”

The room was empty, the false wall had been pushed open, likely by Sharon, and the exit hall was visible behind the racks of clothes. Wanda looked to the boy, “Who are you?”

The door banged open and Pietro jumped inside. His arm was bleeding and he was holding it delicately, breathing heavily.

“Pietro! What happened?” Wanda’s attention turned to her brother.

“Fucking Johnny. He saw one of the coppers grab his doll and lost his head. That fucking idiot pulled out his gun in a room full of police. He was clipped before he could even pull the trigger. Everyone started shooting then, I got hit in the crossfire.” He grimaced and held the wound on his bicep.

The door opened again and Agatha slipped in - she locked it behind her then took in the wild scene in front of her.

“Heard you guys were having a party.” She couldn’t help the sarcasm.

“Nice of you to join us, Mother.” Wanda spoke. “Pietro, grab the boy.”

Her twin pushed through the pain and held Billy in a headlock with one arm. He reached into his jacket and pulled his trusty pocket knife out. He held it at his side as a warning.

“Wanda, let them go. They don’t deserve this.” Agatha looked between Billy and Rio - they were both at the mercy of these sadistic twins. She remembered the gun in her hand and lifted it. She didn’t know where to aim.

“Pick one.” Wanda smiled as she tugged on Rio’s hair, forcing her neck to tilt back. “Who gets to live - your lover or your teenage sidekick?”

“Stop this Wanda. We can all take the run-out, the exit is literally right there. Hurry before the cops make it back here.” Agatha watched the redhead carefully. She also listened for movement on the stage, knowing it couldn’t be long before the coppers continued their raid of the place.

“ You don’t call the shots here! I’m in control! Nobody tells me what to do, not anymore.” Wanda yelled. Rio could feel her shaking behind her and worried about her erratic nature. One slip of the hand and that was that.

Billy started to cry. He tried to hold it in but the sobs escaped from him, and Agatha watched the tears running down his face. He was terrified.

“Billy, dear. Look at me. You’re going to be alright.” Agatha tried to get him to calm down. She saw Pietro struggling to hold his grip. She saw the blood dying his shirt sleeve and his face contorting in pain. “You’re going to see Tommy again. Just hold on.”

Wanda dropped her knife. It clattered against the floor and drew everyone’s attention. Rio took the opportunity to twist out of her clutches and break free. She ran to Agatha and fell into her arms. The gun also dropped to the ground as Agatha wrapped Rio into a tight hug.

Wanda was stark white, all the color had been drained from her face. She looked at Billy like he was both a celebrity and a phantom, like she was both star struck and absolutely terrified.

“How old are you?” She stammered the words slowly.

“Ummm, I’m almost 17.” Billy was looking at her with confusion. His eyes flicked between her and Agatha.

Wanda collapsed on the floor. Her head in her hands.

“You have to do this.” Vision said coldly as he placed one of the babies on the doorstep. “We can’t provide for them.”

“Vis, please. They’re our boys.” Wanda cradled the sleeping baby in her arms. They were only a week old, but it was abundantly clear that it wasn’t going to work. Wanda and Vision were living in an abandoned warehouse in the Bronx with a dozen other Sokovian refugees. There was hardly enough food for the adults, let alone any children.

There was no running water, no heating. They burned whatever garbage they could find in attempts to stay warm through the brutal city winter. They didn’t have enough money to send for Pietro yet - she was all alone. Her parents were gone, her husband was always out working - “building an empire” he said, and so she was left with endless time by herself.

The pregnancy had been a mistake. A night of passion gone too far, and then Wanda had begged to keep it. She had felt so lonely in this country since arriving, and this was the one thing she felt ownership over. The only thing that felt she could control. Vision had relented at first after seeing her excitement and had briefly considered the possibility, but reality came crashing down when it wasn’t just one baby that came out but two.

When the first little boy was placed on her chest Wanda whispered out, “Tommy” like she was finally releasing her deepest secret into the world. When the second was cleaned and handed to Vision, he looked into the innocent crying eyes and said, “Billy.”

Wanda had glanced up at him with a quizzical look at his name choice. He rocked gently and said, “After William Shakespeare - All the world’s a stage.”

She felt like she might burst - it was like her heart had been pulled from her chest and split in two. It was glorious pain, uncomparable joy and sorrow.

But that was nothing compared to the feeling of placing her sons on the doorstep of the orphanage. It was agony, it was a live death. Saying goodbye to the life she hoped could be hers. Offering up her heart on a platter.

“Darling, they are hungry. We can’t…we can’t feed them. I wish it wasn’t so.” Vision tried to reason with her but there was no reason that would make this okay.

“If we do this, I will hate you forever.” She spat the words out, knowing she didn’t really mean them. But not knowing any other way to convey this loss. She loved her husband, but it would be a lie to say she didn’t harbor an unending feeling of resentment for this decision.

“It will get better with time.” Vision hardened his heart and stepped back.

“I’m sorry. I’m so sorry, boys.” Wanda placed one last kiss on both of their heads and left a note with the baby names and birth dates in Billy’s carrier. She wiped the tears from her eyes but nothing would stop them from falling for weeks, for months, for years.

She would replay that moment endlessly in her nightmares. She would agonize over the lives that they were living without her - were they happy? Did they miss her?

“Wanda? Wanda, what’s wrong?” Pietro’s voice brought her back to the present.

“Let him go.” She spoke flatly but the strength of the words caused her twin to release his hold on the teen.

Billy rushed over to Agatha and hugged her with an outpouring of emotion like she was his shield, his sanctuary. The look on Wanda’s face was devastating.

The door splintered open at that moment as a gaggle of police kicked it down with their guns drawn. “Freeze! Grab some air!”

At that moment, everything seemed to happen in slow motion.

Agatha pushed Billy as hard as she could towards the escape hall. “Get Lilia!” She shouted - her voice rough and desperate. He booked it at full speed before any of the cops could register what happened.

An officer kicked Wanda from her kneeling position with more force than necessary and she hit the floor hard, causing Pietro to lunge for the gun that Agatha had dropped. Another cop saw the move and fired, hitting Pietro right in the chest. He took one final shuddering breath, and his eyes glazed over.

Wanda screamed with the full force of her lungs. She grabbed her hunting knife from the floor and threw it at the cop who had shot her brother. It spun in the air and connected with a sickening sound in its target.

It hit him in the guts and stuck, causing him to falter his next shot. Instead of drilling into Wanda, the bullet found a home in Rio.

She looked down at her thigh and couldn’t reconcile the dripping wound with her expectation for what should be there. The pain hadn’t even registered in her brain yet. It was like she was looking down at someone else’s limb.

“NO!! Rio!” Agatha’s voice shattered out of her mouth.

She watched in shock as Rio faltered on her feet.

She lunged to help lower her down and then ripped a skirt from the nearby clothes rack. She tied the fabric tightly around the thigh - it looked like the bullet had gone all the way through, there was blood coming out of both sides.

“Bunny, I need you to hold this tightly. Right there.” Agatha moved Rio’s hands to hold the fabric to her leg. “So good, just like that. You’re going to be fine, okay? You’re going to be just fine, sweetheart.” Her voice was trembling, her vision was blurring. There was so much blood.

The cops stared in shock before one spoke up, “Fuck Sullivan, what have you done?”

Another one sprung into action. “Let’s cuff these two. Thompson, call an ambulance! Fuck…nobody say a word. We were just defending ourselves. D’Angelo, help Sullivan with that knife. Let’s go!”

Wanda was mute, staring down at Pietro’s lifeless body. She didn’t resist arrest or make any acknowledgement that it was happening. She was escorted from the room without a sound.

Another officer grabbed Agatha and wrestled a pair of handcuffs on her. “Stop, she needs me! Let me go, you bastards!” Agatha was thrashing now, staring down at Rio.

Her lover was barely moving. The usual fire was gone. Her face was a beautiful statue - the shock freezing her features in look of disbelief. She was holding the makeshift tourniquet and looking at Agatha with fear in her eyes.

“Agatha…don’t leave. Please, my love.” Her voice was shaking, barely audible, a quiet plea.

“Rio!” She called out as the cop forced her to her feet and bumped her out of the room. She tried to twist and turn to get one last glimpse, but the cop was moving too fast. “Hold on, Rio!” She screamed and her voice broke.

“Shut up.” The cop muttered.

“Fuck off, filthy pig.” Agatha bit back, which earned her a swift jab at the back of her knees. She could only hope that Billy had made it out, that Lilia was coming, that someone had actually called an ambulance.

Rio, my precious Rio. Her body caved under the stress and adrenaline. Her mind shut down.

The last thing she remembered was being pushed out from behind the stage and seeing the bodies littered across the floor.

The road is wild and wicked

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Agatha had collapsed in the club and been carried out by two cops. She awoke in the back of the paddywagon - her hands were still cuffed behind her back, and she was leaning against the cold metal wall. There were seven others stuffed in there with her. She saw Wanda immediately but didn’t recognize any of the others, who must be part of the gang.

She then remembered Rio. Rio with a bullet wound. Rio bleeding on the floor. Rio scared and begging her to stay.

She felt the tears falling before she could muster the energy to stop them. She wanted to bawl and scream simultaneously but not here. It was overwhelming and crushing. How could she keep going? How could she live in a world without this woman who had her in a chokehold?

The car stopped, and she heard the front doors slam. The back door flung open and a cop unceremoniously pulled the catch-of-the-day out one by one. She was shuffled into the station and dumped in a holding cell with Wanda and the two other women that had been picked up, while the men were taken elsewhere. They removed the bracelets from her wrists and slammed the metal gate.

“Hey! Hey! I need my phone call. Please.” She grabbed the bars and called out to nobody. There were at least 30 other gals in the cell, and from what she could hear across the hall, the men’s cell was overflowing. This was going to be a long night.

Agatha’s adrenaline was settling and the exhaustion was threatening to knock her out. She dropped onto the concrete bench next to Wanda.

“Nothing to say, red?” She looked at the woman beside her. Wanda was blank-faced, staring at the ground in a trance. She didn’t make a move that she heard or knew who was speaking. Agatha didn’t care enough to push it.

Hours dragged by. This place was woefully understaffed. The sun was already starting to rise by the time the processing team booked her. She considered a fake name, but unfortunately several of the officers had already clocked who she was. One of the downfalls of cultivating a reputation in this town.

“Harkness, one phone call.”

“Jesus, finally.” She sighed and pushed herself up. She dialed Lilia’s phone number and tapped her foot waiting. It rang and rang…nothing. Fuckkkk.

She swallowed hard and grabbed the bridge of her nose. Deep breath, it’s fine. Maybe she’s just…out or helping someone else or.. . She rotated the dial and entered Jen’s number.

A few seconds passed. “Hello?” Jen’s voice came through the earpiece - the relief like a cold rain on a steaming hot day.

“Jen! What’s happening?? Is Rio okay? Did everyone make it out alright?” She rambled the words out in a torrent.

“Whoa, whoa. Where are you?”

“I’m at the police station - they pinched me. Have you seen Rio?”

“No, I got out as soon as Billy warned me, and I ran home. I haven’t been back yet. I don’t know what happened.”

Damn it. “I’m glad you made it. Can you check in with the rest of the crew? I don’t think I’m getting out of here today.”

“Of course. I’ll tell them you’ve been locked up. Stay safe in there.” Jen knew Agatha could handle herself in any situation, but jail was a whole different beast.

“Thanks, Jen.” She hung up and the worry within her was only growing. Where was Rio? Lilia? Billy?

Agatha went back to the cell dejected. She watched the other young women from the club slowly empty out as their loved ones showed up with the $25 bail money and a range of disapproving looks on their faces.

“Hey, what’s my bail?” She jumped up to the door when the officer came to let out another low life.

“Harkness, ha! You wish. The big boss isn’t setting bail for you or your pretty friend over there. The pressure from the top brass is too great.” The young man smirked.

“What the fuck? You can’t do that! I want a lawyer!” She shook the gate angrily to the sound of his laughter. “Where’s my lawyer?!”

“Rio, honey. Are you there?”

The soft resonant sound entered her mind. It was like stepping through the thickest fog. She felt hazy and disoriented. She blinked slowly and winced at the lights.

“Where am I…what’s going on?” Her voice sounded foreign like it belonged to a stranger.

“Sweets, you’re in the hospital.” Lilia rubbed Rio’s hand gently and leaned against the hospital bed.

“What happened? Where’s Agatha?” She looked around, her neck felt stiff. There was nobody else in the small white room.

“You got shot by a fucking trigger-happy cop.” Lilia broke the news. “Alice is on another floor. She got trampled in the mad panic when she came down to warn everyone. She fell and landed on a mess of broken glass. They were able to stabilize her. Do you remember…”

Rio looked down and threw the warm blanket back. There was a stiff bandage wrapped around her thigh. She tried to lift it and bit her tongue to hold back the shout. She held her breath and collapsed backwards on the pillows.

She tried to push her mind back in time.

The biting burn in her leg like someone had slammed an ice pick into her thigh. It was so sudden and unexpected that her brain couldn’t even process the sensation. One second she was watching the life leave Pietro’s eyes and the next she was staring at the spread of red down her stockings.

The expression on Agatha’s face as if the world was crashing down around them. The flurried panic and painful exasperation. Her name being shouted again and again.

The rush of blue uniforms lifting and carrying her love away. Someone telling her that help was on the way.

Being trapped in the room with that silver-haired corpse. The smell of blood overwhelming her nostrils. Her consciousness drifted in and out as she tried to stay awake.

Billy appearing out of nowhere with Lilia in tow. Being lifted and carried like a child.

Hearing someone whisper, “You’re going to make it. Hold on for Agatha. She needs you.”

She opened her eyes again and looked at Lilia, “Is Agatha alright?”

The older woman looked at her with love in her eyes, “I haven’t heard from her. She was hauled out and taken. I was going to go down to the station but wanted to make sure you didn’t wake up alone.”

“She could have escaped. She saved Billy…why didn’t she run?” Rio stared down at her hands.

“Do you really have to ask?” Lilia had a look on her face. “You were hurt. You were in pain. They would have had to drag her out screaming to get her away from you.”

Rio felt warmth climbing her neck and cheeks. “When you see her…can you tell her thank you?”

“Of course. I’ll head over now. Are you okay here?”

“Yeah, I’ll be fine. Go, she is probably worrying herself sick.” Rio squeezed Lilia’s hand and gave her a small wave goodbye as she left.

A nurse came into the room with a tray of food for breakfast. “How are you feeling, dearie?” She was a short woman with a pleasant heart-shaped face. She adjusted the pillows so Rio was sitting up.

Rio attacked the scrambled eggs with the fork. She felt famished, “I feel groggy but mostly okay. Trying to move my left leg was a mistake.”

The nurse nodded, “It may feel like that for a while unfortunately. The doctor cleaned and sewed up the wound, but it will take time for the muscles to heal. You’re very fortunate that the bullet passed through. I treated many men overseas who weren’t as lucky. I’ll grab some morphine, which should help you rest.”

“Thanks, ma’am.” Rio continued eating her meal while the nurse ducked out. She rolled a metal cart back in with her.

“I’ve just got to give you an anti-tetanus shot - standard practice these days.”

“Go ahead.” Rio presented her arm and took the injection- the pain barely more than a pinch.

“Here’s your pain medicine, rest up.” Rio finished her meal then took the tablets. She thought of Agatha to calm her racing thoughts - her piercing blue eyes, the timbre of her voice, the feel of her smooth fingers running through her hair, the scent of her skin. It wasn’t long before she surrendered to the drug-induced sleep.

Lilia hurriedly walked to the neighborhood police station where they typically held the folks rounded up in raids.

She was running on less than two hours sleep since it had been near midnight when Billy showed up at her door.

He had arrived huffing and puffing, saying the club had been raided and Agatha needed her. She threw on the nearest dress, grabbed a coat, and sped over to the speakeasy - grateful for the close proximity.

Billy pulled her to the secret entrance behind the apartment building on the opposing corner. When she saw Rio lying there on the green room floor, her heart stopped. She looked so pale, and there was so much blood. She glanced at Pietro, already well and truly gone and knelt down to close his unseeing eyes. She saw her gun laying slack in his open hand and pocketed it.

“Take her down to Sydenham Hospital. Can you carry her?” She looked at the young man, who was nervously shifting on his feet, trying to avoid looking at the dead body.

“Yes, I can do it.” He lifted Rio with surprising ease. She whimpered at the change in position but held on tightly to Billy, who rushed out the exit.

“Be careful! I’ll be there as soon as I can.”

Lilia eased out of the room to assess the damage. Backstage was empty, there were costumes, instruments, and trash littering the area as people had obviously scrambled to get out of there.

She stepped from behind the curtain and saw several physicians and nurses attending to fallen or injured police officers and any gang members still living. The place was a disaster zone - tables thrown to act as barriers, glasses smashed all over the floor, bodies slumped in awkward positions in booths or across the ground.

She walked down the steps and tried to avoid eye contact with the lost souls in her pathway. Mostly young men from the gang from the looks of things. Such a sad ending to a short life.

Officers were carried off in stretchers, groaning and clutching their injuries, and the eerie silence that remained was suffocating.

She hurriedly cashed out the till and collected the tips before any wiseguys got the bright idea to rob them. She checked the storage hall and back room - empty. She locked the doors to protect whatever liquor was left. She sat on one of the barstools that was still standing and poured a shot of vodka.

The liquid was a welcome intrusion and would hopefully soften the edges of this nightmare. She knew it had been a mistake to dance with the devil, but she hadn’t expected it would ever end this tragically.

When she finally arrived at the prison, she spoke to the officer at the desk, “I’m here to see Agatha Harkness.”

The man looked through the notebook in front of him, “She can’t have any visitors.”

“Excuse me? Why not?”

“Ummm…it just says here - she is not to see anyone.” The officer couldn’t be older than 20. He was out of his depth.

“Where’s the chief?” Lilia didn’t have time to faff around.

“You can’t…just…ummm…the chief isn’t…” He was tripping over his words and starting to sweat under the filthy glare coming from this woman.

“Tell him Lilia is here to see him.” The boy didn’t move. “That will be all.”

He nervously rose and scurried to the back. He came back trailing behind Chief Jones, looking sheepish.

“Lilia, this way.” He gestured for her to follow. They entered his meticulously organized office.

“Chief, do you want to explain what the hell happened last night? I thought we had an agreement.” She took a seat and crossed her legs.

He took a stack of bills out of his drawer and passed them over his mahogany desk. “Here, take it back. I’m sorry. I only found out as they were gearing up to leave. The new attorney general is on the warpath, I couldn’t call it off. It wasn’t supposed to go down like that.”

Lilia stashed the cash in her purse, “Two of my staff are in the hospital, Agatha is behind bars, and the club is a graveyard of gang members and cops. Who knows when we’ll be able to re-open?”

“I’m really sorry, Lilia. I promise that wasn’t the intention. What can I do? How can I help?”

“For starters, you could let me speak to Agatha. I’ll be in contact when I think of anything else.” She stood without prompting.

“I can give you five minutes before people start asking questions.” He grabbed his keyring from a hook on the wall.

“That’s enough.”

He led them to an interrogation room and sat her down. A minute passed and Agatha was placed across from her. Lilia could see the immediate look of relief on her face. The chief closed the door behind him.

Agatha sprung up and hugged Lilia tightly. “Is Rio alive?” Her voice was quaking with fear.

“Yes, my dear. She’s okay.” Agatha crumbled in Lilia’s arms. Her body shook with all the sobs that she had accumulated and held at bay for hours. They were reaping their vengeance now.

“Shhhh. It’s alright. She just woke up in the hospital. The doctor treated her leg and said she will have to stay for a week to monitor for infection. She seems okay - she was asking for you.” Lilia ran her fingers in circles on Agatha’s back, trying to soothe the crippling waves of sadness.

It took a moment for Agatha to get her breathing under control, “They said I can’t pay bail. I’m stuck here.” Her lungs gasped for air as the realization overtook her.

“Let me see what I can do.”

“How is everyone else? I know Jen made it - I’m assuming Billy fetched you like I asked?”

“Yup, the boy did good. He’s just fine. I saw Alice in the hospital. It was touch and go for a second there. She had cuts all across her arms and a large piece of glass lodged near her ribs. The doctor said it was a miracle it didn’t hit her lungs. She’s going to be down for the count for a while though. Billy said Darcy made it home, and that he saw Herb and Sharon as he was running to my place.”

“What are we going to do now? How do we move forward?” The thought had been nagging Agatha, and she only had time to think while sitting in the cold jail cell.

“Let’s just take it one step at a time. Let me try to get you out of this joint first.”

Agatha nodded then suddenly remembered, “Can you check in on my place and feed Ebony? I don’t know when I’m getting out of here.”

“No problem, I still have your spare key. I’ll take care of everything.”

They heard a knock on the door and an officer forced Agatha out. The chief came to sit where she had just been.

“How long are you going to hold her?” Lilia looked to the man for answers.

“My hands are tied. Her name is too well known, they want to make an example of her. Maximoff is the same. These two are too infamous to let slide.”

“Come on, there are thousands upon thousands of speakeasies in this godforsaken town. We’re peanuts compared to the big dogs out there. I’ll pay - whatever it takes. Slap her with a fine, we can cover it.”

“I wish it were so simple. That might help, but she’s going to do time. She has to. I’ll see if I can get them down to a few weeks rather than months or a year. Would she agree to take a plea bargain?” The chief removed his hat and ran his fingers through his short white hair.

“What’s the charge?”

“Conspiracy to violate the National Prohibition Act and operating an illegal business.”

“Oh eat my ass, chief! That carries a $10,000 fine! It could be 5 years in prison, are you kidding?” Lilia raised her voice.

“No, they wouldn’t let a woman go away for that long. The pollies are just looking for a win. I think I could negotiate three weeks and maybe a thousand bucks. She may have to do some community service but that’s it. It’s the best I can offer.”

“Fool me once…” Lilia gave him a look that would strike fear into anyone.

He extended his hand across the table, and she shook it with hesitation, “You’re good people, Lil. I’ll talk to the judge and the prosecutor. I may be an old man, but my name still carries some weight around these parts.”

The chief was a man of his word this time. Agatha pled guilty and was sentenced to just three weeks on Welfare Island and a fine of $500. It was hardly a slap on the wrist, and she was beyond grateful, considering the alternative.

Wanda was less lucky. She went to trial and even with the gang money funding her high-powered lawyer, it wasn’t enough to save her from a sneaky tax evasion and racketeering charge that carried a 2 year sentence.

They travelled together on the boat to the women’s prison, which was located on the thin strip of land in the middle of the East River. It was formerly known as Blackwell’s Penitentiary but recently renamed to Welfare Island to try to kick the poor reputation. The castle-like building was four stories and had over 800 cells, yet somehow, as a cruel twist of fate, they ended up in cells next to each other.

Agatha changed into the drab grey dress uniform. Ugh these stockings are going to itch like hell . She tried to adjust the horrific cheap fabric but it was a losing battle. It was a far cry from the normal silk ones she normally bought. She could also already feel the blisters forming at the back of her heels from the stiff excuses for shoes they doled out. The flats were already worn down and clearly molded to the shape of some other poor sod’s feet.

She got acquainted with her new living space - she could touch both side walls with her arms outstretched. There was a plank bed attached to the wall, with a shelf above it and a single bible. One foldable chair in the corner and a tiny window for light and ventilation. It was beyond bleak. She missed her apartment, her stuff, her life.

Wanda had yet to say a word to Agatha or anyone for that matter. She was a husk of her former self. She saw her in the dining hall, during the morning and nightly checks by the guards, and out on the yard for work, but the redhead ignored her completely. The soul behind her eyes was gone. Agatha would feel sorry for her if she didn’t resent the mobster for this entire debacle.

It was their third night in the Big House. She had gotten used to the wails and non-stop noise that echoed through the concrete halls. They were on the ground floor and could hear the constant commotion above them. Agatha was laying on her bunk when she heard the familiar sound of her next door neighbor, “What is he like?”

She wasn’t sure at first if she imagined it or if it was really addressed to her. The voices were generally hard to distinguish, but this was a voice she knew. “Sorry?”

“Billy - what’s he like?” Wanda was sitting in her cell, leaning against the wall that they shared.

Agatha sat up and moved near the bars. She contemplated not saying anything, but it was obvious that this question had been eating at her neighbor. She decided to rise above the games, “He is hilarious. He’s got more energy than he knows what to do with. He is incredibly hard-working - I usually have to beg him to take a day off. He loves movies and takes Tommy to the cinema every weekend. They are best friends. He is sarcastic and can give as much as he gets. He’s so so kind.”

She could hear the soft cries and whimpering sniffles but kept going, “Billy is…resilient. He never lets a challenge get him down, and he’s been through a lot already. He wants to go to New York University and saves everything he earns. He can read people and get an immediate sense of them, almost like he can infiltrate their mind. He is nosy and loves gossip but never uses it for personal gain. He looks more beautiful in a dress than most women I know. He sets his mind to things and never gives up.”

Wanda was a leaky tap now. The tears were a salve on her soul. Hearing about this boy, no - her Billy, was like a bandage on her broken heart.

“He can annoy the living hell out of me sometimes, but I love him. I love the kid. I’m so grateful to know him. He brings endless enjoyment to my life.” Agatha wiped the tears from her eyes at the confession. She had never vocalized her appreciation for the teen but saying it now was as healing for her as it seemed to be for the broken woman on the other side of the wall.

“Thank you. Thanks, Agatha. I see why they call you Mother now. You really do have a maternal side.” Wanda held her knees against her chest and felt the tears running down her legs.

Agatha let the compliment wash over her. It wasn’t the origin of her name, but it felt nice regardless.  “I’m sure he would like to meet you properly, Wanda. He doesn’t know that you’re his...I mean, he doesn’t know who you are.”

“I don’t want him to be embarrassed or ashamed of me. His father and I aren’t exactly the best role models. And now I’m going to spend the next two years in prison - not really Mother of the Year material.” She sounded weary and drained.

“He’s not like that. He’s the least judgemental kid I’ve ever met. He can see the good in everyone. You don’t have to decide now, but I can tell him if you want. He can come visit you.”

There was a long pause. Agatha wasn’t sure if Wanda was icing her out again. “I’ll think about it.” She finally spoke. “Goodnight Agatha. Thank you.”

Chapter End Notes

Thank you for reading and sticking with me through the cliffhanger!

I hate to lock Agatha away, but it won't be for long.

Our love was forged in fire

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Dear Agatha,

I think about you every day. It’s beyond boring in the hospital - there is absolutely nothing to do. I’ve started making up songs in my head because there is nothing else to keep my mind occupied. All I can hear is your voice calling my name as the cops hauled you away. It echoes in my mind - it’s so quiet here.

I miss you desperately. I wish you were here now. I’m never bored when you’re around. I hope prison isn’t as bad as they say. I told the nurse that you were at Welfare Island and she looked scared. They say it’s awful and that the treatment is horrific - is that true? I can’t stand it if it is.

I have to stay at the hospital for just a few more days. My leg is healing well, but I can still barely stand. What if I can’t dance again? What if I never walk properly? They have given me crutches, and I’ve been practicing but it hurts my arms. I don’t know how I’m going to get around. I wish you were here to help.

Lilia said you were getting out in two weeks. I’ll try to be there at the gates when you are finally a free woman again. I will be thinking of nothing else except having you in my arms again.

I have a lot to say in person that I don’t want to put in a letter. Think of me, mi reina.

Love,

Rio

Dearest Rio,

You have robbed me of my mystery. I am yours eternally now. I cannot imagine any universe, any life, any existence where I am not tied to you inextricably.

I won’t sugar coat it - prison is as awful as they say. I am counting down the minutes until I am free from these shackles and in your arms again. It is miserable living here. I am starving for regular food, for some devil’s candy, for your touch.

Wanda is here with me. She is in the cell next to mine. She has been cordial and asks me about Billy. If you haven’t already guessed, she is his birth mother. I’m going to break the news to him when I’m out, please don’t say anything unless he’s already deduced it.

I can’t wait to see you. I will carry you anywhere you need to go if you still can’t walk properly. I’ll happily get on my hands and knees for you.

No, not like that…unless you also want that…either can be arranged. This time here has made me appreciate every aspect of my life tenfold. I wanted to wait to say this to your face, but I am compelled to write it out now - I love you. I am so overwhelmingly in love with you.

Yours eternally,

Agatha

Rio held onto the letter with both hands. She read and re-read Agatha’s declaration like it was the only sentence in existence. I love you. I love you. She loves me. It was the truth laid bare, and she couldn’t be happier. She regretted holding it back in her letter now.

She was on the couch in Lilia’s apartment, laying back with her bad leg up on the cushions, trying to keep it raised. She got discharged from the hospital yesterday morning and was told to return in a week to get the bandages changed and have a doctor examine the wound.

Lilia helped her hobble home on her wooden crutches and cooked her spaghetti and meatballs to fill her up. It made her think of Agatha - her heart ached.

“How’s the club looking?” She asked Lilia in between bites. The crew had been spending their nights cleaning up the joint after the disastrous event last week.

“Better than it did that’s for sure. We’re going to have to replace most of the furniture in the dance hall. I don’t know how they managed to smash every chair that we owned but there ya go. The flooring is gonna need to go too, the blood just won’t come out. Luckily we put aside money for repairs and maintenance.” Lilia explained.

“Won’t the cops just show up again?” The thought made a shiver run down Rio’s spine.

“Usually once they hit up a place, they leave it alone for a while. Since Agatha took the fall, I think they’ll cool their heels for some time.”

“Is Alice out yet?” She hadn’t been able to visit her when they were in the hospital together. The staff preferred the patients stay separate to avoid spreading any unnecessary illness.

“Not quite yet. She has to stay another week or two - her injury is very sensitive and they said it is at high risk of re-opening. It needs more time to heal.”

“Can I come with you today?” Rio missed everyone and wanted to help however possible.

“Are you sure? Didn’t the doctors say you should be resting?” Lilia raised an eyebrow.

“Please, Lilia. I’m losing it cooped up in here. I won’t overdo it, I just want to see the crew.”

“If you hurt yourself more…” She warned.

“I won’t, I promise!”

“Agatha will have my head if you do.” Lilia said and then, “We’re leaving in half an hour.”

Rio beamed and slowly walked to her bedroom to put on some decent clothes to leave the house. She was able to get around on her crutches alright, but it was definitely slow going. She was starting to be able to put some weight on her leg, but it still felt incredibly weak.

“Ready?” Lilia peeked in and Rio nodded.

They walked the short distance to the club. Lilia was as patient as ever with Rio’s pace. She had been a godsend since Rio had gotten out of the hospital - helping her get in and out of the bath, cooking her delicious meals, changing her bandages, getting her prescriptions. Rio couldn’t be more grateful.

The stairs down into the basement proved a tricky challenge. Lilia held onto Rio’s crutches and offered her other arm as they carefully stepped their way down to the club.

“Rio!!”

Billy rushed over and threw his arms around her, almost knocking them both to the ground.

“Whoa! Careful kid, I’m not as steady as I used to be.” She held onto him for balance.

“Sorry, sorry, sorry. I didn’t think you would be here today! How are you? You look great. How’s your leg? When will you be back at work? I miss you!” All of his thoughts spilled out.

Rio laughed. He hadn’t changed one bit, “I’m okay. I probably won’t be back for a few more weeks yet. It’s still too painful to stand for long periods, but the doctor said it will keep getting better every day.”

“Wow, I’ve never met anyone who has been shot before. What was it like?”

Jen approached them, “Morbid much? I doubt she wants to discuss that, teen!” She hugged Rio tightly, “Glad to see you on your feet.”

“Hey Jen, it’s so good to see you too.”

“What’s up, rookie?” Darcy called up from behind the bar, she was stacking the new glassware. Rio waved back with a smile.

“This place doesn’t look half bad, ya know? You’ve made a lot of progress.” Rio looked around the club. The team had cleared out all the wreckage, so it was mostly just an empty room now but at least it was clean.

“We’re pulling the booths out today. Most of them are riddled with bullet holes or stained with blood so…” Billy shrugged with a hammer in one hand and a crowbar in the other.

“You can count up the remaining supply of booze, Rio.” Lilia suggested, knowing that task could be completed without much physical labor.

“Okay, happy to help wherever.”

She walked to the storage hall to take inventory. Luckily there was already a clipboard on one of the stacks of boxes. She counted each crate and noted the liquor type and amount on the sheet. After about 30 minutes or so, Billy appeared in the dim hall with her.

“Everything alright?” He asked.

“Yeah, all good. How are you?” She could sense he wanted to ask her something but wanted to give him the space to start. He leaned against the brick wall, and there was a long pause. She had never seen him be silent for so long.

He took a deep intake of air, “Why did Wanda let me go? They could have…you know…it could have been me. Is she my…my mother?”

Rio hesitated for a moment. She knew that Agatha wanted to be the one to break this news, but the look on Billy’s face was too deep to ignore. “Yeah, I think so. But that doesn’t change anything about you.”

“She’s…not a good person.” He spoke slowly. “But, she let me go?”

“People are complicated. It’s not always like the movies where there is a hero and a villian. I don’t think she knew who you were until Agatha said Tommy’s name.”

“Why did she abandon us?” Billy spoke but the voice that came out sounded like his five-year-old self.

“I can’t answer that, kid. I’m sure it wasn’t an easy decision though.”

The Hidden Gate reopened its doors on the first Friday of July. It had taken over a month to restock their alcohol supply, acquire new furniture, tear up and put down new flooring, and make the place presentable again.

It would have taken most places double the time, but once again Lilia’s endless connections came in handy. On top of that, the whole swath of regulars at the club decided to pool their modest incomes and donate a hefty sum to the renovations. They wanted their place back as soon as possible. As much as the team missed it, the customers missed it more.

Lilia was able to get a team of contractors to do the entire floor in one weekend. They matched the look of the old design, but the fresh varnish made it really sparkle. The new booths dazzled with a unique fabric choice - a deep, mysterious ripe plum. Agatha had searched high and low to find it and scoured every back alley in the city to source enough for the club.

Wall decor was replaced, bullet holes were either filled in or covered with art, broken lamps were restored, and eventually the place looked better than it ever had. This was the longest closure in its history.

On opening night, Darcy took up the post at the door as Alice was still out of commission. She had been discharged from the hospital but was advised not to put herself in any dangerous situations. Of course, nobody expected anything bad to happen, but you could never be 100% sure in this line of work. All the other staff members returned, excited to be back together again.
