Others simply stared, dumbstruck by her close proximity, and some openly ogled her - wishing they were the object of her affection. But Mother could only be swayed by one person.

“Excuse me, miss. I think the dance floor needs to be broken in by a certain skilled dancer. I heard there was one working here.” Agatha swaggered around the bar and held her arm out for Rio to take.

Rio couldn’t hide the blush that appeared on her cheeks. Nothing could compare to the feeling of Agatha’s light shining on you. She took the outstretched arm and decided to leave her cane behind the bar.

As they walked towards the stage, the crowd parted a pathway for the duo, as if this was all planned in advance.

“Did you put them up to this?” Rio whispered out of the side of her mouth.

“Innocent old me? Well I never!” Agatha jested and winked. She always had something up her sleeve to surprise Rio with.

The people cleared a space on the dance floor as the drummer counted in a mid tempo jazz song.

Agatha could sense a tinge of anxiety in her partner, which was unexpected. If there was anywhere on Earth that Rio felt the most confident, it would be the dance floor. “I’ve got you.” She mouthed as the music was growing in volume.

Rio nodded, “I know.” She said back and took Agatha’s hands.

“This one is for our fearless leader and for the greatest dancer this joint has ever seen. Let’s hear it for Agatha and Rio!” The band leader called out loudly from the stage.

Rio felt like she could die of embarrassment, but the way Agatha was beaming at her made her set her shoulders back and stand tall. The crowd was clapping in time and rallying around them. The energy was potent and drowned out any fear she had about dancing on her weak leg.

She looked into Agatha’s eyes, and everything faded away. They nodded with the beat and then their bodies moved as if compelled by an outside force. Agatha took the lead and Rio, for once, was completely happy to let her. They hardly needed to communicate at all. It was like they were in each other’s heads.

As Agatha would move to lift her arm, Rio was already getting ready to spin out. As Rio pulled left for a twirl, Agatha was right in step with her. It wasn’t a push and pull - it was a glorious partnership, a perfect harmony between two unlikely sources.

The onlookers shouted encouragement as they marvelled at the brilliant show, and when the song finished, the applause was deafening. Rio looked around at all the smiling faces and felt an unbelievable high.

“I see why you crave attention now.” She murmured to her dance partner, who let out a loud cackle.

“Oh no, have I created a monster?” Agatha covered her mouth in roguish shock.

“Nah, I don’t think I could handle this all the time.” Rio started walking back to the bar. “Plus I doubt you could handle the competition.”

“Don’t go there, daddy-o! You wish you could compete with me.” Agatha called out to Rio’s retreating figure.

The night continued without any shocks or surprises. It was a night of rejoicing, of reunions, of celebration. It went until the dawn broke over the city and exhaustion threatened to take everyone down. Nobody wanted to go, but Agatha promised everyone they would be open again tomorrow. Eventually the masses took their final swigs and heaved their bodies up the stairs to the real world.

Rio was hiding the last bottle of gin in the wall alcove when she felt a pair of arms wrap around her waist.

“Ready to make like the wind and blow out of here?” Agatha asked in her ear.

“Ready when you are, sweetheart.” Rio replied.

The couple said their goodbyes and went home together. The walk to their shared apartment was one of Rio’s favorite parts of their routine. It was a quiet reprieve after a night of constant noise and music and demands. They didn’t often converse or debrief. It was enough to enjoy each other’s company in the simple act of walking together.

They made the short walk night after night. Throughout the entire summer, the club was packed to the brim. The police raid hadn’t left a black mark on the place; it somehow seemed to only increase its allure. People came from every borough and even from other cities and other states. One night Rio served a group of women who had travelled all the way from Paris and even a fella from across the ocean in Australia.

As the summer nights got shorter and the cool breeze off the Hudson snaked through the air, a thought that had been itching at the back of Rio’s head finally set itself in motion.

“Any plans tomorrow?” She asked Agatha one Sunday afternoon as they lounged on the couch.

“Nothing on the calendar.” She narrowed her eyes suspiciously, “Why?”

“I want to take you somewhere.”

“Where?”

“Patience is a virtue.” Rio jabbed.

“I never did care much for virtues.” She said over the newspaper she was reading. “Well at least tell me what I should wear.”

“Don’t pretend you don’t look good in everything.”

“I can’t help that! But is this a formal occasion? Should I wear sporting wear? Will I need a fur coat? Should I don gloves? A girl needs to know these things in advance.” Agatha rambled on.

“Wear something casual and a warm coat. Shoes you can walk around in. Happy?” Rio relented.

“Very.” Agatha moved over and kissed Rio on the cheek. “I look forward to whatever you have planned, my love.”

The next morning, they took the subway down the entire length of Manhattan to Battery Park. They rose to the surface on a clear and sunny day and walked down to the edge of the water.

In the distance, Lady Liberty could be seen standing sentinel over the horizon.

“You know I’ve never been to see her up close. I’ve lived here for so long and never made the trip.” Agatha confessed.

“Well, well, well. Today’s your lucky day.” Rio smiled.

“Really?” Of all the things Agatha could have guessed they were doing today that hadn’t even crossed her mind.

“I already bought the ferry tickets. Let’s go!” She led them to the dock and boarded the boat with the other hordes of tourists for the short ride over to Bedloe’s Island.

When they disembarked on the island, they walked with the crowd to the front of the imposing statue.

“Wow.” Rio said aloud. It was one thing to see it from across the river but standing under her towering form was something else entirely.

“I remember when she was all bronze.” Agatha noted as they both stared up. “I think the green suits her better. It’s a great color.” She looked to Rio knowing it was her favorite. The statue had only recently shifted color in the past few years as the copper naturally weathered over time.

“She’s beautiful.” Rio felt tears springing to her eyes. She was taken back to her original boat ride from Puerto Rico. She had watched the city skyline as they approached and then remembered how her eyes fell on the Statue of Liberty. She had heard people talk about it and seen photos, but seeing it in that moment was indescribable.

She had been on the precipice of such a dramatic life change - full of fear and worry and excitement. The statue seemed to convey a welcome as if it spoke directly to her, like a calming reminder that she wasn’t alone.

Rio felt movement beside her and looked down to see Agatha extend a handkerchief in front of her. She took it and dabbed her eyes. They sat along the short brick wall under the statue’s persistent gaze, and Rio placed her cane at their feet.

“I always wanted to see this place up close. It’s such an iconic landmark and holds such a significant place in my memory of this country. It’s a reminder of the past, but I also see it as a symbol of my future. A future I want to share with you.

I have never loved anyone as much as I love you, Agatha. I finally understood what liberty felt like when we first kissed. There was no expectation and no role that I was trying to play. I feel completely free when we’re together like my voice matters, like I have a say. I’m never scared, never walking on eggshells, and never worried about your intentions.

And you are a shining light through all my doubts. You love me so completely that I never question it. I didn’t know it was possible to feel like this, yet here we are.” Rio saw the tears falling down Agatha’s face now and passed back the hankie with a soft smile. She gripped her hand tightly.

“I never thought I would find freedom in another person, but I’ve found it in you. I want to spend my life with you.” Rio reached into her coat pocket and pulled out a small velvet box. Agatha let out a gasp of true surprise.

She had been saving all her earnings and tips for the last few months and was able to amass a decent sum, thanks largely to the fact that she no longer paid rent since moving in with Agatha. She didn’t want for anything, so when she walked by the family-owned jewellery shop near the grocery store one weekend, she went in on a whim. The kind shop owner showed her the latest styles but it was an older ring that caught her eye.

Rio opened the box and revealed a silver band with intricate flowing filigree with a small square cut, deep blue sapphire gemstone in the middle.

Agatha reached out and took the ring out herself, never one to wait for anyone. The smile on her face stretched from ear to ear. She eagerly placed the ring on her hand.

“So…that’s a yes?” Rio had watched the whole sequence with joy.

Agatha couldn’t take her eyes off her hand but glanced up to see the earnest brown eyes staring at her, “Yes!” She almost tackled Rio in a bear hug, knocking her back to her elbows on the grass behind them.

She pulled back and let her own declaration burst out, “I love you desperately, obsessively, passionately, overwhelmingly. You’ve changed me, Rio. I considered asking the prison warden if I could see a shrink because I thought something must be wrong with my head. I missed you so much I thought I was going crazy. I thought there was no way that I could be so singularly fixated on a person, but I am.

I used to be so tough and alluringly unavailable, and now I melt at your touch and crumble at your every request. You’ve cast your charm. It’s over - I’m done - You’re it for me.”

“You’re sure? Last chance to back out.” Rio joked.

“Very funny. Just like Lady Liberty, I’ve been carrying a torch for you for ages now. I don’t see any other future without you by my side. What about you? Are you sure?”

“I know it won’t be easy, but after everything we’ve been through so far, I can’t imagine doing it with anyone else.” Rio leaned in and placed a chaste kiss on the side of Agatha’s mouth. It could be read as innocent by any bystander, but they could both feel the promise and the heat behind it.

“You’re stuck with me now. You know that right?” Agatha questioned with a tease in her tone. They stood and wandered over to the edge of the island beside the river.

“Maybe it’s you who’s stuck with me.” Rio chuckled then stared off, deep in thought. “I wish we could get married.”

“We’ll do something special. We could host a big party at the club and invite everyone we know. We could say vows to each other in the middle of the forest up in the Catskills. We could scream our love from the top of the Woolworth Building. It may not be legal, but it will be real to us. That’s enough.”

They leaned against the railing, hand in hand, and marveled across the water at the gorgeous skyline of their city.

“Where did you come from?” Agatha broke the silence.

“Umm…Puerto Rico?” Rio looked at her with confusion.

“Yes I’m aware. I meant how did you end up in my life? In this city full of so many countless people, how did we find each other?”

Rio looked out at the city again and could see the tiny specks bustling along in their own individual lives. “I don’t know. Maybe it’s just the natural order of all things. I don’t necessarily believe in a God or anything, but I do believe in fate and the unspoken magic all around us. I can’t believe it was simply chance that brought me to you.

“I almost don’t care. I’m just grateful to have you. Whatever happens from here, wherever we go, I plan to enjoy every second that we get together.” Agatha released her intention out into the world and held onto Rio’s hand tightly.

They had come so far in such a short time, but she couldn’t wait to see what happened next.

Chapter End Notes

Epilogue should be up either tomorrow or the day after. I can't believe it's almost over. This started as a small idea that blew up into an entire world. I've had a great time teasing it out into this story.

Thank you as always for reading!

Epilogue - glory at the end

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

On December 5th, 1933, the hammer fell and Prohibition faded into the night, the 13 year "noble experiment" came to an unceremonious and welcome end.

It’s estimated that the federal government lost a total of $11 billion in tax revenue and spent over $300 million trying to enforce this ill-conceived law. On average, over 1000 Americans died every year of Prohibition from the effects of drinking tainted, unregulated liquor. The homicide rate during the 20’s is said to have increased by 78% over the previous period, in addition to increases in robberies, assaults, and related crimes.

Thousands upon thousands lost their jobs as every trade related to alcohol was eliminated, in addition to the knock on effects on all hospitality and entertainment industries. Public trust in law enforcement hit an all time low due to the rampant corruption, bribes, and the rise in organized crime.

The road to hell was paved with good intentions.

While many suffered during this period, others prospered. Notorious gangster, Al Capone estimated that his bootlegging criminal organization, The Outfit, made as much as $100 million a year during Prohibition. He ran about 6,000 speakeasies in Chicago, which are said to have made more than $6 million a week.

Agatha had a similar story to tell (though much less extravagant). The Hidden Gate was able to rake in several million dollars in its tenure as an illegal speakeasy. She was a keen saver and pocketed a pretty penny from her efforts and shared the love with her staff. They were all able to ride out the stock market crash and ensuing Depression while the rest of the country descended into poverty.

They kept the doors open through it all - becoming a legal establishment as soon as they were able to apply for the permits. The “peculiar” folks of the city needed somewhere to meet, somewhere to let their hair down, so even though most restaurants and bars were struggling to find clients, Agatha’s place was as popular as ever. She was able to keep prices low due to the booming years prior and that kept the seats and the dance floor full.

Rio remained by her side. The pair were a fixture of the area, and a pillar of the community. Everyone who was anyone knew them, the inseparable duo that ran the best bar in the city. Some knew them as “roommates” while most knew they were as good as married. Outside of work, they donated generously to the local orphanages, and they volunteered their time at the local soup kitchen, which had lines around the block during the Great Depression. They held season tickets at the new Yankee Stadium and were frequent patrons of the Great White Way.

In 1935, they decided to finally move out of Agatha's apartment and bought a brownstone on Manhattan Avenue to make their home. It was bittersweet to say goodbye to the third floor of that beautiful building where they first shared a space together.

They had made so many memories in that one-bedroom apartment. It was where they had shared a bed for the first time. Where they had taken care of Ebony before she passed of old age. Where they had hosted weekly Sunday night dinners with their friends.

But the new townhouse was more than worth it. There was a massive kitchen where Rio could cook up her favorite dishes, a spacious parlor where Agatha could spin around her lover for a late night dance, a rooftop landing where they could share a kiss under the stars.

“Will you ever tire of kissing me?” Rio asked one day as they lounged on the roof.

“I don’t think that day will ever arrive. Something will have gone terribly wrong if I ever get tired of this.” Agatha declared and planted another smacker on her lover.

“Would you give up a kingdom to marry me?” They had just recently listened to the shocking radio address from Edward VIII, who was the first English monarch to abdicate the throne. He gave it all up to marry an American divorcée.

“I would surrender all titles, relinquish all my money, disown my name, and sully my reputation a thousand times if it meant I could legally marry you.” Agatha proclaimed in a fairly convincing English accent.

“And I would do the same for you. Do you think it could happen someday?”

“Giving up my royal birthright?” Agatha joked.

“No, smartmouth. Do you think we’re any closer to getting married in the eye’s of Uncle Sam?” Rio held Agatha’s hand and asked the question without jest. It didn’t often bother her anymore, but sometimes it rose to the surface again.

Agatha stared up at the moon, “I can’t see a world where it happens. Are you…unhappy with our life?”

“Not at all. I love everything we have together. There are just things I wish we could have that everyone else gets. I wish I could kiss you on the street or call you my wife. I wish I didn’t have to hide the most important part of my life sometimes.” Rio loved Agatha completely, but her frustration at the injustice of the world was occasionally hard to come to terms with.

“Close your eyes.” Agatha whispered and looked over as Rio listened. “Imagine we live a hundred years in the future. Can you see it? They’ve just passed a new law - it’s now legal for us to get married. We jump in our flying car and zoom to the courthouse. A robot performs our ceremony as we exchange rings. Beep Boop, I declare you wife and…wife. You may now kiss the bride.” Agatha surprised Rio with a sloppy peck on the lips. They giggled like schoolchildren.

“Golly, we gotta wait a hundred years? I’m not a very patient person.” Rio whined.

“I know, my love. One day things will change. I have to believe that. We may not be around to see it, but I hope the things we do in our life will be the stepping stones that lead to real progress. It may take decades, but the road towards acceptance is wild and wicked. We can only keep marching forward.”

Rio took over management of the pharmacy when Lilia finally decided to hang up her coat and retire. She kept things running smoothly and made a pointed effort to hire new immigrants whenever possible. She would occasionally jump on the soda fountain to pour some drinks, just for old times sake.

Lilia was a wealthy woman by the time she stopped working at the shop, but she still liked to stay busy. She spent every weekend at the theatre and shared her thoughts on the performances and performers with anyone who would listen. Somehow this led her to a side gig as a critic for Gotham Life magazine. Her cutting reviews could make or break the latest shows, as the city’s art-lovers looked to her well-trained ear and cunning wordplay to decide where to spend their hard-earned wages.

Billy graduated from NYU with honors and a degree in business. He took over the accounting and financial management for both the pharmacy and bar and helped settle the books to paint a plausible story for its sustained success throughout the 20s. He handled all that, in addition to his full-time career working in film distribution at The Astoria Studio in Queens. The timing couldn’t have been more perfect. As the talkies exploded on the movie scene, Billy was there to usher them into the mainstream and ride the Golden Age of Hollywood straight to the bank.

He and Tommy saw Wanda a few times a year. She left Vision and the gang after serving her time. The past was too haunting and that part of her life died with her brother. She took the money she made in her divorce and paid for Billy’s entire education - he was able to keep his savings and go on a dream trip to Hollywood with his twin. Wanda moved out to New Jersey to start fresh and reset. She hung up her knives and lived a quiet life, punctuated by joyous visits from her sons.

Jen’s moonshine was acquired by Jean-Paul’s Northstar Distillery and sold under their brand name. She was able to negotiate a 10% profit sharing agreement and almost fainted when the first cheque arrived in the mail. Her product was found on shelves across North America, and they were even able to export it overseas to Europe, where it found a surprising cult following in France. She settled down with a Canadian gal who caught her eye on one of her trips to Montreal and decided to move up North permanently.

Alice recovered from her injuries and determined that security was really not worth the risk. It had been exciting at first, but her brush with death had recalibrated her priorities. She decided to pursue her long-forgotten dream of music and dove back into the piano. She became only the second woman to join the New York Philharmonic, just two years after the pioneer harpist Stephanie Goldner.

In 1965, the month of Agatha’s 85th birthday, the couple was contacted by The Ladder magazine for an interview. It was the first and only nationally distributed lesbian publication in the country. They were looking for couples who had been together for decades to inspire hope in a community that was struggling to find much of it otherwise.

The 40’s and 50’s had been a perilous time in the country with the government actively persecuting anyone outside the expected heterosexual norm. Where the 20’s had been a time of sexual freedom and exploration, the pendulum swung hard and fast in the opposite direction. Laws were passed to criminalize “that way of life” and homosexuals were tied to communists and targeted in what came to be known as the “Lavender Scare.”

Thousands lost their jobs, were arrested, were attacked. Millions simply hid in fear, but always, in the background, others reached out and found each other. Brave souls sought community and built safe havens and protected each other.

Rio helped Agatha ease into her favorite lilac shirtwaist dress with matching short gloves. She was as spry as ever thanks to decades pounding the pavement in New York, but Rio liked helping her get dressed. She passed over a pair of pearl earrings, which Agatha affixed to her ears and admired in the mirror.

“Here you go, my love.” Then helped pin a special flower brooch to her lapel. She brushed the long white locks that cascaded down Agatha’s back. It took effort to maintain but Rio had to admit that the long hair really worked. Then again, at this point she could say every hairstyle looked good on Agatha.

Rio donned her black cigarette pants and a classic red check button-down shirt blouse. She loved how fashion had evolved over time to allow more variety in her options. She had also gone through all types of hairstyles through the years, but now in the later era of her life, she was back to a classic bob. She didn’t care much for accessories except for one important ring she never took off her left hand, a gold band with a pear-shaped emerald that Agatha had gifted her on their 1 year anniversary.

“Ready?” She asked Agatha, who smiled up at her from her seat at her dressing table. Rio helped her stand and they linked arms.

The two walked downstairs gently when they heard the doorbell ring and greeted the interviewer. They all took up spots in the front sitting room. Agatha brought out a pitcher of iced tea and a tray of Rio’s homemade quesitos, a childhood favorite similar to a cheese danish.

The interviewer opened her notebook and clicked her pen. Rio threw her arm around Agatha’s shoulder and leaned in. She felt a familiar hand on her thigh, gently massaging around a very old scar - a long-practiced habit.

“So how did you two meet?” The young interviewer asked with interest, looking between the two elders.

“Do you want to tell her, bunny?” Rio shook her head with a bashful smile and Agatha smirked, always the ham no matter her age, she loved retelling the tale.

“The year was 1922…”

Chapter End Notes

That's all folks!

This was the first story I've ever finished and posted. I never thought anyone else would care to read an AU set during this time period or care to read my writing at all, but I'm very grateful for all of you that did. If you've made it to the end, I want to thank you for your support. This story became what it did due to the great commentators who left their thoughts and hopes and fears.

I'm already planning my next work. If you have any requests for other time periods that you would like to see or just any thoughts on this now completed story, please let me know!
